First Sect: Souls Perceive Particulars
Razi explains the first sect's view that rational souls perceive particulars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first sect's argument that rational souls perceive particulars and how this leads to the soul's perfection after death.

Core Idea
The soul's perception of particulars is proven by the very structure of our judgments.

This lesson introduces the first sect among those who affirm the soul's survival. They argue not only that the soul perceives universals, but also particulars, using a logical analysis of a simple proposition. Razi then explains how this perception and action reach perfection after death, approaching the angels and attaining the greatest bliss.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation. Let the author's argument flow before you interpret.
Notice the logical structure: claim, proof, conclusion, then after death consequences.
2
Analyze the propositional argument
Focus on the judgment 'this person is human'. Identify the subject (particular) and predicate (universal). Understand how this proves the soul perceives particulars.
Assent (tasdiq) requires conception (tasawwur) of both subject and predicate.
3
Consider the after death implications
Reflect on what happens after death: the bodily veil is removed, perception and action increase to perfection, and the soul approaches the rank of angels. This is the greatest bliss.
Think about why the veil prevents full perception now.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطائفة الأولى : الذين يقولون : النفوس الناطقة مدركة للجزئيات. واحتجوا عليه بأنه يمكننا أن نحكم بأن هذا الشخص هو إنسان فهذه قضية موضوعها شخص معين - وهو جزئي - ومحمولها هو الإنسان - وهو كلي - والتصديق مسبوق بالتصور، فصاحب هذا التصديق عنده إدراك المحمول الذي هو الكلي، وإدراك الموضوع الذي هو الشخص لكن مدرك هذا الكلي هو النفس، فمدرك هذا الجزء أيضًا هو النفس، فثبت أن النفس مدركة للجزئيات؟ إذا ثبت هذا فنقول : النفس لها صفتان الإدراك والفعل، والإدراك قسمان : إدراك الجزئيات وإدراك الكليات فالنفس هي الموصوفة بهذين القسمين من الإدراك، وبهذا الفعل الذي هو التحريك ، فإذا مات البدن وزال الحجاب الجسماني تجلت عليها أنوار عالم الجلال، فازداد إدراكها وفعلها وانتهت في ذلك إلى حد الكمال، وقربت درجتها من درجة الملائكة - الذين هم أرواح عالم السماوات - وذلك هو الغبطة الكبرى، والدرجة العظمى.
The first sect: those who say that rational souls perceive particulars. They argued for it by the fact that we can judge that this person is a human. So this is a proposition whose subject is a specific person—which is a particular—and whose predicate is 'human'—which is a universal. Assent is preceded by conception. So the one who makes this assent has a perception of the predicate, which is the universal, and a perception of the subject, which is the person. But the perceiver of this universal is the soul, so the perceiver of this particular is also the soul. Thus it is established that the soul perceives particulars. If this is established, we say: the soul has two attributes: perception and action. Perception is of two kinds: perception of particulars and perception of universals. So the soul is qualified by these two kinds of perception, and by this action which is motion. When the body dies and the bodily veil is removed, the lights of the world of majesty are revealed to it, so its perception and action increase, and it reaches the limit of perfection in that, and its rank approaches the rank of angels—who are the spirits of the celestial worlds—and that is the greatest bliss and the supreme station.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage presents the first sub-sect of those who believe all rational souls survive death. They argue that the soul perceives particulars, using the example of judging 'this person is human'. In this judgment, the subject is a particular individual, and the predicate is a universal. Since the soul perceives the universal, and the judgment requires perception of both, the soul must also perceive the particular. Therefore, the soul perceives particulars and universals. After death, when the body's veil is removed, the soul's perception and action become perfect, approaching the rank of angels, which is the ultimate bliss.

Key Terms
النفس الناطقة
إدراك الجزئيات
إدراك الكليات
الغبطة الكبرى
الحجاب الجسماني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The soul only perceives universals, not particulars.
Correction: The first sect's argument shows that because we can judge particulars with universals, the soul must perceive both.

Checkpoint
How does the first sect prove that the soul perceives particulars?
A) By arguing that the soul moves the body
B) By analyzing the judgment 'this person is human'
C) By citing revelation about angels
D) By referring to dreams

Key Takeaway
The soul's perception includes both particulars and universals, and its perfection after death is the greatest bliss.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the judgment 'this person is human.' According to Razi's argument, your soul is perceiving both a particular and a universal in that moment. How does this awareness change the way you see your own mental acts? Are you conscious of your soul's activity in everyday judgments?
?
The passage says that after death, when the bodily veil is removed, the soul's perception and action increase until it reaches perfection. What veil in your own life—attachment to the body, desires, distractions—is blocking your soul's perception of the divine lights right now? What would it mean for you to begin removing that veil today?
?
The greatest bliss is when the soul's rank approaches that of angels. Do you truly desire that? Or are you content with a life of sensory pleasures? What would you be willing to sacrifice to increase your soul's perception and action now?

Souls Need Celestial Instruments After Death
Razi states the second sect's view on post-mortem perception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second sect's view that human souls require bodily instruments to perceive particulars and, after death, attach to parts of the heavens to continue perceiving.

Core Idea
The soul needs a physical instrument to perceive particulars, even after death.

Imam al-Razi now presents a second view on how the human soul perceives after death. This view maintains that the soul always needs a bodily instrument for particular perceptions. Even after the death of the physical body, the soul can attach itself to a celestial body, which then serves as its instrument. Let's examine this position as Razi outlines it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice the key claim about the soul's dependency on instruments.
The passage is a single sentence, so pay attention to its logical flow.
2
Identify the core claim
The passage states that human souls cannot perceive particulars except through bodily instruments. Underline this condition.
3
Understand the post-death solution
After death, the bodily instruments are impaired. The passage offers a solution: the soul attaches to a part of the heavens, which becomes a new instrument. Ask yourself how this differs from reincarnation.
This is not reincarnation into another human body.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this view was proposed. It attempts to preserve the soul's ability to perceive after death without denying its need for instruments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والطائفة الثانية : الذين قالوا بأن هذه الأرواح البشرية لا تقوى على إدراك الجزئيات إلا بواسطة آلات جسمانية، فإذا مات البدن واختلت هذه الآلات الجسمانية لم يبعد تعلق هذه النفوس بجزء من أجزاء السماوات حتى يكون ذلك الجزء آلة للنفس بها تقوى على الإدراكات الجزئية من الإبصار والسماع والتخيل والتفكر.
And the second sect: those who said that these human souls are not able to perceive particulars except through bodily instruments. So when the body dies and these bodily instruments become impaired, it is not unlikely that these souls attach themselves to a part of the parts of the heavens, so that that part becomes an instrument for the soul by which it is able to have particular perceptions of sight, hearing, imagination, and thought.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage presents the second sub-sect's view. They hold that the human soul cannot perceive particulars without bodily instruments (like the brain and senses). After the death of the body, these instruments are corrupted. However, the soul can attach itself to a part of the heavens (a celestial body) which then serves as a new instrument. Through this, the soul can continue to perceive particulars such as sight, hearing, imagination, and thinking. This view attempts to explain post-mortem perception without reincarnation.

Key Terms
الآلات الجسمانية
تعلق النفس
أجزاء السماوات
الإدراكات الجزئية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think this view teaches reincarnation of the soul into another human body.
Correction: The passage explicitly says the soul attaches to a part of the heavens, not to another human body. It is a new instrument, not a new life.

Checkpoint
According to the second sect, what enables the soul to perceive particulars after death?
A) Direct intuition without any instrument
B) Attachment to a part of the heavens
C) Reincarnation in another human body
D) Divine illumination without means

Key Takeaway
The second sect holds that the soul always needs an instrument to perceive particulars, and after death it uses a celestial part as its instrument.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This sect says your soul will never cease to require an instrument. What instrument are you relying on right now to perceive the truth of this lesson—your intellect, your faith, or your ego? Which one will fail you when your body dies?
?
If your soul could attach to a celestial part to continue seeing and hearing, what would you most want to witness in the afterlife? Does that desire reflect what you truly value now?
?
The passage insists that even after death, the soul remains dependent on a physical medium. Does that make you feel more connected to the physical world or more cautious about how you use your bodily instruments today? What will you change?

The Reincarnationist View: Three Sub-Groups
Razi enumerates three reincarnationist sub-groups.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reincarnationist (tanasukh) doctrine and its three sub-groups as described by Imam al-Razi.

Core Idea
Reincarnationists believe souls transfer between bodies based on moral state, with three distinct levels of transfer.

Imam al-Razi now turns to the third sect within the discussion of the soul's fate after death: those who believe in reincarnation (tanasukh). Unlike resurrectionists, they deny the return of the soul to its original body. Razi outlines their core belief and then distinguishes three sub-groups with varying degrees of physical transfer, from human-only to mineral bodies.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the English translation. Notice how Razi first states the general principle of reincarnation before listing the three groups.
2
Identify the three sub-groups
Find the three distinct positions Razi attributes to the reincarnationists. What is the scope of body transfer allowed by each?
The third group is presented as the most severe punishment.
3
Reflect on the rationale
Consider why the third group's view leads to the worst punishment, according to the explanation about the 'narrow depths' in Hell and the dimming of powers.
The text cuts off here, but the idea is that fewer powers mean darker bodies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطائفة الثالثة : الذين يقولون : النفس إذا انقطع تعلقها عن بدن معين تعلقت ببدن آخر، فإن كانت في البدن الأول من النفوس الزكية الفاضلة تعلقت ببدن كريم فاضل، وإن كانت في البدن الأول من النفوس الجاهلة المؤذية تعلقت ببدن مناسب لها، وهؤلاء هم القائلون بالتناسخ، وهم فرق : إحداها : الذين يقولون : الأرواح الإنسانية لا تتعلق إلا بالأبدان الإنسانية، ثم إنها لا تزال تنتقل من بدن إلى بدن إلى أن تكمل النفس وتصير طاهرة عن جميع العلائق الجسمانية، وحينئذ تتخلص إلى عالم القدس والطهارة. وثانيها : الذين يجوزون انتقال الأرواح الإنسانية إلى أبدان البهائم، ويقال لهم أهل المسخ . وثالثها : الذين قالوا : الأرواح البشرية إذا فارقت أبدانها فقد تتعلق بأبدان الحيوانات، وبأبدان النباتات والمعادن والبسائط قالوا وهذا هو غاية العذاب، وإليه الإشارة بالدركات الضيقة في جهنم. قالوا : وذلك لأن القوى الناطقة والحساسة والفعالة والغاذية كلها أنوار تفيض من عالم الأرواح، فتغوص في بواطن الأجسام، وبواطن الأجسام مظلمة جدا، إلا أنها مستنيرة بسبب غوص هذه القوى فيها وكلما كانت هذه القوى أقل كانت بواطن
The third sect: those who say: when the soul's attachment to a particular body is cut off, it attaches to another body. If it was in the first body among the pure virtuous souls, it attaches to a noble virtuous body; if it was in the first body among the ignorant harmful souls, it attaches to a body suitable for it. These are the proponents of reincarnation (tanasukh). They are groups: One of them: those who say: human souls attach only to human bodies; then they keep transferring from body to body until the soul becomes complete and becomes pure from all bodily attachments, and then it is released to the world of holiness and purity. The second: those who permit the transfer of human souls to animal bodies; they are called the people of metamorphosis (ahl al-maskh). The third: those who said: human souls, when they leave their bodies, may attach to animal bodies, and to plant bodies, minerals, and simple substances. They said: this is the utmost punishment, and it is referred to by the narrow depths in Hell. They said: that is because the rational, sensory, active, and nutritive powers are all lights flowing from the world of spirits; they sink into the interiors of bodies, and the interiors of bodies are very dark, but they are illuminated by the sinking of these powers into them. The fewer these powers are, the [darker] the interiors...
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage presents the third sub-sect: the reincarnationists (tanasukh). They believe that after death, the soul attaches to another body appropriate to its moral state: virtuous souls to noble bodies, ignorant souls to suitable bodies. Three sub-groups are distinguished: (1) Those who hold that souls transfer only among human bodies until purification, then ascend to the holy world. (2) Those who allow transfer to animal bodies (metamorphosis). (3) Those who allow transfer to animals, plants, minerals, and simple substances—considered the severest punishment, referenced in the Quran as 'narrow depths' in Hell. They explain this by saying that the various powers (rational, sensory, active, nutritive) are lights from the spirit world that sink into bodies, illuminating them; fewer powers result in darker bodies. The text cuts off mid-explanation.

Key Terms
التناسخ
المسخ

النفوس الزكية
النفوس الجاهلة
القوى الناطقة
القوى الحساسة
القوى الفعالة
القوى الغاذية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Reincarnation is the same as resurrection.
Correction: Reincarnation denies bodily resurrection and holds that souls transfer to other bodies, not return to the original.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the reincarnationist sub-groups mentioned?
A) Souls transfer only among human bodies
B) Souls transfer to animal bodies
C) Souls transfer to plants and minerals
D) Souls become angels directly after death

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Razi presents three reincarnationist sub-groups, ranging from human-only transfer to transfer into plants and minerals, with the latter considered the severest punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your actions determined the form you would take in your next life, would you live differently today? What specific changes would you make in your thoughts or deeds, knowing that every moment shapes your spiritual state?
?
The first sub-group believes that the soul must become 'pure from all bodily attachments' to ascend to the holy world. What attachments are you holding onto that keep you from spiritual purity, and what would it cost you to let them go?
?
The third group equates punishment with sinking into lower forms of existence – animals, plants, minerals. In what ways are you allowing yourself to be spiritually 'diminished' by neglecting your rational and spiritual faculties? What is one concrete step you can take tomorrow to reverse that decline?

The Soul's Direct Perception of Particulars
Razi presents the first group's view on spiritual resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that the soul directly perceives both universals and particulars, and how after death this perception reaches perfection.

Core Idea
The soul perceives directly; death removes the bodily veil, unleashing perfection.

In this passage, Imam al-Razi first establishes that the soul is the perceiver of both universals and particulars. He then presents the first group's view that after death, freed from the bodily veil, the soul attains perfect perception and action, approaching the rank of angels. This sets the stage for discussing spiritual resurrection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage establishing the soul's perception
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Notice how Razi argues that the soul perceives both universals and particulars by linking the perception of particulars to the soul.
The argument builds on the earlier discussion of the soul's attributes.
2
Identify the soul's two attributes
The passage states that the soul has two attributes: perception and action. Perception is further divided into two kinds: perception of particulars and perception of universals.
3
Understand what happens after death
When the body dies and the bodily veil is removed, the lights of the world of majesty become manifest to the soul, increasing its perception and action to perfection.
This is the state of spiritual resurrection for the first group.
4
Reflect on the rank of angels
Razi compares the perfected soul to angels, who are spirits of the celestial world. This is described as the greatest bliss and highest degree.
This emphasizes the positive outcome of direct perception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإدراك الموضوع الذي هو الشخص لكن مدرك هذا الكلي هو النفس، فمدركك هذا الجزء أيضًا هو النفس، فثبت أن النفس مدركة للجزئيات؟ إذا ثبت هذا فنقول : النفس لها صفتان الإدراك والفعل، والإدراك قسمان : إدراك الجزئيات وإدراك الكليات فالنفس هي الموصوفة بهذين القسمين من الإدراك، وبهذا الفعل الذي هو التحريك ، فإذا مات البدن وزال الحجاب الجسماني تجلت عليها أنوار عالم الجلال، فازداد إدراكها وفعلها وانتهت في ذلك إلى حد الكمال، وقربت درجتها من درجة الملائكة - الذين هم أرواح عالم السماوات - وذلك هو الغبطة الكبرى، والدرجة العظمى.
والطائفة الثانية : الذين قالوا بأن هذه الأرواح البشرية لا تقوى على إدراك الجزئيات إلا بواسطة آلات جسمانية، فإذا مات البدن واختلت هذه الآلات الجسمانية لم يبعد تعلق هذه النفوس بجزء من أجزاء السماوات حتى يكون ذلك الجزء آلة للنفس بها تقوى على الإدراكات الجزئية من الإبصار والسماع والتخيل والتفكر.
الطائفة الثالثة : الذين يقولون : النفس إذا انقطع تعلقها عن بدن معين تعلقت ببدن آخر، فإن كانت في البدن الأول من النفوس الزكية الفاضلة تعلقت ببدن كريم فاضل، وإن كانت في البدن الأول من النفوس الجاهلة المؤذية تعلقت ببدن مناسب لها، وهؤلاء هم القائلون بالتناسخ، وهم فرق :
إحداها : الذين يقولون : الأرواح الإنسانية لا تتعلق إلا بالأبدان الإنسانية، ثم إنها لا تزال تنتقل من بدن إلى بدن إلى أن تكمل النفس وتصير طاهرة عن جميع العلائق الجسمانية، وحينئذ تتخلص إلى عالم القدس والطهارة. وثانيها : الذين يجوزون انتقال الأرواح الإنسانية إلى أبدان البهائم، ويقال لهم أهل المسخ .
وثالثها : الذين قالوا : الأرواح البشرية إذا فارقت أبدانها فقد تتعلق بأبدان الحيوانات، وبأبدان النباتات والمعادن والبسائط قالوا وهذا هو غاية العذاب، وإليه الإشارة بالدركات الضيقة في جهنم.
قالوا : وذلك لأن القوى الناطقة والحساسة والفعالة والغاذية كلها أنوار تفيض من عالم الأرواح، فتغوص في بواطن الأجسام، وبواطن الأجسام مظلمة جدا، إلا أنها مستنيرة بسبب غوص هذه القوى فيها وكلما كانت هذه القوى أقل كانت بواطن الأجسام أشد ظلمة وأعظم ضيقًا فالأرواح البشرية إذا انتقلت من أبدانها إلى هذه الأجسام بقيت في غاية الظلمات والضيق والشدة، أما أجسام الأفلاك فإنها لكثرة القوى الروحانية التي فيها كانت في غاية الضوء والفسحة، فالأرواح البشرية إذا فارقت أبدانها وانتقلت إلى التعلق بعالم الأفلاك كانت في غاية الغبطة والفرح والضوء والسرور والروح والراحة والريحان.
فهذا هو الإشارة إلى تفصيل مذاهب القائلين بالمعاد الروحاني.
The perception of the subject which is the individual, but the perceiver of this universal is the soul, so your perceiver of this particular is also the soul, so it is established that the soul perceives particulars? If this is established, we say: The soul has two attributes: perception and action. Perception is of two kinds: perception of particulars and perception of universals. So the soul is described by these two kinds of perception, and by this action which is movement. When the body dies and the bodily veil is removed, the lights of the world of majesty become manifest to it, so its perception and action increase and reach the limit of perfection, and its rank approaches the rank of angels—who are the spirits of the celestial world—and that is the greatest bliss and the highest degree. The second group: those who say that these human spirits cannot perceive particulars except through bodily instruments. When the body dies and these bodily instruments are disrupted, it is not improbable that these souls become attached to a part of the heavens so that that part becomes an instrument for the soul by which it can perceive particulars such as sight, hearing, imagination, and thought. The third group: those who say: When the soul's attachment to a particular body is cut off, it attaches to another body. If in the first body it was among pure virtuous souls, it attaches to a noble virtuous body; if in the first body it was among ignorant harmful souls, it attaches to a body suitable for it. These are the proponents of transmigration (tanāsukh), and they are sects: One of them: those who say that human spirits attach only to human bodies, then they keep transferring from body to body until the soul becomes complete and pure from all bodily attachments, and then it is released to the world of holiness and purity. The second: those who permit the transfer of human spirits to animal bodies, and they are called the people of metamorphosis (maskh). The third: those who say that human spirits, when they depart their bodies, may attach to animal bodies, plant bodies, minerals, and simple bodies. They said this is the extreme torment, and it is indicated by the narrow depths in Hell. They said: That is because the rational, sensitive, active, and nutritive powers are all lights flowing from the world of spirits, descending into the interiors of bodies. The interiors of bodies are extremely dark, except they become illuminated by the descent of these powers into them. The less these powers are, the darker and narrower the interiors of bodies become. So human spirits, when they transfer from their bodies to these bodies, remain in extreme darkness, narrowness, and severity. As for the celestial bodies, due to the abundance of spiritual powers in them, they are in extreme light and spaciousness. So human spirits, when they depart their bodies and transfer to attachment to the celestial world, are in extreme bliss, joy, light, delight, spirit, comfort, and fragrance. This is the indication of the details of the doctrines of those who affirm spiritual resurrection.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage classifies the various views on spiritual resurrection (al-maʿād al-rūḥānī). It begins by establishing that the soul perceives particulars directly, then presents three groups: (1) Those who hold that the soul perceives particulars directly without instruments, and after death, freed from the bodily veil, it attains perfection and bliss akin to angels. (2) Those who hold that souls need bodily instruments; after death, they attach to a part of the heavens as an instrument for perception. (3) Those who hold transmigration (tanāsukh), which is subdivided into three sects: (a) souls transfer only among human bodies until purification, (b) souls transfer to animal bodies (maskh), and (c) souls transfer to animals, plants, minerals, etc., resulting in extreme torment due to darkness and narrowness. The passage explains that the degree of light or darkness depends on the spiritual powers present in the bodies. This serves as a detailed exposition of the doctrines of spiritual resurrection alone.

نفس
إدراك
جزئيات
كليات

Checkpoint

The Need for Bodily Instruments After Death
Razi presents the second group's view on spiritual resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second group's view that human spirits require bodily instruments even after death to perceive particulars.

Core Idea
Souls need instruments; after death they attach to celestial parts for perception.

Imam al-Razi now presents a second group of thinkers who hold that human spirits cannot perceive particulars without bodily instruments. When the body dies and its instruments are disrupted, these souls attach to a part of the heavens, which becomes a new instrument for perception. This view contrasts with the first group's direct perception.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the second group
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note the key claim: souls need bodily instruments to perceive particulars.
2
Understand the problem of death
When the body dies, the bodily instruments are disrupted. The second group argues that the soul then attaches to a part of the heavens.
This part of the heavens serves as an instrument for perception.
3
Identify the types of perception enabled
The passage lists sight, hearing, imagination, and thought as examples of perception enabled by this celestial instrument.
These are specific kinds of perception of particulars.
4
Contrast with the first group
Unlike the first group, the second group believes that the soul cannot perceive directly without an instrument, even after death.
This is a key difference between the two views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإدراك الموضوع الذي هو الشخص لكن مدرك هذا الكلي هو النفس، فمدركك هذا الجزء أيضًا هو النفس، فثبت أن النفس مدركة للجزئيات؟ إذا ثبت هذا فنقول : النفس لها صفتان الإدراك والفعل، والإدراك قسمان : إدراك الجزئيات وإدراك الكليات فالنفس هي الموصوفة بهذين القسمين من الإدراك، وبهذا الفعل الذي هو التحريك ، فإذا مات البدن وزال الحجاب الجسماني تجلت عليها أنوار عالم الجلال، فازداد إدراكها وفعلها وانتهت في ذلك إلى حد الكمال، وقربت درجتها من درجة الملائكة - الذين هم أرواح عالم السماوات - وذلك هو الغبطة الكبرى، والدرجة العظمى.
والطائفة الثانية : الذين قالوا بأن هذه الأرواح البشرية لا تقوى على إدراك الجزئيات إلا بواسطة آلات جسمانية، فإذا مات البدن واختلت هذه الآلات الجسمانية لم يبعد تعلق هذه النفوس بجزء من أجزاء السماوات حتى يكون ذلك الجزء آلة للنفس بها تقوى على الإدراكات الجزئية من الإبصار والسماع والتخيل والتفكر.
الطائفة الثالثة : الذين يقولون : النفس إذا انقطع تعلقها عن بدن معين تعلقت ببدن آخر، فإن كانت في البدن الأول من النفوس الزكية الفاضلة تعلقت ببدن كريم فاضل، وإن كانت في البدن الأول من النفوس الجاهلة المؤذية تعلقت ببدن مناسب لها، وهؤلاء هم القائلون بالتناسخ، وهم فرق :
إحداها : الذين يقولون : الأرواح الإنسانية لا تتعلق إلا بالأبدان الإنسانية، ثم إنها لا تزال تنتقل من بدن إلى بدن إلى أن تكمل النفس وتصير طاهرة عن جميع العلائق الجسمانية، وحينئذ تتخلص إلى عالم القدس والطهارة. وثانيها : الذين يجوزون انتقال الأرواح الإنسانية إلى أبدان البهائم، ويقال لهم أهل المسخ .
وثالثها : الذين قالوا : الأرواح البشرية إذا فارقت أبدانها فقد تتعلق بأبدان الحيوانات، وبأبدان النباتات والمعادن والبسائط قالوا وهذا هو غاية العذاب، وإليه الإشارة بالدركات الضيقة في جهنم.
قالوا : وذلك لأن القوى الناطقة والحساسة والفعالة والغاذية كلها أنوار تفيض من عالم الأرواح، فتغوص في بواطن الأجسام، وبواطن الأجسام مظلمة جدا، إلا أنها مستنيرة بسبب غوص هذه القوى فيها وكلما كانت هذه القوى أقل كانت بواطن الأجسام أشد ظلمة وأعظم ضيقًا فالأرواح البشرية إذا انتقلت من أبدانها إلى هذه الأجسام بقيت في غاية الظلمات والضيق والشدة، أما أجسام الأفلاك فإنها لكثرة القوى الروحانية التي فيها كانت في غاية الضوء والفسحة، فالأرواح البشرية إذا فارقت أبدانها وانتقلت إلى التعلق بعالم الأفلاك كانت في غاية الغبطة والفرح والضوء والسرور والروح والراحة والريحان.
فهذا هو الإشارة إلى تفصيل مذاهب القائلين بالمعاد الروحاني.
The perception of the subject which is the individual, but the perceiver of this universal is the soul, so your perceiver of this particular is also the soul, so it is established that the soul perceives particulars? If this is established, we say: The soul has two attributes: perception and action. Perception is of two kinds: perception of particulars and perception of universals. So the soul is described by these two kinds of perception, and by this action which is movement. When the body dies and the bodily veil is removed, the lights of the world of majesty become manifest to it, so its perception and action increase and reach the limit of perfection, and its rank approaches the rank of angels—who are the spirits of the celestial world—and that is the greatest bliss and the highest degree. The second group: those who say that these human spirits cannot perceive particulars except through bodily instruments. When the body dies and these bodily instruments are disrupted, it is not improbable that these souls become attached to a part of the heavens so that that part becomes an instrument for the soul by which it can perceive particulars such as sight, hearing, imagination, and thought. The third group: those who say: When the soul's attachment to a particular body is cut off, it attaches to another body. If in the first body it was among pure virtuous souls, it attaches to a noble virtuous body; if in the first body it was among ignorant harmful souls, it attaches to a body suitable for it. These are the proponents of transmigration (tanāsukh), and they are sects: One of them: those who say that human spirits attach only to human bodies, then they keep transferring from body to body until the soul becomes complete and pure from all bodily attachments, and then it is released to the world of holiness and purity. The second: those who permit the transfer of human spirits to animal bodies, and they are called the people of metamorphosis (maskh). The third: those who say that human spirits, when they depart their bodies, may attach to animal bodies, plant bodies, minerals, and simple bodies. They said this is the extreme torment, and it is indicated by the narrow depths in Hell. They said: That is because the rational, sensitive, active, and nutritive powers are all lights flowing from the world of spirits, descending into the interiors of bodies. The interiors of bodies are extremely dark, except they become illuminated by the descent of these powers into them. The less these powers are, the darker and narrower the interiors of bodies become. So human spirits, when they transfer from their bodies to these bodies, remain in extreme darkness, narrowness, and severity. As for the celestial bodies, due to the abundance of spiritual powers in them, they are in extreme light and spaciousness. So human spirits, when they depart their bodies and transfer to attachment to the celestial world, are in extreme bliss, joy, light, delight, spirit, comfort, and fragrance. This is the indication of the details of the doctrines of those who affirm spiritual resurrection.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage classifies the various views on spiritual resurrection (al-maʿād al-rūḥānī). It begins by establishing that the soul perceives particulars directly, then presents three groups: (1) Those who hold that the soul perceives particulars directly without instruments, and after death, freed from the bodily veil, it attains perfection and bliss akin to angels. (2) Those who hold that souls need bodily instruments; after death, they attach to a part of the heavens as an instrument for perception. (3) Those who hold transmigration (tanāsukh), which is subdivided into three sects: (a) souls transfer only among human bodies until purification, (b) souls transfer to animal bodies (maskh), and (c) souls transfer to animals, plants, minerals, etc., resulting in extreme torment due to darkness and narrowness. The passage explains that the degree of light or darkness depends on the spiritual powers present in the bodies. This serves as a detailed exposition of the doctrines of spiritual resurrection alone.

Key Terms
آلات جسمانية
إدراك جزئيات
أجزاء السماوات

B) A part of the heavens
C) Another human body
D) No instrument is needed

Key Takeaway
The second group holds that souls need bodily instruments even after death, and they attach to celestial parts to perceive particulars like sight and thought.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This passage says souls 'cannot perceive particulars except through bodily instruments.' In your daily life, how often do you let your physical desires and senses dictate your spiritual state? What would it mean to recalibrate that dependence before death?
?
The idea that the soul must find a new instrument after death suggests that God's creation is purposeful even in the afterlife. How does that challenge any complacency you have about the reality of the Hereafter? What step can you take today to live with that reality?

Transmigration and Its Sects
Razi presents the third group's view on spiritual resurrection: transmigration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third group's doctrine of transmigration (tanasukh) and its three sects regarding the transfer of souls after death.

Core Idea
Transmigration cycles souls through bodies until purification or punishment.

Imam al-Razi concludes his classification with the third group: those who affirm transmigration (tanasukh). They believe that when the soul leaves one body, it attaches to another. He then divides them into three sects: those who restrict transfer to human bodies, those who allow transfer to animal bodies (maskh), and those who allow transfer to plants, minerals, and simple bodies, resulting in extreme torment. This passage highlights the diversity within this rejected doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on transmigration
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note the general principle: the soul attaches to a new body based on its previous state.
2
Identify the three sects
The passage enumerates three sects: (1) souls transfer only among human bodies until purification, (2) souls can transfer to animal bodies, (3) souls can transfer to animals, plants, minerals, etc.
These are listed as 'إحداها', 'وثانيها', 'وثالثها'.
3
Understand the reasoning for torment
The third sect explains that the darkness and narrowness of lower bodies cause extreme torment, while celestial bodies bring bliss.
This is based on the amount of spiritual powers in each body.
4
Relate to spiritual resurrection
Razi presents this as part of the detailed doctrines of those who affirm spiritual resurrection, but note that transmigration is a deviant view in orthodox Islam.
This classification is for completeness, not endorsement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Rationale for Combined Spiritual and Bodily Resurrection
Rational argument for combining spiritual and bodily resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument put forth by Imam Razi for combining spiritual and bodily resurrection in the afterlife.

Core Idea
Only in the afterlife can soul and body achieve their fullest happiness together.

This lesson explores a sophisticated argument from Imam Razi that reconciles reason and revelation on the nature of resurrection. He explains why both spiritual and bodily happiness are needed and why their combination is only possible after death. The passage also touches on the refutation of those who deny resurrection entirely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully to get a sense of Razi's argument.
Pay attention to the key terms like معاد روحاني and معاد جسماني.
2
Identify the two kinds of happiness
Notice that Razi distinguishes between spiritual happiness (knowledge and love of God) and bodily happiness (sensory pleasure). This is the foundation of his argument.
3
Understand why combination is impossible now but possible later
Razi argues that in this world, the weakness of the soul prevents experiencing both together, but after death, the soul gains strength and can be reunited with the body to achieve both simultaneously.
This is the key move that reconciles reason and revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل السابع: في تفصيل مذاهب القائلين بالمعاد الروحاني والجسماني معا اعلم أن كثيرًا من المحققين قالوا بهذا القول، وذلك لأنهم أرادوا الجمع بين الحكمة والشريعة فقالوا دل العقل على أن سعادة الأرواح في معرفة الله وفي محبته، وعلى أن سعادة الأجساد في إدراك المحسوسات.
قالوا: لأن الاستقراء دل على أن الجمع بين هاتين السعادتين في الحياة الدنيوية غير ممكن، وذلك لأن الإنسان حال كونه مستغرفًا في تجلي أنوار عالم الغيب لا يمكنه الالتفات إلى شيء من اللذات الجسمانية، وحال كونه مشغولاً باستيفاء اللذات الجسمانية لا يمكنه الالتفات إلى اللذات الروحانية، لكن هذا الجمع إنما يتعذر لأجل أن الأرواح البشرية ضعيفة في هذا العالم، فإذا مات واستمدت هذه الأرواح من عالم القدس والطهارة وقويت وكملت فإذا أعيدت إلى الأبدان مرة أخرى لم يبعد أن تصير هذه الحالة هي الغاية القصوى في مراتب السعادات.
وهذا المعنى لم يقم على امتناعه برهان عقلي وهو جمعه بين الحكمة النبوية والقوانين الفلسفية، فوجب المصير إليه وأما معرفة تفاصيل هذه الأحوال، فمما لا سبيل إليها في هذا العالم.
فقد تكلمنا الآن في تقرير المعاد الجسماني وحده والمعاد الروحاني وحده، وفي كيفية الجمع بينهما، وأما الذين ينكرونهما معا فهو قول من قال: النفس هي فقط، فإذا مات الإنسان فقد عدمت النفس. ثم إنه ينكر إعادة المعدوم، المزاج وحينئذ يلزم إنكار المعاد مطلقا . إلا أن الكلام في إبطال هاتين المقدمتين قد تقدم.
واعلم أنا كنا قد ذكرنا أن مطالب مسألة المعاد أربعة :
الأول : كيفية تخريب العالم الأصغر، وهو الإنسان.
Chapter Seven: On detailing the doctrines of those who affirm both spiritual and bodily resurrection together. Know that many of the verifiers (muḥaqqiqūn) held this view, because they intended to combine wisdom (ḥikma) and divine law (sharīʿa). They said: Reason indicates that the happiness of souls lies in knowledge of God and love of Him, and that the happiness of bodies lies in perception of sensible things. They said: Because induction (istiqrāʾ) indicates that combining these two kinds of happiness in this worldly life is impossible. That is because when a person is immersed in the manifestation of the lights of the unseen world, he cannot attend to any bodily pleasure; and when he is occupied with enjoying bodily pleasures, he cannot attend to spiritual pleasures. But this combination is impossible only because human souls are weak in this world. When [a person] dies and these souls derive strength from the world of holiness and purity, and become strong and perfect, then when they are returned to bodies once again, it is not improbable that this state becomes the ultimate goal in the ranks of happiness. No rational proof has been established for its impossibility, and it combines prophetic wisdom and philosophical principles, so it must be adopted. As for knowing the details of these conditions, there is no way to them in this world. We have now spoken on establishing bodily resurrection alone, spiritual resurrection alone, and how to combine them. As for those who deny both, it is the view of those who say: the soul is only the temperament (mizāj); when a person dies, the soul ceases to exist. Then he denies the restoration of the nonexistent, and thus denial of resurrection follows absolutely. However, the refutation of these two premises has already preceded. Know that we have mentioned that the requirements of the question of resurrection are four: First: the manner of corrupting the microcosm, which is man.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage is a rational argument for the combined resurrection of soul and body. Razi first states that many verifiers (muḥaqqiqūn) affirm both to reconcile reason and revelation. They reason: rational happiness is knowing and loving God; bodily happiness is sensory perception. In this world, they cannot be combined because immersion in one precludes the other, due to the weakness of human souls. After death, souls gain strength from the divine world; upon return to bodies, they can achieve both simultaneously, which is the highest happiness. No rational proof disproves this, and it combines prophetic wisdom and philosophical principles, so it is obligatory to accept. Details are unknown in this world. Then Razi summarizes that he has covered bodily resurrection alone, spiritual resurrection alone, and their combination. He notes the view of those who deny both, i.e., those who reduce soul to temperament and deny resurrection, but says their refutation was already presented. Finally, he announces that the topics of resurrection are four, starting with the destruction of the microcosm (man), a foreshadowing of the next discussion.

معاد جسماني
حكمة
شريعة
سعادة
استقراء
برهان عقلي
عالم الغيب
مزاج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Razi claims spiritual and bodily happiness can be combined in this world.
Correction: Razi explicitly states that this combination is impossible in this world due to the soul's weakness; it is only possible in the afterlife.

Checkpoint
Why is combining spiritual and bodily happiness impossible in this world according to the passage?
A) Because the soul is too weak
B) Because the body is impure
C) Because it is rationally impossible
D) Because divine law forbids it

Key Takeaway
Razi argues that the ultimate happiness of both soul and body is only achievable after death when the soul, strengthened, returns to the body in the afterlife.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You often feel torn between spiritual devotion and worldly enjoyment. After reading this passage, how does your perspective on death change? Are you willing to delay the fulfillment of both until you are reunited with your body in the afterlife, or do you continue to demand it now, despite the soul's weakness?
?
This passage says that after death, the soul becomes strong and perfect. If you truly believed that, would you fear death less? What attachments to this world are you holding onto that prevent you from longing for that ultimate happiness?
?
Razi argues that no rational proof forbids the combination of spiritual and bodily happiness in the next life. Yet you act as if this world is all there is. How would your daily choices—your work, your relationships, your leisure—change if you lived with the certainty that the next life offers both pleasures together?

The Spiritual Resurrection View
Imam Razi describes the state of souls in spiritual resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the spiritual resurrection view as described by Imam Razi, including the contrast between earthly and celestial bodies.

Core Idea
Souls find light and joy only in the celestial realm.

In this passage, Imam Razi outlines the doctrine of spiritual resurrection held by some theologians. He contrasts the darkness of earthly bodies with the luminosity of celestial spheres, explaining the soul's journey after death. Read carefully to grasp the core of this view.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic once to absorb its rhythm and notice key terms like 'ظلمة' and 'ضوء'.
2
Identify the two types of bodies
Notice the contrast between earthly bodies (dark, constricting) and celestial bodies (luminous, spacious). This contrast is central to the argument.
The passage uses 'ظلمة' for darkness and 'ضوء' for light.
3
Understand the soul's transfer
The passage describes what happens when souls depart from their bodies: if they attach to earthly bodies they remain in darkness; if they attach to celestial spheres they are in light and joy.
4
Reflect on the spiritual resurrection claim
Consider that this view sees resurrection as only spiritual, not bodily. The passage is presenting this position, not necessarily endorsing it.
This is a specific theological position within discussions of the afterlife.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأجسام أشد ظلمة وأعظم ضيقًا فالأرواح البشرية إذا انتقلت من أبدانها إلى هذه الأجسام بقيت في غاية الظلمات والضيق والشدة، أما أجسام الأفلاك فإنها لكثرة القوى الروحانية التي فيها كانت في غاية الضوء والفسحة، فالأرواح البشرية إذا فارقت أبدانها وانتقلت إلى التعلق بعالم الأفلاك كانت في غاية الغبطة والفرح والضوء والسرور والروح والراحة والريحان. فهذا هو الإشارة إلى تفصيل مذاهب القائلين بالمعاد الروحاني.
Bodies are more intensely dark and greatly constricting, so when human souls transfer from their bodies to these bodies, they remain in extreme darkness, constriction, and severity. As for the celestial bodies, due to the abundance of spiritual powers in them, they are in extreme light and spaciousness. So when human souls depart from their bodies and transfer to attachment to the realm of the celestial spheres, they are in extreme delight, joy, light, pleasure, spirit, comfort, and fragrance. This is an indication of the detailed positions of those who affirm spiritual resurrection (al-maʿād al-rūḥānī).
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage describes the view of those who believe only in spiritual resurrection, denying bodily resurrection. The author contrasts two types of bodies: earthly bodies, which are dark and constricting, and celestial bodies (the spheres), which are luminous and spacious. When human souls leave their earthly bodies and attach to earthly elements, they remain in darkness and narrowness. But if they attach to celestial spheres, they experience extreme joy and light. This is the essence of the spiritual resurrection doctrine: the soul's migration to a higher, luminous realm.

Key Terms
المعاد الروحاني
الأرواح البشرية
الأفلاك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think this passage denies bodily resurrection entirely.
Correction: The passage only describes the spiritual resurrection view, not necessarily endorsing it. It is an exposition of a particular theological position.

Checkpoint
According to the description of spiritual resurrection, what happens to human souls after death?
A) They remain attached to earthly bodies in darkness.
B) They transfer to celestial spheres and experience light and joy.
C) They are annihilated and cease to exist.
D) They are reborn in new earthly bodies.

Key Takeaway
In spiritual resurrection, the soul finds ultimate joy by attaching to the luminous celestial spheres after leaving the dark earthly body.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage describes earthly bodies as dark and constricting. What attachments to this world are keeping your soul in darkness, and what steps will you take this week to loosen their hold so your soul can move toward the light?
?
Your soul is destined for either the constriction of earthly attachments or the spaciousness of the celestial realm. Which direction is your soul oriented toward right now, and what is one concrete change you can make today to set it on the path to true delight?
?
The soul experiences extreme delight upon reaching the celestial spheres. Does your daily pursuit of pleasure align with that eternal joy, or are you settling for temporary comforts that leave your soul in darkness? What will you sacrifice to seek that lasting light?

Combining Spiritual and Bodily Resurrection
Imam Razi presents the view of those who combine spiritual and bodily resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument for combining spiritual and bodily resurrection as presented by the investigators (al-muḥaqqiqūn) and how it reconciles reason and revelation.

Core Idea
The ultimate happiness combines spiritual and bodily joys, made possible in the afterlife.

This lesson explores the view of those who affirm both spiritual and bodily resurrection. Imam Razi presents the reasoning of the 'investigators' who seek to harmonize rational philosophy with revealed law. They argue that while this combination is impossible in this life due to the soul's weakness, it becomes achievable in the afterlife when the soul is strengthened.

Guided Path
1
Understand the claim of the investigators
Recognize that the investigators affirm both spiritual and bodily resurrection, aiming to combine wisdom and religious law.
They are not rejecting one in favor of the other.
2
Identify the two types of happiness
Note that reason indicates spiritual happiness lies in knowledge and love of God, while bodily happiness lies in sensory perception.
These are distinct and separate in nature.
3
See why combination is impossible in this world
Induction shows that a person cannot be absorbed in spiritual pleasures and bodily pleasures simultaneously because the soul is weak in this world.
The soul's weakness prevents multitasking between the two realms.
4
Learn why it becomes possible in the afterlife
After death, the soul derives strength from the sacred realm and becomes powerful. When returned to the body, it can combine both types of happiness.
This is presented as the ultimate happiness, with no rational proof against it.
5
Note the denial of materialists
The passage briefly mentions those who deny resurrection altogether, reducing the soul to the temperament, but notes that this refutation has already been given.
This serves as a contrast to the affirmed position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل السابع: في تفصيل مذاهب القائلين بالمعاد الروحاني والجسماني معا اعلم أن كثيرًا من المحققين قالوا بهذا القول، وذلك لأنهم أرادوا الجمع بين الحكمة والشريعة فقالوا دل العقل على أن سعادة الأرواح في معرفة الله وفي محبته، وعلى أن سعادة الأجساد في إدراك المحسوسات. قالوا : لأن الاستقراء دل على أن الجمع بين هاتين السعادتين في الحياة الدنيوية غير ممكن، وذلك لأن الإنسان حال كونه مستغرفًا في تجلي أنوار عالم الغيب لا يمكنه الالتفات إلى شيء من اللذات الجسمانية، وحال كونه مشغولاً باستيفاء اللذات الجسمانية لا يمكنه الالتفات إلى اللذات الروحانية، لكن هذا الجمع إنما يتعذر لأجل أن الأرواح البشرية ضعيفة في هذا العالم، فإذا مات واستمدت هذه الأرواح من عالم القدس والطهارة وقويت وكملت فإذا أعيدت إلى الأبدان مرة هناك قوية قادرة على الجمع بين الأمرين، ولا شك أن هذه الحالة هي الغاية القصوى في مراتب السعادات. وهذا المعنى لم يقم على امتناعه برهان عقلي وهو جمعه بين الحكمة النبوية والقوانين الفلسفية، فوجب المصير إليه وأما معرفة تفاصيل هذه الأحوال، فمما لا سبيل إليها في هذا العالم. فقد تكلمنا الآن في تقرير المعاد الجسماني وحده والمعاد الروحاني وحده، وفي كيفية الجمع بينهما، وأما الذين ينكرونهما معا فهو قول من قال: النفس هي فقط، فإذا مات الإنسان فقد عدمت النفس. ثم إنه ينكر إعادة المعدوم، وحينئذ يلزم إنكار المعاد مطلقا . إلا أن الكلام في إبطال هاتين المقدمتين قد تقدم.
Chapter Seven: On detailing the positions of those who affirm both spiritual and bodily resurrection. Know that many of the investigators (al-muḥaqqiqīn) held this view, because they intended to combine wisdom (al-ḥikma) and religious law (al-sharīʿa). They said: reason indicates that the happiness of souls lies in knowledge of God and love of Him, and that the happiness of bodies lies in perceiving sensory things. They said: because induction (al-istiqrāʾ) indicates that combining these two happinesses in this worldly life is impossible. This is because when a person is immersed in the manifestation of the lights of the unseen world, he cannot attend to any bodily pleasures; and when he is occupied in obtaining bodily pleasures, he cannot attend to spiritual pleasures. But this combination is only impossible because human souls are weak in this world. When [a person] dies and these souls derive strength from the world of sanctity and purity, and become strong and complete, then when they are returned to bodies once again there, they are strong and capable of combining the two matters. There is no doubt that this state is the ultimate limit in the ranks of happiness. No rational proof has been established against the impossibility of this meaning, and it combines prophetic wisdom and philosophical laws, so it is necessary to adopt it. As for knowing the details of these states, there is no way to them in this world. Now we have spoken about establishing bodily resurrection alone and spiritual resurrection alone, and about the manner of combining them. As for those who deny both together, it is the view of those who say: the soul is only the temperament; when a person dies, the soul ceases to exist. Then he denies the return of the non-existent, and thus the denial of resurrection (al-maʿād) follows absolutely. However, the discussion on refuting these two premises has preceded.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage presents the view of the 'investigators' who affirm both spiritual and bodily resurrection. The author explains that they aim to reconcile reason (wisdom) and revelation (sharia). Reason shows that spiritual happiness is in knowing and loving God, while bodily happiness is in sensory perception. Inductive observation shows that in this world, one cannot simultaneously be absorbed in spiritual contemplation and bodily pleasures because the soul is weak. After death, the soul is strengthened by drawing from the sacred realm, and when it is returned to the body in the afterlife, it becomes capable of combining both types of happiness. This, he says, is the ultimate happiness, and no rational proof refutes it. The author also mentions the deniers (materialists) who reduce the soul to the temperament and deny resurrection altogether, but notes that their refutation has already been given.

المحققين

Correction: The investigators argue that after death, the soul becomes strong enough to attend to both spiritual and bodily pleasures simultaneously when reunited with the body, making the combination possible.

Checkpoint

A) Because God does not will it.
B) Because human souls are too weak in this world to attend to both simultaneously.
C) Because bodily pleasures are forbidden in this world.
D) Because the body and soul cannot coexist after death.

Key Takeaway
The investigators argue that the ultimate happiness lies in the combination of spiritual and bodily joys, which becomes achievable in the afterlife when the soul is strengthened.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about your life, which do you find yourself prioritizing: spiritual pursuits like prayer and learning, or bodily pleasures? How does this passage challenge the way you balance them right now? What one change can you make today to give more weight to spiritual happiness?
?
The investigators say that in the afterlife, the soul becomes strong enough to combine both joys. What are you doing right now to strengthen your soul for that journey? If you were to die today, would your soul be ready to derive strength from the world of sanctity?
?
This passage is about harmonizing wisdom (reason) and religious law. Have you ever felt a tension between what your intellect concludes and what your faith teaches? What would it look like for you to genuinely seek this harmony instead of choosing one side? Will you commit to exploring that tension rather than avoiding it?

The Third Demand: Destruction of the Macrocosm
Imam Razi enumerates the four demands of resurrection and details the third with Quranic proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third demand of resurrection — the destruction of the macrocosm — and its basis in rational possibility and Quranic revelation.

Core Idea
The destruction of the universe is possible by reason, but actual occurrence is known only from the Qur'an.

In this passage, Imam Razi continues his systematic treatment of resurrection (al-ma'ad) by shifting from the microcosm (human) to the macrocosm (the entire universe). He explains that while reason can affirm the possibility of cosmic destruction, the certainty of its occurrence comes exclusively from divine revelation. He then marshals an array of Quranic verses describing the transformation of earth, mountains, seas, heavens, and celestial bodies on the Day of Judgment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage gently
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the repetitive structure: each component is introduced with 'As for...' followed by verses.
2
Identify the four demands
The passage starts by listing the four demands (maṭālib) of resurrection. Find them and note the progression from microcosm to macrocosm.
3
Focus on the third demand
The third demand is the destruction of the macrocosm. Notice that Razi first states its rational possibility, then says actual occurrence is only from the Qur'an. Locate this key distinction.
This is the central teaching: reason vs. revelation.
4
Examine the Quranic proofs
Razi cites multiple verses for each element: earth, mountains, seas, heavens, sun/moon. Read each set and observe the vivid descriptions of cosmic dissolution.
These verses collectively establish the occurrence of the destruction.
5
Reflect on the fourth demand
The passage concludes by introducing the fourth demand (rebuilding) and a brief rational argument from God's knowledge and power. See how this connects to the third demand.
The fourth demand is only started here; the details are deferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنا كنا قد ذكرنا أن مطالب مسألة المعاد أربعة : الأول : كيفية تخريب العالم الأصغر، وهو الإنسان. الثاني : كيفية عمارته بعد تخريبه وهو البعث والحشر والنشر. المطلب الثالث : كيفية تخريب العالم الأكبر، وقد بينا بالدليل العقلي جوازه، وأما الوقوع فلا يمكن أن يؤخذ إلا من القرآن قال الله تعالى في صفة الأرض: ﴿يَوْمَ تُبَدَّلُ الْأَرْضُ غَيْرَ الْأَرْضِ وَالسَّمَاوَاتُ﴾ [إبراهيم: ٤٨] . وأما الجبال : فقد ذكر أحوالها في آيات : إحداها : قوله تعالى: ﴿وَحُمِلَتِ الْأَرْضُ وَالْجِبَالُ فَدُكَّا دَكَّةً وَاحِدَةً﴾ [الحاقة: ١٤] . وثانيها: قوله تعالى: ﴿إِذَا رُجَّتِ الْأَرْضُ رَجًا وَبُسَّتِ الْجِبَالُ بَسًّا﴾ [الواقعة: ٤-٥] . وثالثها : قوله تعالى : ﴿وَتَكُونُ الْجِبَالُ كَالْعِهْنِ الْمَنفُوشِ﴾ [القارعة: ٥] . ورابعها : قوله تعالى : ﴿وَتَرَى الْجِبَالَ تَحْسَبُهَا جَامِدَةً وَهِيَ تَمُرُّ مَرَّ السَّحَابِ﴾ [النمل: ٨٨] . وخامسها : قوله تعالى: ﴿وَسُيِّرَتِ الْجِبَالُ فَكَانَتْ سَرَابًا﴾ [النبأ: ٢٠] . وأما البحار فقال تعالى في صفتها : ﴿وَالْبَحْرِ الْمَسْجُورِ﴾ [الطور: ٦] وفي آية أخرى ﴿وَإِذَا الْبِحَارُ فُجِّرَتْ﴾ [الانفطار: ٣] . وأما السماوات فقد ذكر صفاتها في آيات : إحداها : قوله تعالى: ﴿وَيَوْمَ تَشَقَّقُ السَّمَاءُ بِالْغَمَامِ وَنُزِّلَ الْمَلَائِكَةُ تَنزِيلًا﴾ [الفرقان: ٢٥] . وثانيها : قوله تعالى: ﴿إِذَا السَّمَاءُ انفَطَرَتْ﴾ [الانفطار: ١] و ﴿وَإِذَا السَّمَاءُ انشَقَّتْ﴾ [الانشقاق: ١] . وثالثها : قوله تعالى : ﴿وَفُتِحَتِ السَّمَاءُ فَكَانَتْ أَبْوَابًا﴾ [النبأ: ١٩] . ورابعها قوله تعالى : ﴿يَوْمَ تَكُونُ السَّمَاءُ كَالْمُهْلِ﴾ [المعارج: ٨] . وقال في صفة الشمس والقمر: ﴿إِذَا الشَّمْسُ كُوِّرَتْ وَإِذَا النُّجُومُ انكَدَرَتْ﴾ [التكوير: ١-٢] وقال في سورة القيامة : ﴿وَجُمِعَ الشَّمْسُ وَالْقَمَرُ﴾ [القيامة: ٩] . والمطلوب الرابع: هو أنه تعالى كيف يعمر هذا العالم الكبير بعد تخريبه؟ واعلم أن المعتمد في هذه المسألة هو أنه تعالى عالم بجميع الجزئيات والكليات، قادر على جميع الممكنات، فيكون لا محالة قادرًا على خلق الجنة والنار، وعلى إيصال جميع مقادير الثواب والعقاب إلى المطيعين والمذنبين وأما تفاصيل تلك الأفعال فلا يمكن
Know that we have mentioned that the demands of the issue of resurrection (al-maʿād) are four: First, the manner of destruction of the microcosm, which is man. Second, the manner of its reconstruction after its destruction, which is the resurrection (al-baʿth), gathering (al-ḥashr), and spreading (al-nashr). The third demand: the manner of destruction of the macrocosm. We have already shown by rational proof its permissibility. As for its actual occurrence, it can only be taken from the Qur'an. God Almighty said concerning the earth: "On the Day when the earth will be changed to another earth and the heavens [as well]" [Ibrahim:48]. As for the mountains, He mentioned their states in verses: First, His saying: "And the earth and the mountains are lifted up and crushed with one crushing" [al-Haqqah:14]. Second, His saying: "When the earth is shaken with a [violent] shaking, and the mountains are crushed, crushed" [al-Waqi'ah:4-5]. Third, His saying: "And the mountains will be like carded wool" [al-Qari'ah:5]. Fourth, His saying: "And you see the mountains, thinking them rigid, while they will pass as the passing of clouds" [an-Naml:88]. Fifth, His saying: "And the mountains are removed and become a mirage" [an-Naba':20]. As for the seas, He said concerning their description: "And the sea set on fire" [at-Tur:6], and in another verse: "And when the seas are erupted" [al-Infitar:3]. As for the heavens, He mentioned their descriptions in verses: First, His saying: "On the Day when the heaven will split open with clouds and the angels will be sent down in succession" [al-Furqan:25]. Second, His saying: "When the sky is split open" [al-Infitar:1] and "When the sky is split asunder" [al-Inshiqaq:1]. Third, His saying: "And the heaven is opened and becomes as gates" [an-Naba':19]. Fourth, His saying: "On the Day when the sky will be like molten copper" [al-Ma'arij:8]. And He said concerning the description of the sun and moon: "When the sun is wrapped up [in darkness] and when the stars fall, dispersing" [at-Takwir:1-2]. And He said in Surat al-Qiyama: "And the sun and the moon are joined together" [al-Qiyama:9]. The fourth demand: how God Almighty will rebuild this macrocosm after its destruction. Know that the relied-upon in this issue is that He Almighty is knower of all particulars and universals, powerful over all possible things, so He is inevitably able to create Paradise and Hell, and to deliver all measures of reward and punishment to the obedient and the sinful. But as for the details of those actions, they cannot [be known fully].
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage covers the third and fourth of the four demands (maṭālib) of resurrection. The first two demands (destruction of the microcosm and its reconstruction) are briefly stated. The third demand focuses on the destruction of the macrocosm (the universe). The author states that rational proof establishes its possibility, but actual occurrence is known only from revelation. He then cites numerous Quranic verses describing the transformation of the earth, mountains, seas, heavens, sun, and moon on the Day of Judgment. These verses collectively depict the catastrophic dissolution of the physical world. The fourth demand asks how God will rebuild the universe after its destruction. The author argues that since God knows all things and has power over all possibilities, He is certainly able to create Paradise and Hell and to dispense reward and punishment. However, the details of those eschatological events are beyond human knowledge in this world.

Key Terms
المعاد
تخريب العالم الأكبر
الآيات
الجنة والنار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that reason alone can prove the occurrence of the destruction of the universe.
Correction: The text explicitly states that rational proof only shows its possibility (jawāz), not its actual occurrence; the latter is known exclusively from the Qur'an.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Razi, how can we know that the destruction of the macrocosm will actually occur?
A) Through rational demonstration alone.
B) Through induction from natural disasters.
C) Only from the Qur'an.
D) Through philosophical speculation.

Key Takeaway
The destruction of the macrocosm is rationally possible but scripturally confirmed, and God's power over all possible things ensures the resurrection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author says that the actual destruction of the universe can only be known from the Qur'an, not from reason. Is your trust in the Qur'an's reports about the future of the cosmos as firm as your trust in rational proofs? What would it take for you to feel the same certainty about the Day of Judgment as you feel about, say, a mathematical fact? Let this question unsettle you until you act on it by reading the Qur'an with a heart seeking that certainty.
?
You have just read the detailed descriptions of the earth, mountains, seas, and heavens being destroyed. Which of these images strikes you most forcefully? Why? And what change must that image make in how you live today—right now, not tomorrow?
?
The author ends by saying that God is knower of all and powerful over all, so He can create Paradise and Hell. Do you live as if the reality of Paradise and Hell is as certain as the existence of the ground beneath your feet? If not, what is holding you back from that certainty? Identify one specific habit or thought pattern that you will change today because of this lesson.

Quranic Evidence for the Destruction of the Universe
Razi lists Quranic verses describing the destruction of earth, mountains, seas, heavens, and celestial bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses Quranic verses to demonstrate that the actual occurrence of the destruction of the universe is known only through revelation.

Core Idea
The Quran provides detailed descriptions of the cataclysmic events of the Day of Resurrection.

Razi has already proven by rational argument that the destruction of the universe is possible. But actual occurrence is known only through revelation. In this passage, he gathers verses from the Quran that describe the transformation of the earth, mountains, seas, heavens, and celestial bodies. This lesson guides you through these verses and how they form a comprehensive picture of the end of the world.

Guided Path
1
Understand the role of revelation
Razi distinguishes between rational permissibility and actual occurrence. Notice that he says the latter is taken only from the Quran.
This sets the epistemological foundation.
2
Explore verses for each element
Go through each category: earth, mountains, seas, heavens, sun/moon. Read each verse and its translation.
Observe the richness of descriptions.
3
Reflect on comprehensiveness
Multiple verses are cited for each element, showing the Quran's detailed account of the end of the world.
4
Connect to theological purpose
This evidence confirms the reality of the Day of Resurrection beyond rational demonstration, grounding faith in scripture.

The third demand: the manner of destroying the greater universe, and we have already proven by rational proof its permissibility. As for its occurrence, it can only be taken from the Quran. Allah Almighty said describing the earth: 'And the Day the earth is changed to other than the earth and the heavens' [Ibrahim:48]. As for the mountains, He mentioned their states in verses: First: His saying, exalted: 'And the earth and the mountains are lifted and crushed with one crushing' [Al-Haqqah:14]. Second: His saying, exalted: 'When the earth is shaken with a shaking and the mountains are crumbled with a crumbling' [Al-Waqi'ah:4-5]. Third: His saying, exalted: 'And the mountains become like carded wool' [Al-Qari'ah:5]. Fourth: His saying, exalted: 'And you see the mountains, thinking them firm, while they pass like the passing of clouds' [An-Naml:88]. Fifth: His saying, exalted: 'And the mountains are set in motion and become a mirage' [An-Naba':20]. As for the seas, He said, exalted, describing them: 'And the kindled sea' [At-Tur:6], and in another verse: 'And when the seas are burst forth' [Al-Infitar:3]. As for the heavens, He mentioned their descriptions in verses: First: His saying, exalted: 'And the Day the heaven is split with clouds and the angels are sent down in a descent' [Al-Furqan:25]. Second: His saying, exalted: 'When the heaven is split asunder' [Al-Infitar:1] and 'When the heaven is rent asunder' [Al-Inshiqaq:1]. Third: His saying, exalted: 'And the heaven is opened and becomes doorways' [An-Naba':19]. Fourth: His saying, exalted: 'On the Day the heaven becomes like molten copper' [Al-Ma'arij:8]. And He said describing the sun and moon: 'When the sun is wrapped up and when the stars fall' [At-Takwir:1-2], and He said in Surat Al-Qiyamah: 'And the sun and moon are joined' [Al-Qiyamah:9].

Commentary
This passage is a presentation of Quranic evidence for the destruction of the world, forming the third sub-question (al-matlub al-thalith) of the thirtieth question. Razi begins by noting that the permissibility of destruction is proven by rational proof, but its actual occurrence can only be known from revelation. He then lists verses from the Quran describing the transformation of the earth and the destruction of mountains, seas, and heavens, as well as the sun and moon. The verses demonstrate that the Quran provides detailed descriptions of the cataclysmic events of the Day of Resurrection. He cites multiple verses for each element, showing the comprehensiveness of the Quranic account. The passage emphasizes the role of revelation in confirming the details of eschatological events, beyond rational demonstration.

Refutation of the Fourth Doubt on Scriptural Transmission
Razi refutes the fourth doubt regarding the interruption of scriptural transmission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi refutes the fourth doubt regarding the interruption of scriptural transmission by addressing objections about abrogation, changing interests (masālih), and the reliability of Jewish transmission.

Core Idea
Abrogation reflects changing interests, not a change in God's knowledge.

This lesson presents Razi's response to a key objection about the interruption of prophetic transmission. The objector claims that if a law is abrogated, it implies that God changed His mind (badā'), and that the Jews' transmission of their scripture is reliable. Razi systematically refutes each point, showing that abrogation is due to differing interests and that the Jewish transmission chain was broken. Understanding this refutation clarifies the Islamic position on the integrity of previous scriptures.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the objections
Read the Arabic and translation, then list the four objections the author answers.
The first part is a general principle about good and evil.
2
Understand the response to the claim of interrupted transmission
The author says the prophet's people were destroyed by Nebuchadnezzar, breaking the chain of tawatur.
This explains how a scripture can be lost.
3
Analyze the refutation of the badā' objection
The author denies that abrogation implies a change in God's knowledge; instead, rulings change due to changing interests.
This is a crucial theological distinction.
4
Examine the response regarding the change of worship day and the Jewish transmission
The author argues that lack of known wisdom does not prove lack of wisdom, and that Jewish transmission is not reliable because it is interrupted.
This shows that the burden of proof lies with the objector.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحسن فيها على التفصيل، وإن لم يكن معلوما إلا أن وجه القبح فيها أيضا غير معلوم، ولا يبعد أن يحصل فيها وجه من وجوه الحكمة، وإن كنا لا نعرفه.
وأما الشبهة الرابعة فجوابها لم لا يجوز أن يقال : إنه ال بین أن شرعه منقطع مجذوذ، وكان معلومًا بالتواتر في دينه إلا أن قومه هلكوا بالكلية في زمان بخت نصر وصار الباقي أقل من عدد التواتر، فلا جرم انقطع هذا النقل. وقوله : النسخ يدل على البداء" قلنا : لا نسلم؛ فإنه لا يمتنع اختلاف الأحكام لاختلاف المصالح. وقوله : لا تأثير لتحويل العبادة من يوم السبت إلى يوم الجمعة" قلنا : كما لم يعلم وجه التفصيل في هذا التحويل لم يعلم أيضًا عدم الحكمة فيه، فسقط
الاستدلال.
10
وقوله : اليهود نقلوا قوله تمسكوا "بالسبت قلنا : إن تواترهم منقطع، فلا يفيد العلم، وبالله التوفيق.
The good in it is detailed, and if it is not known, except that the aspect of evil in it is also unknown, and it is not far that an aspect of wisdom occurs in it, even if we do not know it. As for the fourth doubt, its answer: why not say that his law was interrupted and cut off, and it was known by tawatur in his religion, but his people were entirely destroyed in the time of Nebuchadnezzar, and the remainder became less than the number of tawatur, so necessarily this transmission was cut off. And his saying: 'abrogation indicates badā'' we say: we do not accept; because it is not impossible that rulings differ due to differing interests. And his saying: 'there is no effect in changing worship from Saturday to Friday' we say: just as the detailed wisdom in this change is not known, so also the lack of wisdom in it is not known, so the inference falls. And his saying: 'the Jews transmitted his saying: hold fast to Saturday' we say: their tawatur is interrupted, so it does not give knowledge, and with God is success.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the fourth doubt (shubha) in a discussion likely about the preservation or abrogation of previous scriptures. The author first makes a general point about the possibility of wisdom in actions even if unknown. Then he addresses the fourth doubt: someone objects that the law of a prophet is interrupted. The answer explains that it is possible that the prophet's law was interrupted because his people were wiped out by Nebuchadnezzar, leaving too few for reliable transmission (tawatur). Next, the objector says abrogation implies badā' (change in God's knowledge). The author denies this, stating that rulings can change according to changing interests (masālih). Then the objector claims that changing the day of worship from Saturday to Friday has no effect. The author responds that just as the detailed wisdom of this change is unknown, so it cannot be asserted that there is no wisdom. The final objection: the Jews transmitted the command to keep Saturday. The author replies that their transmission chain was interrupted, so it does not yield certainty. The refutation ends with 'and with God is success'.

Key Terms
الشبهة الرابعة
التواتر
النسخ
البداء
المصالح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Abrogation (naskh) implies that God changes His mind (badā').
Correction: Razi clarifies that abrogation is due to changing interests (masālih) and does not entail any change in God's knowledge or will.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason given for the interruption of the prophet's transmission in the answer to the fourth doubt?
A) The people were destroyed in the time of Nebuchadnezzar
B) The prophet himself revoked it
C) The transmission was weak from the beginning
D) The Jews altered it

Key Takeaway
Razi demonstrates that the interruption of transmission can be explained historically, and that abrogation does not imply badā' but rather reflects divine wisdom in changing interests.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

In your daily life, there are commands from Allah that you do not fully understand the wisdom behind. Do you still obey wholeheartedly, or do you secretly doubt that there is any wisdom? What can you do this week to trust His wisdom even when you cannot see it?

Razi argues that abrogation reflects changing interests, not a change in God's knowledge. How does this affect your trust in the consistency of Allah's attributes? Are you living as if you believe He is unchangeably wise and just, or do your actions betray a fear that He might 'change His mind'?
?
The interruption of transmission happened because the people were destroyed. Your faith has reached you through an unbroken chain. What are you personally doing to preserve and transmit this faith to the next generation? If you were the only link left, would the chain break because of your negligence?
