The Ninth Proof: Iblis' Exception of the Sincere
Razi uses Iblis' oath and God's testimony to prove prophetic infallibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Iblis' oath and God's testimony together prove that the prophets are infallible.

Core Idea
Iblis cannot mislead the sincere, and God confirms prophets are sincere – hence they are sinless.

This lesson examines the ninth proof from Imam al-Razi's al-Arba'een, which draws on two Qur'anic facts: Iblis acknowledges his inability to mislead God's sincere servants, and God explicitly identifies certain prophets as being among those sincere ones. By combining these two points, a compelling logical argument for prophetic infallibility emerges.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice how Razi quotes Iblis' oath and then God's testimonies.
2
Identify the two premises
The argument has two key premises: (1) Iblis cannot mislead the sincere, (2) God declares certain prophets as sincere. Find these in the text.
The first premise is from Iblis' own words, the second from God's statements.
3
Trace the logical conclusion
From premises 1 and 2, conclude that Iblis' misguidance could not reach those prophets. Therefore, no sin occurred from them.
This conclusion establishes their infallibility.
4
Reflect on the misconception
Consider the common misunderstanding that sincerity might coexist with minor sins. Razi's proof shows sincerity here means full immunity from Iblis' influence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة التاسعة: قوله تعالى حكاية عن إبليس: ﴿قَالَ فَبِعِزَّتِكَ لَأُغْوِيَنَّهُمْ أَجْمَعِينَ إِلَّا عِبَادَكَ مِنْهُمُ الْمُخْلَصِينَ﴾ [ص: ٨٢-٨٣] استثنى المخلصين عن إضلاله وإغوائه، ثم إنه تعالى شهد على إبراهيم وإسحاق ويعقوب أنهم من المخلصين، حيث قال: ﴿إِنَّا أَخْلَصْنَاهُم بِخَالِصَةٍ ذِكْرَى الدَّارِ﴾ [ص: ٤٦] وقال في حق يوسف: ﴿إِنَّهُ مِنْ عِبَادِنَا الْمُخْلَصِينَ﴾ [يوسف: ٢٤] ولما أقر إبليس بأنه لا يغوي المخلصين وشهد الله تعالى بأن هؤلاء من المخلصين ثبت أن إغواء إبليس ووسوسته ما وصلا إليهم، وذلك يوجب القطع بعدم صدور المعصية عنهم.
The ninth proof: His saying – exalted be He – narrating from Iblis: 'He said: By Your might, I will surely mislead them all, except Your sincere servants among them [al-mukhlaseen].' [Sad 38:82-83] He excepted the sincere from his misguidance and leading astray. Then He – exalted be He – testified concerning Ibrahim, Ishaq, and Ya'qub that they are among the sincere, where He said: 'Indeed We purified them with a pure quality, the remembrance of the Home [of the Hereafter]' [Sad 38:46] and said concerning Yusuf: 'Indeed he is among Our sincere servants [al-mukhlaseen]' [Yusuf 12:24]. And when Iblis acknowledged that he does not mislead the sincere, and Allah the Exalted testified that these are among the sincere, it is established that Iblis' misguidance and whispering did not reach them, and that necessitates the certainty that no disobedience occurred from them.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a proof (hujja) for prophetic infallibility. Al-Razi cites the verse where Iblis swears by God's might to mislead all of humanity except God's sincere servants (al-mukhlaseen). Iblis acknowledges his inability to misguide the sincere ones. Then al-Razi points to other verses where God explicitly states that certain prophets—Ibrahim, Ishaq, Ya'qub, and Yusuf—are among the sincere (mukhlaseen). Since Iblis cannot misguide the sincere, and God confirms these prophets are sincere, it logically follows that Iblis' misguidance and whispering never reached them. Therefore, no sin could have occurred from them, because all sins are a form of following Iblis' misguidance. Thus, this argument proves their infallibility.

Key Terms
المخلصين (mukhlaseen)
إغواء (misguidance)
إبليس (Iblis)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that being 'sincere' can coexist with minor sins
Correction: Al-Razi uses Iblis' statement to show that the sincere are entirely immune to his misguidance.

Checkpoint
According to the ninth proof, why are prophets immune to sin?
A) Because they were born sinless
B) Because Iblis swore to mislead them but failed
C) Because God declared them sincere (mukhlaseen) and Iblis cannot mislead the sincere
D) Because they repented immediately after sinning

Key Takeaway
Iblis' admission that he cannot mislead the sincere, combined with God's testimony that prophets are sincere, proves their immunity from sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Iblis swore he could mislead everyone except the sincere. If you are being honest with yourself right now, do you believe you are among the sincere? What evidence in your daily life supports or challenges that belief?
?
Reflect on a recent time when you fell into sin, even a small one. Could that sin have been avoided if you had been more sincere? What would it take for you to be counted among the mukhlaseen?
?
The prophets were declared sincere by Allah Himself. You are not a prophet, but you are called to sincerity. What is one concrete change you can make today to move closer to that state, knowing that Iblis is powerless against the sincere?

Tenth Proof: Those Who Did Not Follow Iblis Are the Prophets
Al-Razi's disjunctive proof for prophetic infallibility using Quran 34:20.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Razi uses a disjunctive syllogism from the Quran and consensus to prove that the prophets never sinned.

Core Idea
The prophets are the only believers who never followed Iblis, proving their sinlessness.

Al-Razi presents a powerful logical argument for prophetic infallibility rooted in a Quranic verse. He identifies two possibilities for who the excepted group in the verse could be, then eliminates one by appealing to both the Quran and consensus, leaving only the prophets. This lesson traces his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the verse citation and the logical structure that follows.
2
Identify the Quranic exception
The verse says most followed Iblis except a 'group of believers'. Ask: who could this group be?
Al-Razi immediately presents two possibilities.
3
Understand the disjunctive argument
The group is either the prophets or other believers. If they are other believers, those others would be more honorable (atqa) than prophets by Quran 49:13, which is impossible by consensus. Therefore, the group must be the prophets.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.
4
Connect sinlessness to the argument
Since sin is defined as following Iblis, and the prophets did not follow him, they never sinned. Reflect on how this proves infallibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة العاشرة: قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَلَقَدْ صَدَّقَ عَلَيْهِمْ إِبْلِيسُ ظَنَّهُ فَاتَّبَعُوهُ إِلَّا فَرِيقًا مِّنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ﴾ [سبأ: ٢٠] فذلك القوم الذين لم يتبعوا إبليس إما يقال: إنهم هم الأنبياء والرسل – صلوات الله وسلامه عليهم – أو غيرهم، فإن كانوا غير الأنبياء لزم أن يكونوا أفضل من الأنبياء؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ أَكْرَمَكُمْ عِندَ اللَّهِ أَتْقَاكُمْ﴾ [الحجرات: ١٣]. وتفضيل غير النبي على النبي باطل بالإجماع، فوجب القطع بأن أولئك الذين لم يتبعوا إبليس هم الأنبياء – صلوات الله وسلامه عليهم – وكل من أذنب فقد اتبع إبليس، فدل هذا على أن الأنبياء – صلوات الله وسلامه عليهم – ما أذنبوا البتة.
The tenth proof: Allah the Exalted said: 'And indeed Iblis had confirmed his assumption about them, so they followed him, except a group of the believers.' [Saba' 34:20] Those people who did not follow Iblis – either it is said that they are the prophets and messengers – peace and blessings of Allah be upon them – or others. If they are other than the prophets, then it would necessitate that they are better than the prophets, because of His saying: 'Indeed the most honorable of you with Allah is the most righteous of you' [Al-Hujurat 49:13]. And preferring a non-prophet over a prophet is invalid by consensus. So it is necessary to be certain that those who did not follow Iblis are the prophets – peace and blessings of Allah be upon them – and whoever has sinned has followed Iblis. So this indicates that the prophets – peace and blessings of Allah be upon them – never sinned at all.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a proof (hujja) for prophetic infallibility. Al-Razi cites the verse in which Iblis' assumption about humans is confirmed—they follow him, except a group of believers. This exception implies that there are some believers who did not follow Iblis. The question then arises: who are these excepted believers? They are either the prophets or some other believers. If they are not the prophets, then those non-prophets would be more righteous than the prophets, because the verse equates honor with taqwa (God-consciousness). But it is an established consensus (ijma') that no non-prophet can be superior to a prophet. Therefore, the excepted group must be the prophets themselves. And since sin is defined as following Iblis, and the prophets are those who did not follow him, it follows that they never committed any sin.

Key Terms
اتبع (follow)
فريق (group)
مؤمنون (believers)
أنبياء (prophets)
إبليس (Iblis)
تفضيل (preferring)
إجماع (consensus)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The excepted group could be ordinary believers who are more pious than prophets.
Correction: Al-Razi argues that if ordinary believers were more pious (atqa), they would be better than prophets, which is impossible by consensus. Thus, the group must be the prophets themselves.

Checkpoint
In the tenth proof, what is the key premise that forces the conclusion that the excepted group are the prophets?
A) The verse explicitly names the prophets
B) If they were non-prophets, they would be better than prophets, which is invalid by consensus
C) Iblis himself said he would not mislead prophets
D) The prophets admitted they never sinned

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi proves that the only believers who never followed Iblis are the prophets, establishing their complete sinlessness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that whoever sins has followed Iblis. Think of a sin you committed recently. In that moment, did you recognize that you were following Iblis? What will you do tomorrow to catch yourself before you follow his whispers again?
?
The prophets never failed to resist Iblis. You and I fail often. How does this truth make you feel about your own weakness? Will you let it drive you to despair, or to seek Allah's help more earnestly? What specific action can you take tonight to strengthen your resolve?
?
Al-Razi's proof shows that the most honorable people are those who do not follow Iblis. Your honor with Allah depends on your taqwa. If you were to die right now, what would your record show? How can you, starting today, ensure that you are counted among those who resist Iblis, even if you are not a prophet?

Eleventh Proof: Prophets Cannot Be of Satan's Party
Razi argues that if prophets sinned, they would belong to Satan's party, which is false; this proves their sinlessness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'anic division of people into two parties (Satan's and Allah's) leads to a proof of prophetic sinlessness.

Core Idea
If prophets sinned, they would be in Satan's party—an absurd consequence.

Razi here uses a clever argument based on Qur'anic categories. He shows that sin would place prophets in a group that contradicts their exalted status. Let's see how he builds this proof from the verses themselves.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Note the two Qur'anic verses Razi cites.
Pay attention to the logical structure: division, implication, absurd conclusion.
2
Identify the two parties
Razi divides morally responsible people into two groups based on Qur'an: the party of Satan (al-Khasirun) and the party of Allah (al-Muflihun). Understand who belongs to each.
Satan's party does what Satan wants; Allah's party are the successful.
3
Trace the conditional argument
If prophets sinned, they would be doing what Satan commands, thus belonging to Satan's party. Then the verse about losers would apply to them.
The argument relies on the definition of 'party of Satan'.
4
See the reductio ad absurdum
If prophets are in Satan's party, then ordinary sinless believers (ascetics) would be in Allah's party. This would make ordinary believers far better than prophets, which is impossible.
The absurdity proves the original assumption (prophets sin) is false.
5
Reach the conclusion
Therefore, prophets must be sinless. They cannot belong to Satan's party, and they are the best of creation.
This proof is based purely on Qur'anic divisions and logical necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الحادية عشر: أنه تعالى قسم المكلفين إلى قسمين: حزب الشيطان، كما قال: ﴿أُولَٰئِكَ حِزْبُ الشَّيْطَانِ أَلَا إِنَّ حِزْبَ الشَّيْطَانِ هُمُ الْخَاسِرُونَ﴾ [المجادلة: ١٩]، وحزب الله، كما قال: ﴿أُولَٰئِكَ حِزْبُ اللهِ أَلَا إِنَّ حِزْبَ اللهِ هُمُ الْمُفْلِحُونَ﴾ [المجادلة: ٢٢]. ولا شك أن حزب الشيطان هم الذين يفعلون ما يريده الشيطان ويأمرهم به، فلو صدرت الذنوب عن الأنبياء والرسل لصدق عليهم أنهم من حزب الشيطان، ولصدق عليهم قول الله تعالى: ﴿أَلَا إِنَّ حِزْبَ الشَّيْطَانِ هُمُ الْخَاسِرُونَ﴾ [المجادلة: ١٩]، ولصدق على الزهاد من آحاد الأمة قوله تعالى: ﴿أَلَا إِنَّ حِزْبَ اللهِ هُمُ الْمُفْلِحُونَ﴾ [المجادلة: ٢٢]. وحينئذ يلزم أن يكون كل واحد من آحاد الأمة أفضل بكثير من الأنبياء – صلوات الله وسلامه عليهم – ولا شك في بطلان ذلك.
The eleventh proof: He – the Exalted – divided the morally responsible into two groups: the party of Satan, as He said: 'Those are the party of Satan; beware, indeed the party of Satan are the losers' [Al-Mujadilah 58:19], and the party of Allah, as He said: 'Those are the party of Allah; beware, indeed the party of Allah are the successful' [Al-Mujadilah 58:22]. And there is no doubt that the party of Satan are those who do what Satan wants and commands them. So if sins occurred from the prophets and messengers, it would be true of them that they are of the party of Satan, and the saying of Allah the Exalted 'Beware, indeed the party of Satan are the losers' would apply to them. And the saying of Allah the Exalted 'Beware, indeed the party of Allah are the successful' would apply to the ascetics among the ordinary members of the community. And then it would entail that every single ordinary member of the community is far better than the prophets – peace and blessings of Allah be upon them – and there is no doubt about the falsehood of that.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is a proof (hujja) for prophetic infallibility. Al-Razi presents a division from the Qur'an: people are divided into two parties—the party of Satan and the party of Allah. The party of Satan is characterized by following Satan's desires and commands. If prophets committed sins, they would be following Satan's commands (since sin is what Satan desires), so they would belong to the party of Satan. Consequently, the verse condemning the party of Satan as losers would apply to them. Meanwhile, ordinary ascetics who avoid sin would be considered the party of Allah, successful. This would absurdly imply that ordinary believers are far better than prophets, which is impossible. Therefore, prophets cannot sin, because that would place them in the wrong party.

Key Terms
حزب الشيطان (party of Satan)
حزب الله (party of Allah)
الخاسرون (the losers)
المفلحون (the successful)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets might occasionally sin but remain in Allah's party due to repentance or status.
Correction: Sin, by definition, is doing what Satan desires; any sin would place the prophet in Satan's party according to the Qur'anic division, making the absurd consequence unavoidable.

Checkpoint
In the eleventh proof, what would be the consequence if prophets sinned?
A) They would still be in God's party due to their prophethood
B) Ordinary believers would become better than prophets
C) Satan would be more powerful
D) The verses would be contradictory

Key Takeaway
Prophets cannot sin because that would place them in Satan's party, an outcome contradictory to their rank and the Qur'anic description of believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you honestly examine your daily actions, which party's character do they belong to? This passage leaves no neutral ground. What would it take for you to ensure you are firmly in the party of Allah today?
?
The argument shows that any sin aligns with Satan's will, even 'small' ones. Is there a sin you have minimized or excused? How does this truth remove your excuse, and what step will you take this week to break that habit?
?
Prophets are sinless; you are not. Yet you are called to be among the successful party. What is the one area of your life where you are most vulnerable to following Satan's desires, and how can you turn it into an act of obedience to Allah starting now?

The Twelfth Proof: Prophetic Infallibility from Superiority over Angels
Al-Razi presents a proof for prophetic infallibility via comparison with sinless angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Razi uses the superiority of prophets over sinless angels to argue for prophetic infallibility.

Core Idea
If prophets sinned, they’d be less than sinless angels—but they’re superior, so they can’t sin.

This proof builds on an Ash'ari premise that prophets are superior to angels. Since angels never sin, any sin by prophets would make them inferior, contradicting their established excellence. Al-Razi cites a Quranic verse to reinforce the principle that God does not equate the righteous with the wicked.

Guided Path
1
Read and note the premises
Read the passage carefully and identify the two main premises: prophets are superior to angels, and angels are sinless.
2
Understand the logical implication
If prophets sinned, they would be less excellent than sinless angels, which contradicts their superiority. This is a contradiction, so the assumption that they can sin must be false.
3
Reflect on the Quranic support
Read the verse from Surat Sad (38:28) and consider how it supports the idea that God does not treat the righteous like the wicked, reinforcing the argument that prophets cannot be sinful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية عشر: أن أصحابنا بينوا أن الأنبياء أفضل من الملائكة، وسنقيم الدلالة على أن الملائكة ما أقدموا على شيء من الذنوب، فلو صدرت الذنوب عن الأنبياء – صلوات الله وسلامه عليهم – لامتنعوا أن يكونوا أزيد في الفضل عن الملائكة، لقوله تعالى: ﴿أَمْ نَجْعَلُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ كَالْمُفْسِدِينَ فِي الْأَرْضِ أَمْ نَجْعَلُ الْمُتَّقِينَ كَالْفُجَّارِ﴾ [ص: ٢٨].
The twelfth proof: Our companions have clarified that the prophets are superior to the angels, and we will establish the evidence that the angels never commit any sin. So if sins occurred from the prophets – peace and blessings of Allah be upon them – they would be prevented from being greater in excellence than the angels, because of His saying: 'Or do We make those who believe and do righteous deeds like those who spread corruption in the land, or do We make the righteous like the wicked?' [Sad 38:28].
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is a proof (hujja) for prophetic infallibility. Al-Razi references an Ash'ari doctrine that prophets are superior to angels, and he asserts that they will later prove that angels never sin. Given that angels are sinless and prophets are superior, if prophets committed sins, they would be less excellent than the sinless angels, which would contradict the established superiority. The Quranic verse (Sad 38:28) is cited to support the principle that God does not treat believers and righteous people the same as corrupters and wicked people. Thus, prophets, being the best of creation, cannot be associated with sin.

Key Terms
الملائكة (angels)
الفضل (excellence)
المتقين (the righteous)
الفجار (the wicked)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think angels are superior to prophets.
Correction: The Ash'ari position is that prophets are superior to angels, as al-Razi asserts. This premise is essential for this proof to work.

Checkpoint
In the twelfth proof, why does the fact that angels are sinless and prophets are superior to them prove prophets are sinless?
A) Because if prophets sinned, they would be like angels
B) Because if prophets sinned, they would be less than sinless angels, contradicting their superiority
C) Because angels do not need to be sinless
D) Because the verse only talks about believers

Key Takeaway
Prophets, being superior to sinless angels, must themselves be sinless; otherwise their excellence would be contradicted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that prophets are superior to sinless angels and that sin would diminish that excellence, what standard does that set for your own life as one who follows them? Will you stop making excuses for the sins you tolerate in yourself?
?
Read the verse, 'Or do We make those who believe and do righteous deeds like those who spread corruption in the land?' – Where do your daily actions place you? Are you willing to face the contradiction if your life looks more like the corrupt than the righteous?
?
This proof hinges on the idea that sin directly lowers one's rank. How would your schedule, habits, or relationships change today if you truly believed that every sin strips you of honor in God's sight? What is one sin you will abandon right now in response?

The Thirteenth Proof: Ibrahim's Imamate Necessitates Infallibility
Razi argues that Ibrahim's imamate requires sinlessness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the role of Ibrahim as an imam implies that prophets must be sinless.

Core Idea
A prophet as an imam must be sinless; his actions are to be followed.

This lesson presents a concise rational proof from the Quran that prophets cannot sin. Imam Razi uses the verse where Allah makes Ibrahim an imam for all people. The logic is simple: an imam is followed; if he sinned, that sin would have to be followed, which is absurd. Therefore, Ibrahim—and by extension all prophets—must be infallible.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text including the verse and Razi's reasoning. Then read the English translation to understand the literal meaning.
Notice how the verse is cited as evidence.
2
Understand the definition of imam
Razi states that an imam is one who is followed (يقتدى به). Reflect on what this implies about the imam's actions.
This is the key premise.
3
Follow the logical consequence
If Ibrahim sinned, then his followers would be obligated to imitate that sin. Since God would never obligate sin, Ibrahim must be sinless. Consider why this applies to all prophets who are imams.
This argument is a form of reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة عشر: قوله تعالى في حق إبراهيم: ﴿إِنِّي جَاعِلُكَ لِلنَّاسِ إِمَامًا﴾ [البقرة: ١٢٤] والإمام هو الذي يقتدى به، فلو صدرت الذنوب عن إبراهيم لكان اقتداء الخلق به في ذلك الذنب واجبًا، وإنه باطل.
The thirteenth proof: His saying – exalted be He – concerning Ibrahim: 'Indeed I will make you an imam for the people' [Al-Baqarah 2:124]. And the imam is one who is followed. So if sins occurred from Ibrahim, then the imitation of the people by him in that sin would be obligatory, and that is false.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is a proof (hujja) for prophetic infallibility. Al-Razi cites the verse where Allah declares Ibrahim an imam (leader) for humanity. An imam is someone whose actions are followed. If Ibrahim had committed any sin, it would logically follow that people would be obligated to imitate that sin, since he is a role model. But it is impossible that God would command people to sin. Therefore, Ibrahim must be sinless. The same reasoning applies to all prophets who are examples.

Key Terms
إمام
الاقتداء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A prophet's sin could be an exception and not meant to be imitated.
Correction: The role of an imam requires imitation in all actions. If a prophet sinned, that sin would be part of what is followed, making it obligatory. Since God does not obligate sin, prophets must be sinless.

Checkpoint
In the thirteenth proof, what is the consequence of a prophet sinning given that he is an imam?
A) The sin is forgiven automatically
B) People must imitate the sin
C) The prophet is no longer an imam
D) Only minor sins are not imitated

Key Takeaway
A prophet who is an imam must be sinless because his actions set the example to be followed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof argues that if a prophet sinned, following that sin would be obligatory. When you follow the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ, do you ever excuse yourself from a sunnah because it is 'just a recommended act'? Does this lesson challenge that attitude? Commit to practicing one sunnah you have been neglecting this week, knowing that his every action is a model.
?
Ibrahim was made an imam after he passed tests. Consider the tests you face daily: your patience, honesty, and dedication. Do you live as an imam in your own household or community, conscious that others may imitate your actions? What one area of your character would you be ashamed to have others follow? Ask Allah to purify it starting today.
?
The verse says 'Indeed I will make you an imam for the people.' Allah appoints leaders. Do you truly believe that the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ is the perfect imam in every aspect of life, or do you subtly elevate other sources (culture, personal opinion) over his example? Resolve to consult the Sunnah before making any major decision this month.

The Fourteenth Proof: Covenant Excludes Wrongdoers
Al-Razi argues from Quran that God's covenant excludes wrongdoers, proving prophets sinless.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Razi uses the Qur'anic verse 'My covenant does not reach the wrongdoers' to prove that prophets are sinless.

Core Idea
Prophethood cannot be given to wrongdoers, so prophets must be sinless.

Imam al-Razi presents a logical proof for prophetic infallibility based on a clear Qur'anic statement. The verse declares that God's covenant does not reach wrongdoers. Al-Razi then shows that this covenant must refer either to prophethood or imamate, and in either case, it establishes that prophets cannot be wrongdoers—hence they are sinless.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and understand the premise
Start by reading the Qur'anic verse (2:124) and al-Razi's initial explanation that anyone who commits a sin is a wrongdoer to themselves.
The verse is the foundation of the entire argument.
2
Identify the two interpretations of 'covenant'
Al-Razi presents two possibilities: the covenant is either the covenant of prophethood or the covenant of imamate. Notice how he handles both.
This is a classic disjunction used in kalam.
3
Trace the logical conclusion
Follow the reasoning: if it is prophethood, directly they are sinless; if it is imamate, since imamate is lower, the same applies even more strongly to prophethood. Thus prophets cannot be wrongdoers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة عشر: قوله تعالى: ﴿لَا يَنَالُ عَهْدِي الظَّالِمِينَ﴾ [البقرة: ١٢٤] وكل من أقدم على الذنب كان ظالمًا لنفسه، لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَمِنْهُمْ ظَالِمٌ لِّنَفْسِهِ﴾ [فاطر: ٣٢] إذا عرفت هذا فنقول: ذلك العهد الذي حكم الله تعالى بأنه لا يصل إلى الظالمين إما أن يكون هو عهد النبوة، أو عهد الإمامة، فإن كان الأول فهو المقصود، وإن كان الثاني فالمقصود أظهر؛ لأن عهد الإمامة أقل درجة من عهد النبوة، وإذا لم يصل عهد الإمامة إلى الظالمين، فعهد النبوة أولى. وقد ثبت أن الأنبياء قد نالهم عهد النبوة، فوجب أن لا يكونوا ظالمين، أي لا يكونوا مذنبين.
The fourteenth proof: His saying – exalted be He: 'My covenant does not reach the wrongdoers' [Al-Baqarah 2:124]. And everyone who commits a sin is a wrongdoer to himself, because of His saying: 'Among them is a wrongdoer to himself' [Fatir 35:32]. When you understand this, we say: That covenant which Allah the Exalted has decreed does not reach the wrongdoers – either it is the covenant of prophethood, or the covenant of imamate. If it is the first, then it is the intended meaning; and if it is the second, then the intended meaning is even more apparent, because the covenant of imamate is of a lower degree than the covenant of prophethood. And if the covenant of imamate does not reach the wrongdoers, then the covenant of prophethood is even more so. And it is established that the prophets have received the covenant of prophethood, so it is necessary that they are not wrongdoers, that is, they are not sinners.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is a proof (hujja) for prophetic infallibility. Al-Razi cites the verse in which Allah says, 'My covenant does not reach the wrongdoers.' He explains that anyone who commits a sin is a wrongdoer to himself, as per another verse. The covenant in question is either the covenant of prophethood or the covenant of imamate. If it is the covenant of prophethood, then prophets, who receive that covenant, cannot be wrongdoers. If it is the covenant of imamate, since imamate is lower than prophethood, if imamate does not go to wrongdoers, then prophethood even more so. Since prophets have received the covenant of prophethood, they must not be wrongdoers, hence sinless.

Key Terms
عهد (covenant)
ظالم (wrongdoer)
النبوة (prophethood)
الإمامة (imamate)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The covenant in the verse only refers to imamate, not prophethood.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that even if it refers to imamate, it logically extends to prophethood because prophethood is higher, so the conclusion remains the same.

Checkpoint
In the fourteenth proof, if the covenant is interpreted as the covenant of imamate, what follows?
A) Prophets could still be wrongdoers since they are above imamate
B) The covenant of prophethood would also not reach wrongdoers
C) The verse only applies to imams
D) Prophets are not included in the verse

Key Takeaway
The Qur'anic verse 'My covenant does not reach the wrongdoers' proves that prophets, who received God's covenant, must be sinless.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's covenant is denied to wrongdoers, and you hope to be among those who receive His covenant, what sins are you still clinging to that might be blocking that covenant? Will you repent of them today, not just in word but in action?
?
Al-Razi argues that even the lower covenant of imamate is forbidden to wrongdoers. How does this challenge your casual attitude toward 'minor' sins? Do you truly believe that every sin distances you from God, or do you act as if some sins are too small to matter?
?
The prophets received God's covenant precisely because they were sinless. Do you desire closeness to God like that? What step will you take this week to uproot a specific sin from your life, so that you too may draw nearer to His covenant?

Four Scriptural Proofs for the Infallibility of Angels
Razi enumerates four scriptural proofs for the sinlessness of angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four scriptural proofs that Imam Razi presents for the infallibility of angels and the reasoning behind each proof.

Core Idea
Angels are infallible because Scripture describes them as perfectly obedient, tirelessly worshipping, honored servants, and messengers.

After establishing the infallibility of prophets, Imam Razi turns to the angels. In this passage, he compiles four clear proofs from the Quran that demonstrate the sinlessness of angels. Each proof uses a different attribute of angels to argue that they cannot commit sin.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the translation to grasp the flow of the four proofs.
The passage is dense but each proof is concise.
2
Identify the four proofs
Notice that Razi lists four distinct arguments. For each, note the verse cited and the reasoning he provides.
The proofs are numbered in the text.
3
Analyze the reasoning for each proof
For proof 1, see how 'doing what is commanded' includes avoiding prohibitions. For proof 2, constant worship precludes sin. For proof 3, honored servants do not rebel. For proof 4, messengers must be infallible by divine selection.
Each proof builds on a different Quranic description.
4
Examine the common misunderstanding
The fourth proof does not rely on every messenger being infallible by default, but on the office requiring infallibility as shown by the verse 'God knows best where to place His message'.
This clarifies that angelic messengers are chosen for their purity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنا لما فرغنا من ذكر الدلائل الدالة على عصمة الأنبياء - صلوات الله وسلامه عليهم - فلنذكر الآن ما يدل على عصمة الملائكة عليهم السلام - ويدل عليه وجوه : الحجة الأولى : قوله تعالى في صفة الملائكة : يَخَافُونَ رَبَّهُم مِّن فَوقِهِمْ وَيَفْعَلُونَ مَا يُؤْمَرُونَ [النحل : ٥٠] قوله: ﴿وَيَفْعَلُونَ مَا يُؤْمَرُونَ﴾ يتناول الملائكة في المأمورات، وترك جميع المنهيات؛ لأن كل ما نهى عن فعله، فقد أمر بتركه. الحجة الثانية : قوله : يُسَبِّحُونَ الَّيْلَ وَالنَّهَارَ لَا يَفْتُرُونَ ﴾ [الأنبياء : ٢٠] ومن صفته كذا لا يصدر عنه الذنب. الحجة الثالثة : قوله تعالى في صفة الملائكة : بل عباد مكرمون يَسْبِقُونَهُ بِالْقَوْلِ وَهُم بِأَمْرِهِ يَعْمَلُونَ [الأنبياء : ٢٧.٢٦]. الحجة الرابعة : الملائكة رسل الله، لقوله تعالى : وجَاعِلِ الْمَلَكَةِ رُسُلًا [فاطر: والرسول معصوم لقوله تعالى في تعظيم الرسول الله أَعلَمُ حَيْثُ يَجْعَلُ رِسالت : [الأنعام: ١٢٤] . فهذا مجموع الدلائل على عصمة الأنبياء والملائكة ـ عليهم السلام.
Know that when we have finished mentioning the proofs that indicate the infallibility of the prophets (peace and blessings of God be upon them), let us now mention what indicates the infallibility of the angels (peace be upon them). It is indicated by aspects: The first proof: His saying, exalted be He, describing the angels: 'They fear their Lord above them and do what they are commanded' [an-Nahl 16:50]. His saying 'and do what they are commanded' includes the angels in the commanded acts and the abandonment of all prohibitions, because everything that is forbidden to do has been commanded to abandon. The second proof: His saying: 'They glorify [Him] night and day, they do not slacken' [al-Anbiya 21:20]. One whose attribute is such cannot commit sin. The third proof: His saying, exalted be He, describing the angels: 'But they are honored servants. They do not precede Him in speech, and they act by His command' [al-Anbiya 21:26-27]. The fourth proof: The angels are messengers of God, by His saying, exalted be He: 'And making the angels messengers' [Fatir 35:1]. And the messenger is infallible by His saying, exalted be He, honoring the messenger: 'God knows best where to place His message' [al-An'am 6:124]. So this is the total of proofs for the infallibility of the prophets and angels (peace be upon them).
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage is a classification (taṣnīf) of four proofs (ḥujaj) for the infallibility (ʿiṣma) of angels. After concluding the proofs for prophetic infallibility, Imam Razi now turns to angels. Each proof is a scriptural argument: (1) The verse from Surah an-Nahl (16:50) states that angels fear their Lord and do what they are commanded. Razi explains that doing what is commanded includes leaving what is prohibited, because prohibition implies a command to abstain. (2) The verse from Surah al-Anbiya (21:20) describes angels as glorifying God tirelessly; such constant worship precludes sin. (3) Another verse from al-Anbiya (21:26-27) calls them 'honored servants' who do not precede God in speech but act by His command, showing submission and lack of rebellion. (4) Angels are messengers (rusul), and messengers are infallible, as indicated by the verse 'God knows best where to place His message' (6:124), which implies that God selects only sinless individuals for prophethood. The passage concludes by summarizing these as the total proofs for the infallibility of both prophets and angels.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the fourth proof is weak because the term 'messenger' can apply to fallen angels or that not every messenger is infallible.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the office of messenger requires infallibility, as God chooses only sinless individuals for prophethood (verse 6:124). Thus, angels as messengers are necessarily sinless.

Checkpoint
Which proof for angelic infallibility uses the fact that angels do not precede God in speech?
A) The first proof from Surah an-Nahl.
B) The second proof from Surah al-Anbiya.
C) The third proof from Surah al-Anbiya.
D) The fourth proof from Surah Fatir.

Key Takeaway
The infallibility of angels is proven by multiple Quranic verses describing their unwavering obedience, constant worship, servitude, and role as messengers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The angels never tire of glorifying Allah, yet your own worship often feels burdensome. What does this reveal about the state of your heart? Will you ask Allah tonight for a love that makes worship effortless?
?
Angels do exactly what they are commanded without hesitation. Is there a clear command of Allah that you are currently delaying or rationalizing away? What would it cost you to obey it right now, and what would it cost you not to?
?
The honored servants do not speak before Allah. How much of your daily speech is measured against His pleasure? Commit today to pause before speaking and ask: 'Is this fit for the presence of my Lord?'

First Objection: The Angels' Question (Ten Aspects)
Razi enumerates the ten aspects of the opponents' first doubt from the angels' story.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ten argumentative aspects the opponents use to challenge angelic infallibility based on the angels' question in Surah al-Baqarah.

Core Idea
The opponents argue that the angels' question exposes their sin in ten distinct ways.

Imam Razi begins by acknowledging that opponents have many objections against angelic infallibility. He selects the first major story—the angels' question to God—and enumerates ten specific angles from which they argue that the angels sinned. Each angle picks out a different dimension of the angels' words or actions, from objecting to God to concealing deeds. This passage lays out these arguments comprehensively; Razi's refutations will follow in subsequent lessons.

Guided Path
1
Read the overall structure
Identify that Razi introduces the story and then lists ten aspects. Notice the use of 'أحدها', 'ثانيها', etc.
The list is orderly; each aspect builds on the previous.
2
Examine aspects 1–5
Focus on the first five aspects: objection to God, backbiting, conjecture, self-admiration, and self-delusion. Note the Quranic verses cited for each.
These aspects focus on the angels' speech and attitude.
3
Examine aspects 6–10
Study aspects six through ten: lying, apology, doubting, concealing, and the Ibn Abbas narration. Observe how each points to a different sin.
These aspects highlight the angels' actions and omissions.
4
Reflect on the cumulative argument
Consider how these ten aspects together aim to undermine angelic infallibility by showing multiple faults.
The opponents use a cumulative case strategy.
5
Prepare for Razi's refutation
Recognize that this passage presents only the attack; the defense will follow in later lessons.
Do not mistake this for Razi's own position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن شبهات المخالفين في هذه المسألة كثيرة، ونحن نذكرها إن شاء الله تعالى على سبيل الاختصار : القصة الأولى : قصة الملائكة وللمخالفين فيها شبهات أربع : الشبهة الأولى : التمسك بقوله تعالى حكاية عنهم : أَتَجْعَلُ فِيهَا مَن يُفْسِدُ فِيهَا وَيَسْفِكُ الدِّمَاءَ [البَقَرَة : ٣٠] فقد احتجوا بها من عشرة أوجه: أحدها: أن قوله : أَتَجْعَلُ ؟ اعتراض والاعتراض على الله من أعظم الذنوب. وثانيها : أنهم طعنوا في بني آدم وهذا الطعن غيبة والغيبة من الذنوب وثالثها : حكمهم على البشر بالفساد والقتل، ولا يجوز أن يقال: إنهم عرفوا بالوحي ؛ لأنه تعالى لما أراد إعزاز آدم وأولاده فكيف يليق بذلك اطلاع الأعداء على الغيوب؟ فثبت أنهم قالوا ذلك عن الظن والحسبان، وذلك عظيم لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنَّ الظَّنَّ لَا يُغْنِي مِنَ الْحَقِّ شَالله [النجم: ۲۸] وقوله: ﴿وَلا تقف ما ليس لك به علوم [الإسراء : ٣٦] . ورابعها : أنهم لما طعنوا في بني آدم مدحوا أنفسهم فقالوا : ﴿وَنَحْنُ نُسَبِّحُ بِحَمْدِكَ وَنُقَدِّسُ لَكَ ﴾ [البَقَرَة : ٣٠] وقالوا : وَإِنَّا لَنَحْنُ الصَّافُونَ وَإِنَّا لَنَحْنُ الْمُسَبِّحُونَ [الصافات: ١٦٥ - ١٦٦] وهذا لفظ يدل على أنهم كانوا يقولون نحن الموصوفون بهذا التسبيح لا غيرنا وكل ذلك عجب والعجب من معظمات الذنوب، لقوله الله ثلاث مهلكات» إلى قوله : (وإعجاب المرء بنفسه». وخامسها : أنهم ذكروا عن أنفسهم الطاعة، وما ذكروا أن ذلك حصل بتوفيق الله تعالى وإعانته، وهذا غرور، وهو من الذنوب. وسادسها : أنه تعالى قال لهم : إِنْبِئُونِي بِأَسْمَاءِ هَٰؤُلَاءِ إِنْ كُنْتُمْ صَادِقِينَ [البقرة: ٣١] فهذا يدل على أنهم قد ذكروا كلاما وكانوا كاذبين فيه. وسابعها : قوله تعالى حكاية عنهم : قَالُوا سُبْحَانَكَ لَا عِلْمَ لَنَا إِلَّا مَا عَلَّمْتَنَا [البقرة: ٣٢] وهذا الكلام لا شك في أنه اعتذار، ولولا تقد الجرم وإلا لما احتاجوا إلى هذا الاعتذار. وثامنها : قوله تعالى للملائكة : ﴿قَالَ أَلَمْ أَقُلْ لَكُمْ إِنِّي أَعْلَمُ غَيْبَ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضِ﴾ [البقرة: الآية ٣٣] وهذا الكلام يدل على أنهم كانوا شاكين في كونه تعالى عالما بجميع المعلومات. وتاسعها : قوله تعالى: وَأَعْلَمُ مَا تُبْدُونَ وَمَا كُنْتُمْ تَكْتُمُونَ ﴾ [البَقَرَة : ٣٣] وهذا يدل على أنهم فعلوا فعلا كانوا يكتمونه، وذلك يقتضي كونه ذنبا إذ لو كان طاعة لما احتاجوا إلى كتمانه. وعاشرها يروى عن ابن عباس أنه قال: إن الله تعالى أمر إبليس مع عسكره
Know that the doubts of the opponents in this matter are many, and we will mention them, God willing, briefly: The first story: the story of the angels. The opponents have four doubts concerning it. The first doubt: clinging to His saying, exalted be He, narrating from them: 'Will You place therein one who will cause corruption therein and shed blood?' [al-Baqarah 2:30]. They have argued from it in ten aspects: The first: that His saying 'Will You place?' is an objection, and objecting to God is among the greatest sins. The second: that they disparaged the children of Adam, and this disparagement is backbiting, and backbiting is a sin. The third: their judgment upon humans of corruption and killing, and it is not permissible to say that they knew by revelation, because when He intended to honor Adam and his children, how would it befit that to inform enemies of the unseen? So it is established that they said that by conjecture and assumption, and that is grave, by His saying: 'And indeed conjecture does not avail against the truth at all' [an-Najm 53:28] and His saying: 'And do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge' [al-Isra 17:36]. The fourth: that when they disparaged the children of Adam, they praised themselves, saying: 'And we glorify You with praise and sanctify You' [al-Baqarah 2:30] and they said: 'Indeed we are the ones who line up in rows, and indeed we are the ones who glorify' [as-Saffat 37:165-166]. This wording indicates that they were saying 'we are the ones described with this glorification, not others', and all that is self-admiration, and self-admiration is among the major sins, by the saying of the Prophet: 'three destroyers...' up to his saying: 'and a person's self-admiration'. The fifth: that they mentioned obedience from themselves, and did not mention that that came about by the success and help of God, and this is self-delusion, and it is a sin. The sixth: that He, exalted be He, said to them: 'Inform Me of the names of these if you are truthful' [al-Baqarah 2:31]. This indicates that they had uttered something and were lying in it. The seventh: His saying, exalted be He, narrating from them: 'They said: Exalted are You; we have no knowledge except what You have taught us' [al-Baqarah 2:32]. This speech is undoubtedly an apology, and had sin not been committed, they would not have needed this apology. The eighth: His saying, exalted be He, to the angels: 'He said: Did I not tell you that I know the unseen of the heavens and the earth?' [al-Baqarah 2:33]. This speech indicates that they were doubting that He, exalted be He, is knowledgeable of all known things. The ninth: His saying, exalted be He: 'And I know what you reveal and what you have concealed' [al-Baqarah 2:33]. This indicates that they did an act which they were concealing, and that necessitates it being a sin, for if it were an act of obedience, they would not have needed to conceal it. And the tenth: It is narrated from Ibn Abbas that he said: 'Indeed God commanded Iblis with his army...'
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage presents the first doubt (shubha) of the opponents against the infallibility of angels, based on the story of the angels' question to God in Surah al-Baqarah (2:30). Imam Razi notes that opponents have four doubts regarding this story, and the first doubt is their clinging to the verse where the angels ask: 'Will You place therein one who will cause corruption and shed blood?' The opponents argue from this verse in ten aspects (wujūh). Each aspect is a distinct angle of argument: (1) The question itself is an objection (iʿtirāḍ) to God, which is a major sin. (2) The angels disparaged humans (backbiting). (3) Their judgment was based on conjecture (ẓann), which is condemned in the Quran (53:28; 17:36). (4) They praised themselves after disparaging others, which is self-admiration (ʿujb), and self-admiration is a major sin, as per the hadith of 'three destroyers'. (5) They attributed their obedience to themselves without acknowledging God's help, which is self-delusion (ghurūr). (6) When God asked them to inform Him of the names, it showed they were lying. (7) Their response 'Exalted are You; we have no knowledge' is an apology, implying prior sin. (8) God's reply 'Did I not tell you...' indicates they doubted His knowledge. (9) God's statement 'I know what you conceal' implies they hid an act, which would be a sin if it were good. (10) A narration from Ibn Abbas that God commanded Iblis and his army—suggesting further wrongdoing, though the text cuts off. The passage is presenting the opponents' arguments; it does not yet include Razi's refutation.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself objecting inwardly to a difficulty God placed in your life, even if you didn't voice it? How does the first aspect (objection as a major sin) force you to reconsider that quiet rebellion? What will you do the next time such a thought arises?
?
When you do something good, do you ever catch yourself feeling proud, thinking 'I did this'? The angels were faulted for not attributing their obedience to God's help (aspect 5). In your next good deed, how will you consciously redirect that praise back to God?
?
Is there a sin you are hiding from others right now, thinking it's safe because no one else knows? Aspect 9 reminds you that God knows what you conceal and that hiding a sin only adds to its gravity. Are you willing to bring that darkness into the light of repentance today?

Defining al-Hamm and Interpreting Yusuf's Intention
Imam Razi defines hamm as 'azm and gives two interpretations of Yusuf's hamm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Razi's definition of al-hamm as 'azm and how he defends Yusuf's integrity through two interpretations of his hamm.

Core Idea
The term 'hamm' in the Qur'an does not automatically imply sinful intent.

Imam Razi in his theological work defines key terms precisely before applying them to Quranic verses. This passage tackles a sensitive verse about Prophet Yusuf, where the word 'hamm' appears. Razi establishes that 'hamm' means determination, and then argues that Yusuf's hamm could not have been toward sin, offering two clever interpretations that uphold his prophetic virtue.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of hamm
Start by reading the passage where Razi defines 'hamm' as 'azm (determination). Notice that he immediately notes determination cannot attach to an essence but only to an action, and the action is unspecified in the verse.
This sets up the ambiguity that requires interpretation.
2
Explore the first interpretation
The first interpretation says Yusuf intended to push Zulaykha away. Razi addresses why a divine proof would be needed for a praiseworthy act, explaining that the proof showed harmful consequences like death or false accusation.
This interpretation shifts the meaning of hamm from sin to self-defense.
3
Examine the second interpretation
The second interpretation involves grammatical fronting and delaying (taqdim wa ta'khir). Razi refutes Az-Zajjaj's objections with Quranic evidence and logical preference.
Note how Razi uses grammar to resolve theological concerns.
4
Reflect on the benefit
Finally, consider why the verse mentions hamm at all if no sin occurred. Razi says it shows Yusuf's restraint despite strong desire, emphasizing piety.
This demonstrates a positive motive for the verse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا ثبت هذا فنقول : الهم هو العزم، ولا يمكن تعلق العزم بذاتها ؛ لأن الذوات حال بقائها لا تتعلق الإرادات بها، بل لا بد من تعلق العزم بإحداث فعل في الذات، وذلك الفعل غير مذكور، فليس القول بأن المراد هو الهم بالزنى أولى من القول بأن المراد هو الهم بفعل آخر. ولنا فيه وجهان : الأول: أن يحمل على أنه هم بأن يدفعها عن نفسه. ولا يقال: فأي فائدة على هذا التأويل في قوله تعالى : ﴿لَوْلَا أَن رَّآ بُرْهَانَ رَبِّهِ﴾ [يوسف: 24] فإن دفعها عن النفس واجب والبرهان لا يصرف عنه لأنا نقول : يجوز أن يكون لما أراه الله برهانا على أنه لو أقدم على ما هم به لأهلكه أهلها وقتلوه أو أنها تدعي عليه المراودة على القبيح، وتنسبه إلى أنه دعاها إلى نفسه وضربها لأجل امتناعها منه فأخبر الله تعالى أنه صرف بالبرهان السوء عنه والفحشاء، وهو القتل والمكروه أو ظن القبيح واعتقاده فيه. والثاني: أن يحمل هذا الكلام على التقدم والتأخر ﴿وَلَقَدْ هَمَّتْ بِهِ وَلَوْلَا أَن رَّأَى بُرْهَانَ رَبِّهِ لَهَمَّ بِهَا﴾ وهذا يجري مجرى قولهم : قد كنت هلكت لولا أن تداركتك، واستبعد الزجاج هذا الجواب من وجهين : أحدهما : أنه لا يجوز تقديم جواب لولا والثاني: أن جوابه يكون باللام كقوله: ﴿فَلَوْلَا أَنَّهُ كَانَ مِنَ الْمُسَبِّحِينَ لَلَبِثَ فِي بَطْنِهِ إِلَى يَوْمِ يُبْعَثُونَ﴾ [الصافات: 143-144]. والجواب : لا نسلم أنه لا يجوز التقديم، والدليل عليه قوله تعالى: ﴿إِن كَادَتْ لَتُبْدِي بِهِ لَوْلَا أَن رَّبَطْنَا عَلَى قَلْبِهَا﴾ [القصص: 10] وأيضًا فلو لم يجعل المقدم على لولا جوابها لكان جوابها محذوفًا، وإذا وقع التعارض بين أن يكون جوابها محذوفا وبين أن يكون مقدما عليها فلا شك أن التقديم أولى، لا يقال: فأي فائدة في قوله : ﴿وَهَمَّ بِهَا لَوْلَا أَن رَّآ بُرْهَانَ رَبِّهِ﴾ [يوسف: 24] إذا لم يحصل هم ؟ لأنا نقول : الفائدة فيه الإخبار عن أن ترك الهم لم يكن لعدم حصول الرغبة في النساء لكنه ترك ذلك مع الرغبة، انقياداً لأمر الله تعالى وطلبا لثوابه.
When this is established, we say: al-hamm is 'azm (determination). Determination cannot be attached to the essence itself because essences, as long as they remain, do not have acts of will attached to them. Rather, determination must be attached to the occurrence of an action in the essence. That action is not mentioned, so the statement that what is meant is the intention to commit adultery is not more likely than the statement that what is meant is the intention to do another action. We have two interpretations for this: First: it is interpreted that he intended to push her away from himself. It is not said: what benefit is there in this interpretation of His saying: 'If it were not that he saw the proof of his Lord'? For pushing her away from oneself is obligatory, and proof does not turn away from it. For we say: it is possible that when Allah showed him a proof that if he proceeded with what he intended, her family would destroy him and kill him, or that she would claim that he made advances toward her in an ugly manner and attribute to him that he called her to himself and struck her because of her refusal. So Allah informed that He turned away evil and immorality from him through the proof, which is death and harm or the assumption and belief of evil about him. Second: this phrase is interpreted as fronting and delaying: 'And certainly she intended him, and if it were not that he saw the proof of his Lord, he would have intended her.' This is like the saying: 'I would have perished if you had not rescued me.' Az-Zajjaj rejected this answer from two aspects: one, that it is not permissible to front the answer of 'lawla'; two, that its answer comes with 'lam' like His saying: 'And if it were not that he was of those who exalt Allah, he would have remained in its belly until the Day they are resurrected.' The response: we do not concede that fronting is not permissible. The evidence for it is His saying: 'She almost disclosed it, if it were not that We bound her heart.' Also, if what is fronted before 'lawla' is not its answer, then its answer would be omitted. When there is a conflict between omitting the answer and fronting it, there is no doubt that fronting is preferable. It is not said: what benefit is there in His saying: 'And he intended her if it were not that he saw the proof of his Lord' if there was no intention? For we say: the benefit in it is the information that the abandonment of the intention was not due to the lack of desire for women, but he abandoned it despite desire, out of submission to Allah's command and seeking His reward.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is a definition and a detailed exegetical argument. Imam Razi first defines 'al-hamm' as 'azm (determination). He notes that determination cannot be directed at a person's essence itself; rather, it must be directed at an action. In the verse about Yusuf, the specific action is not mentioned. Therefore, it is not more likely that the intention was adultery than some other action. Razi then provides two interpretations. The first interpretation: Yusuf intended to push Zulaykha away. Razi anticipates an objection: why would a divine proof be needed to deter him from a praiseworthy action? He answers that the proof showed the harmful consequences—either death at her family's hands or her false accusation. So the proof turned away both the external harm and the moral harm of false suspicion. The second interpretation involves grammatical fronting and delaying: the verse is read as 'She intended him, and if he had not seen the proof, he would have intended her.' This is like a conditional with fronted answer. Az-Zajjaj objected that fronting the answer of 'lawla' is not allowed and that the answer must have 'lam'. Razi refutes by citing a Qur'anic example where the answer is fronted (Surah Qasas, 10). He argues that fronting is preferable to omitting the answer. Finally, he addresses the question: if there was no intention, what is the benefit of the verse? He answers that the benefit is to show that Yusuf's restraint was despite strong desire, out of obedience to Allah.

Key Terms
hamm
'azm
lawla
taqdim wa ta'khir
burhan

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Yusuf intended to commit sin (adultery) with Zulaykha.
Correction: Razi shows that 'hamm' is ambiguous and can refer to a praiseworthy intention like pushing her away, or it can be interpreted grammatically to mean 'would have intended' without actual occurrence.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Razi, what is the definition of 'al-hamm'?
A) A passing thought
B) Determination ('azm)
C) A sinful desire
D) An emotional impulse

Key Takeaway
Razi's careful definition of hamm and use of grammatical analysis defends Yusuf's innocence and highlights that Qur'anic ambiguity can be resolved through sound reasoning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you been in a situation where your intention was misunderstood? How does Yusuf's example of restraint despite desire challenge you to examine your own hidden intentions instead of defending yourself?
?
Razi shows that even a prophet's 'hamm' can be interpreted positively. What does this teach you about the importance of giving others the benefit of the doubt when their motives are unclear—especially those you are quick to judge?
?
Yusuf's abandonment of the intention was not due to lack of desire but out of obedience. Is your obedience to Allah a result of a lack of desire for sin, or is it a conscious submission despite desire? Which is more praiseworthy, and what would it take for you to reach that level?

Objection and Answer on Khidr's Killing of the Boy
Razi presents an objection and answer regarding Khidr's killing of the boy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection against Khidr's killing of the boy and the answer that it was based on a direct divine command.

Core Idea
Fear alone never justifies killing; only a divine command can.

This lesson examines a theological objection to the story of al-Khidr in Surah al-Kahf. The objector questions how a prophet could kill a boy out of mere fear that he would cause trouble. Razi presents the objection and a clear answer that the act was based on a direct command from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the structure of objection and answer come through.
Notice that the objection is introduced as a question.
2
Identify the objection
Find the part that states the problem: Khidr feared the boy would cause his parents trouble, but fear does not provide knowledge or even presumption. Why then is killing allowed?
3
Understand why fear is insufficient
Reflect on the argument: fear (خشية) is a feeling, not a source of certainty. For a serious act like killing, one would need knowledge or at least strong presumption. The objector says fear lacks both.
This highlights a principle in Islamic ethics: actions require sufficient epistemic justification.
4
See the answer: divine command
Razi's answer is concise: 'Perhaps Allah commanded him to kill the person, so he killed him.' This shows that Khidr did not act on his own reasoning but on explicit divine instruction.
5
Reflect on the lesson for prophethood
Consider what this tells us about prophets: they are infallible because they act only on Allah's command, not personal judgment. The objection is resolved by appealing to divine authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثانية والثلاثون وأما السؤال على ملام الخضر الله فهو أنه قال: فَخَشِينَا أَن يُرْهِقَهُمَا طعينا وكفرا له [الكهف: ۸٠] وكيف استباح دم الغلام لأجل الخشية مع أن الخشية لا تفيد علمًا ولا ظنا ؟ والجواب : لعل الله أمره بقتل الشخص، فلذلك قتله.
The thirty-second question: As for the question regarding the blame of al-Khidr, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, it is that he said: 'So we feared that he would overwhelm them with transgression and disbelief' [al-Kahf:80]. And how is it permissible to shed the boy's blood because of fear, when fear does not yield knowledge or even presumption? The answer: Perhaps Allah commanded him to kill the person, so he killed him.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer concerning the story of al-Khidr in Surah al-Kahf. The objector questions how al-Khidr could kill the boy based on mere fear that the boy would cause his parents trouble, since fear does not provide certain knowledge or even strong presumption, which would normally be required for such a serious act. The answer is that al-Khidr did not act on his own reasoning; rather, Allah commanded him to kill that specific person, so his act was obedience to a divine command, not a decision based on fear.

Key Terms
الخضر
الخشية
دم الغلام
الجواب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Khidr's fear alone was sufficient justification for killing the boy.
Correction: The passage clarifies that fear does not provide knowledge or even presumption; the true justification was a direct divine command.

Checkpoint
What is the basis of the objection against Khidr in this passage?
A) He killed the boy without permission from his parents
B) He acted out of fear, which provides no certainty or even strong presumption
C) He disobeyed the command of Musa
D) He acted ignorantly

Key Takeaway
Khidr's killing of the boy was justified only by a direct command from Allah, not by fear or personal reasoning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever used fear as a justification for a harsh decision toward someone? How does Khidr's story challenge your reliance on fear alone?
?
If Allah commanded you to do something that seemed unfair or difficult, would your obedience be immediate or reluctant? What does that reveal about your tawakkul?
?
The objector in this passage insists that fear does not yield knowledge. Where in your life have you acted on fear rather than certainty? How can you seek divine guidance to replace fear with faith?

First Interpretation: A Fabricated Dispute by Enemies
Razi presents the first of many interpretations: the men were enemies who fabricated a dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the people of verification interpreted the story of Dawud's litigants as a ruse by enemies rather than a real case, thereby preserving prophetic infallibility.

Core Idea
The 'litigants' were assassins who faked a dispute when their plot failed.

Imam Razi begins his theological defense of Dawud's prophethood by presenting a series of interpretations from the people of verification. The first interpretation reframes the entire episode as a conspiracy by enemies who intended to kill Dawud. When discovered, they invented a false dispute to cover their real intentions. This lesson unpacks that interpretation and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the interpretation explains the context behind the verse.
The Arabic uses 'tassawaru' (they climbed over) which sets the scene of intrusion.
2
Identify the key elements of the interpretation
Find: who climbed, their real intention, Dawud's reaction, their fear, and the fabricated story.
The fabrication is the dispute they present to Dawud.
3
Reflect on the theological purpose
Consider why this interpretation protects Dawud from any sin or wrongdoing. What does it say about prophetic infallibility?
This interpretation removes any possibility of Dawud making a wrong judgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن أهل التحقيق ذكروا وجوها كثيرة في تأويل الآية : الأول : أن قوله تعالى: ﴿وَهَلْ أَتَنَكَ نَبَؤُا الْخَصْمِ إِذْ تَوَرُوا الْمِحْرَابَ [ص: ٢١] حكاية عن جماعة تسوروا قصره قاصدين قتله والإساءة إليه في أهله وماله، تسوروا قصره في وقت ظنوا أنه غافل، فلما رآهم داود اخافهم لما تقرر في أحد دار غيره من غير أمره إلا لقصد السوء من قتل النفس أو سرقة المال وخصوصًا إذا كان صاحب الدار شخصا معظمًا ، فلما رأوه مستيقظًا انتقض عليهم تدبيرهم وخافوا فاخترع بعضهم عند ذلك الخوف خصومة لا أصل لها، وزعم أنهم إنما قصدوه لأجلها دون ما توهمه فقالوا : خَصْمَانِ بَغَى بَعْضُنَا عَلَى بعض [ص: ٢٢]
Then the people of verification mentioned many aspects in the interpretation of the verse. The first: That His saying, exalted: 'Has there come to you the news of the litigants when they climbed over the wall of the sanctuary?' [Sad:21] is a narration about a group who climbed over his palace intending to kill him and harm him in his family and wealth. They climbed over his palace at a time they thought he was heedless. When Dawud saw them, he feared them, because it is established that no one enters the house of another without permission except for an evil purpose, such as killing a soul or stealing property, especially if the owner is a great person. When they saw him alert, their plan was thwarted and they became afraid. One of them, in that fear, invented a dispute with no basis, claiming that they had come to him because of it, not for what he had supposed. So they said: 'Two disputants, one of us has transgressed against the other' [Sad:22].
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage presents the first of many interpretations offered by the people of verification (ahl al-tahqiq) to reconcile the story without attributing sin to Dawud. The interpretation explains that the two 'litigants' were actually a group of conspirators who climbed the wall of Dawud's sanctuary with intent to kill him and harm his family and property. They chose a time when they thought he was unaware. When Dawud saw them, he became frightened, as it is generally understood that entering someone's home without permission is only for evil purposes like murder or theft, especially when the homeowner is a person of high status. Seeing that Dawud was alert, their plan failed and they grew scared. In that fear, one of them fabricated a story about a dispute between two litigants to cover up their real intentions. They claimed they had come to seek his judgment on a quarrel, not to harm him. Thus the story that follows is a ruse, not a real case, and Dawud's subsequent judgment does not reflect any sin on his part but rather shows his justice in a hypothetical scenario.

Key Terms
أهل التحقيق
الخصم
تسوروا
المحراب
الخصومة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might take the story at face value and conclude that Dawud erred or sinned.
Correction: This interpretation shows that the entire episode was a deception by enemies, not a real judicial case, so Dawud's judgment was not about a real dispute and thus no error occurred.

Checkpoint
According to the first interpretation, why did the men climb over the wall of the sanctuary?
A) To seek judgment on a genuine dispute
B) To kill Dawud and harm his family and property
C) To test Dawud's knowledge
D) To return a lost item

Key Takeaway
The first interpretation shows that the litigants were enemies whose false story was a cover for attempted murder, thus removing any hint of sin from Dawud.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about the prophets in the Quran, do you ever find yourself quick to assume the worst about their actions, forgetting that Allah defends them? How can you train yourself to think charitably (husn al-zann) about the prophets when you encounter ambiguous stories?
?
This passage explains that the enemies invented a lie when their plot failed. Have you ever been in a situation where you were caught in wrongdoing and tried to cover it up with a story? How does this reminder of Dawud's example—fearing Allah even in a testing moment—challenge you to be truthful even when exposed?
?
The interpretation says that entering someone's home without permission is only for evil purposes. In your own life, do you respect the privacy and sanctity of others' homes and personal spaces, or do you sometimes rationalize intrusive behavior? What would it take for you to fully internalize the gravity of violating someone's sanctuary?
