Razi's Refutation of the Popular Story of Dawud
Razi enumerates two deviations in the popular story and then the three apparent proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Razi considers the popular story of Dawud to require deviation from the apparent meaning of the Quran and how he identifies three elements that might otherwise imply sin.

Core Idea
The popular story forces lies onto angels and metaphorical reinterpretation, violating Quranic apparent meaning.

Razi begins by contrasting his interpretation with the widely circulated story about Dawud. He argues that the popular narrative forces two serious deviations from the apparent meaning: attributing falsehood to angels and reinterpreting 'ewes' as women. He then identifies three verses that seem to support the story but argues that they do not necessarily prove sin.

Guided Path
1
Read Razi's opening statement
Read the Arabic passage from 'المسألة الثانية والثلاثون' down to 'إلا ثلاث'. Notice how Razi sets up the contrast between apparent meaning and the famous story.
The passage introduces the two critiques.
2
Understand the two deviations
Focus on Razi's two arguments: the angels would be lying, and interpreting 'ewes' as women is a deviation. List each in your own words.
The first deviation involves a direct lie; the second involves metaphorical interpretation.
3
Identify the three potential proofs
Razi lists three elements from the verses that could suggest sin: 'ظن داود', 'استغفار', and 'غفران'. Write them down and note why each might be problematic.
These are the main points that opponents use to claim sin.
4
Reflect on Razi's claim
Razi asserts that none of the three elements indicate sin. Consider how he will argue this in the next lesson.
This sets up the need for interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثانية والثلاثون
واعلم أن حمل الآية على ما ذكرناه حمل الكلام على ظاهره، أما حملها على القصة المشهورة فإنه يقتضي العدول عن الظاهر من وجهين:
الأول: أن الملائكة لما قالوا خَصْمَانِ بَغَى بَعْضُنَا عَلَى بَعْضٍ [ص: ٢٢] كان هذا كذبًا؛ لأنه لم يبغ أحد من الملائكة على الآخر، وإسناد الكذب إلى اللصوص أولى من إسناده إلى الملائكة.
الثاني: قوله: إِنَّ هَذَا أَخِي لَم يَسْعُ وَتَسْعُونَ نَعْجَةً وَلِي نَعْجَةٌ وَاحِدَةٌ [ص: ٢٣] هذا أيضًا كذب، والقوم يحملون النعاج على النسوان وهو عدول عن الظاهر، وأما على قولنا فقد نسبنا هذا الكذب إلى اللصوص، وهو أولى من نسبته إلى الملائكة.
وبالجملة: فليس في الآية لفظ يشهد بصحة ما ذكره من القصة إلا ثلاث:
أحدها: قوله: ﴿وَظَنَّ دَاوُدُ أَنَّمَا فَتَنَّهُ﴾ [ص: ٢٤] وذلك لأن لفظ الفتنة يوهم.
وثانيها: قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاسْتَغْفَرَ رَبَّهُ﴾ [ص: ٢٤] وذلك يوهم صدور الذنب منه.
وثالثها: قوله: ﴿فَغَفَرْنَا لَهُ ذَلِكَ﴾ [ص: ٢٥]
واعلم أن شيئًا من ذلك لا يدل على أقوالهم.
ويدل عليه وجوه:
الوجه الأول: أما قوله: ﴿وَظَنَّ دَاوُدُ أَنَّمَا فَتَنَّهُ﴾ فالمعنى: امتحناه واختبرناه، فإنه لما أساء الظن بهم، فهل يعاجلهم بالعقوبة أم لا؟ ثم إنه لكمال سلطته وقوة مملكته لم يعاجلهم بالعقوبة، ولم ينتقم منهم، ولم يضربهم، فكان ذلك سببًا لازدياد منصبه في الحكم والدين.
وأما قوله: ﴿فَاسْتَغْفَرَ رَبَّهُ﴾ فليس في الآية أن ذلك الاستغفار لنفسه أو لغيره، ألا ترى أنه تعالى حكى عن الملائكة بأنهم يستغفرون للذين آمنوا؟ وقال أولاد يعقوب: ﴿يَا أَبَانَا اسْتَغْفِرْ لَنَا ذُنُوبَنَا﴾ [يوسف: ٩٧]، قال تعالى لمحمد: ﴿وَاسْتَغْفِرْ لِذَنْبِكَ وَلِلْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَالْمُؤْمِنَاتِ﴾ [محمد: ١٩]، وإذا كان ذلك كذلك احتمل أن يكون المراد أن القوم لما أقدموا على ذلك الفعل المنكر لم يعاجلهم داود بالعقوبة، بل أظهر الحلم، وزاد على ذلك طلبه من الله تعالى أن يعفو عنهم وأن يغفر لهم.
وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿فَغَفَرْنَا لَهُ ذَلِكَ﴾ فيحتمل أن يكون المراد: فغفرنا لأجل حرمته، ولبركة شفاعته ذلك الفعل المنكر الذي أتى به أولئك المتسورون، وهذا التأويل الذي ذكرناه ينطبق عليه القرآن ولا نحتاج فيه إلى إسناد الكذب إلى الملائكة وحمل النعاج على النسوان، ثم إنه يليق به أن يذكر عقيب قوله: ﴿إِنَّا جَعَلْنَاكَ خَلِيفَةً فِي الْأَرْضِ﴾ [ص: ٢٦] فمن بلغت رحمته وشفقته على الرعية إلى هذا الحد كان اللائق برحمته أرحم الراحمين تفويض خلافة الأرض إليه، ويليق به أن يأمر محمدًا ﷺ عند تأذيه من قومه بأن يقتدي به، وهو قوله في أول الآية: ﴿اصْبِرْ عَلَى مَا يَقُولُونَ وَاذْكُرْ عَبْدَنَا دَاوُدَ ذَا الْأَيْدِ﴾ [ص: ١٧]، ومن طلب الحق وأنصف علم أن ما ذكرناه هو الحق الصريح.
الوجه الثاني: لعل الاستغفار إنما كان لأن القوم لما تسوروا داره ظن بهم أنهم يقصدون قتله ثم إنه لما لم تظهر الأمارات الدالة على أن ذلك الظن حق ندم على ذلك الظن، فكان الاستغفار بسببه.
الوجه الثالث: أنه لما هضم نفسه ولم يؤذهم ولم ينتقم منهم مع القدرة التامة دخله شيء من العجب بسبب كمال حلمه فكان الاستغفار منه لأن العجب من المهلكات.
فهذا قول من يقول: لا دلالة في الآية على إثباته بشيء من الزلات، وهو الحق عندي.
وأما من سلم دلالة الآية على الصغيرة فلهم فيه وجوه:
أحدها: أنه كان عالمًا بحسن امرأة أوريا، فلما سمع أنه قتل قَلَ غمه لميل نفسه إلى نكاح زوجته، فعوتب عليه.
وثانيها: أن أهل زمان داود كان يسأل بعضهم بعضًا أن ينزل له عن امرأته ليتزوج بها إذا أعجبته، وكان ذلك جائزًا فيما بينهم، واتفق أن عين داود وقعت على امرأة أوريا فأحبها، فسأله النزول عنها، فاستحيى أن يرده ففعل، فتزوجها، وأم سليمان فقيل له: إنك مع ارتفاع قدرك وكثرة نسائك ما كان يليق بك أن تسأل رجلاً ليس له إلا امرأة واحدة أن ينزل عنها، بل كان الواجب عليك قهر النفس.
The thirty-second issue. Know that interpreting the verse as we have done is taking the speech according to its apparent meaning. As for interpreting it according to the famous story, it requires deviation from the apparent meaning in two respects: First, when the angels said 'Two adversaries, some of us transgressed against others' (Surah Sad 22), this would be a lie, because no angel transgressed against another, and attributing the lie to the thieves is more fitting than attributing it to the angels. Second, His saying 'Indeed this brother of mine has ninety-nine ewes, and I have one ewe' (Surah Sad 23) is also a lie, and they interpret the ewes as women, which is a deviation from the apparent meaning. As for our view, we have attributed this lie to the thieves, which is more fitting than attributing it to the angels. In summary, there is nothing in the verse that testifies to the correctness of the story they mentioned except three things: One: His saying 'And Dawud thought that We had tested him' (Surah Sad 24), because the word 'fitnah' suggests [something]. Second: His saying 'So he sought forgiveness from his Lord' (Surah Sad 24), which suggests the occurrence of sin from him. Third: His saying 'And We forgave him that' (Surah Sad 25). Know that none of this indicates what they claim. There are proofs for our view: First proof: As for His saying 'And Dawud thought that We had tested him', the meaning is that We tested and tried him, for when he thought badly of them, would he hasten to punish them or not? Then, due to the perfection of his authority and the strength of his kingdom, he did not hasten to punish them, nor did he take revenge from them, nor did he strike them, and that became a reason for the increase of his rank in judgment and religion. As for His saying 'So he sought forgiveness from his Lord', it is not in the verse that this seeking forgiveness was for himself or for others. Do you not see that Allah Almighty related about the angels that they seek forgiveness for those who believe? And the sons of Jacob said 'O our father, seek forgiveness for us for our sins' (Surah Yusuf 97). Allah said to Muhammad: 'And seek forgiveness for your sin and for the believing men and believing women' (Surah Muhammad 19). If that is the case, then it is possible that the meaning is that when the people committed that reprehensible act, Dawud did not hasten to punish them, but rather showed forbearance, and in addition he asked Allah to pardon them and forgive them. As for His saying 'So We forgave him that', it is possible that the meaning is: We forgave, on account of his sanctity and the blessing of his intercession, that reprehensible act which those trespassers committed. This interpretation we have mentioned conforms to the Quran, and we do not need therein to attribute lies to the angels or to interpret ewes as women. Moreover, it is fitting that it be mentioned after His saying 'Indeed We have made you a vicegerent on earth' (Surah Sad 26). For one whose mercy and compassion for subjects reaches this extent, it is befitting for the Most Merciful of the merciful to entrust to him the vicegerency of the earth. And it is fitting that He command Muhammad, when he is harmed by his people, to follow his example, which is His saying at the beginning of the verse: 'Be patient over what they say and remember Our servant Dawud, the possessor of strength' (Surah Sad 17). Whoever seeks the truth and is fair knows that what we have mentioned is the manifest truth. Second proof: Perhaps the seeking forgiveness was because when the people scaled his wall, he thought that they intended to kill him. Then, when the signs did not appear indicating that that thought was correct, he regretted that thought, and so the seeking forgiveness was due to it. Third proof: When he humbled himself and did not harm them nor take revenge from them despite complete ability, some self-admiration entered him due to the perfection of his forbearance, so he sought forgiveness, because self-admiration is among the destructive things. This is the view of one who says: There is no indication in the verse of proving any lapses for him, and it is the truth in my view. As for one who concedes that the verse indicates a minor sin, they have several interpretations: One: He was aware of the beauty of the wife of Uriah, and when he heard that he was killed, his grief diminished due to his inclination to marry his wife, so he was reproached for that. Second: The people of Dawud's time used to ask one another to give up his wife for him to marry her if he admired her, and that was permissible among them. It happened that Dawud's eye fell on the wife of Uriah, so he loved her, and he asked him to give her up. Uriah was too shy to refuse him, so he did it, and Dawud married her, and she was the mother of Solomon. So it was said to him: 'With your high status and many wives, it is not befitting for you to ask a man who has only one wife to give her up; rather, you should have subdued your soul.'
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument defending the sinlessness of the prophet Dawud (David) against interpretations that suggest he committed a sin based on the verses of Surah Sad. Razi begins by stating that his own interpretation adheres to the apparent meaning of the Quran, while the popular story (al-qissah al-mashhurah) requires deviation from the apparent meaning in two ways. First, if the angels were the speakers when they said 'Two adversaries, some of us transgressed against others' (38:22), that would be a lie because angels do not transgress against each other. Razi points out that attributing a lie to the thieves (al-lusus) who trespassed is more fitting than attributing it to angels. Second, if the verse 'This brother of mine has ninety-nine ewes' (38:23) is taken literally as a claim by the angels, it would also be a lie, and interpreting 'ewes' as women is a deviation from the apparent meaning. Razi argues that those who accept the popular story must commit these deviations, whereas his view avoids them by attributing the lie to the trespassers. He then identifies three elements in the verses that might seem to imply sin: the word 'fitnah' (trial) in 'Dawud thought that We had tested him' (38:24), his seeking forgiveness (38:24), and Allah's forgiveness (38:25). Razi argues that none of these necessarily indicate sin. He offers three detailed interpretations (wujuh) to show how these verses can be understood without implying sin. In the first interpretation, he explains that 'fitnah' means Allah tested Dawud's forbearance: when Dawud thought badly of the trespassers, he had the power to punish them immediately but instead showed restraint, which increased his rank. As for seeking forgiveness, Razi argues that the Quranic context shows that prophets can seek forgiveness for others (e.g., angels for believers, Jacob for his sons, Muhammad for all believers). Therefore, Dawud's plea could have been for the trespassers, not for himself. Similarly, Allah's forgiveness could mean He forgave the trespassers due to Dawud's intercession. Razi emphasizes that this interpretation fits the Quranic style and avoids the need to attribute lies to angels or interpret ewes metaphorically as women. He also connects this to the following verse (38:26) about vicegerency, showing that Dawud's mercy qualifies him for such a role, and to the earlier command to Muhammad to be patient, implying that Dawud's example is one of patience and mercy. The second interpretation suggests that Dawud's seeking forgiveness was due to regretting his initial suspicion that the trespassers intended to kill him. The third interpretation suggests that Dawud experienced a moment of self-admiration for his forbearance, which is a destructive quality, so he sought forgiveness for that. Razi concludes that the verses contain no proof of any lapse (zallat) for Dawud, and this is the truth in his view. He then reports two alternative views held by those who concede that the verses indicate a minor sin (saghirah): one involving Dawud's desire to marry Uriah's wife after Uriah's death, and another involving a customary practice in Dawud's time where men could request a wife from another man, and Dawud was reproached for not controlling his desire despite his high status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the popular story about Dawud is the correct interpretation of Surah Sad.
Correction: Razi shows that the story forces two deviations from the apparent meaning: attributing lies to angels and interpreting 'ewes' as women, which is unnecessary if the story is rejected.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, how many respects does the famous story require deviation from the apparent meaning?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
Razi rejects the famous story because it forces deviations from the apparent meaning by attributing lies to angels and requiring metaphorical reinterpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When a popular story about a prophet contradicts Allah's revelation, do you have the courage to reject it, even if it means standing against widespread tradition? What is preventing you from doing so today?
?
Have you ever stretched the meaning of a Quranic verse to make it fit a sensational narrative? How can you commit to accepting the apparent meaning unless a clear proof demands ta'wil?
?
If the words 'trial' and 'forgiveness' in a verse cause you to immediately assume sin, what does that reveal about your heart's default attitude toward Allah's chosen messengers? Will you train yourself to think the best of them?

Unseen Matters

Razi's Three Interpretations for Dawud's Alleged Sin
Razi provides three detailed interpretations for the three apparent proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's three detailed interpretations that explain away the three apparent proofs of sin in the Dawud narrative.

Core Idea
Dawud's 'sin' is reinterpreted as forbearance, intercession, or self-critique for perfection.

Having identified three elements that might suggest sin (fitnah, istighfar, maghfirah), Razi now provides three logical interpretations that remove any implication of sin. These interpretations rely on Quranic parallels and contextual reasoning. Read the passage slowly to follow each argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the first interpretation (al-wajh al-awwal)
Razi explains that 'fitnah' means a test of Dawud's patience, and his restraint increased his rank. Then he connects istighfar to intercession for others, and maghfirah to forgiveness of the trespassers due to Dawud's sanctity. Note how each element is reinterpreted.
This interpretation avoids any sin by Dawud.
2
Examine the second interpretation
Razi suggests that Dawud's istighfar was for initially suspecting the trespassers of ill intent, then regretting that suspicion.
Regret for a mistaken thought, not a sin of action.
3
Study the third interpretation
Dawud feared self-admiration (ujb) for his forbearance, so he sought forgiveness for that potential spiritual flaw.
This is a high spiritual station, not a sin.
4
Reflect on Razi's conclusion
Razi declares that there is no indication of any lapse (zallat) for Dawud, and that this is the truth in his view.
This is the final position of the lesson.

المسألة الثانية والثلاثون
واعلم أن حمل الآية على ما ذكرناه حمل الكلام على ظاهره، أما حملها على القصة المشهورة فإنه يقتضي العدول عن الظاهر من وجهين:
الأول: أن الملائكة لما قالوا خَصْمَانِ بَغَى بَعْضُنَا عَلَى بَعْضٍ [ص: ٢٢] كان هذا كذبًا؛ لأنه لم يبغ أحد من الملائكة على الآخر، وإسناد الكذب إلى اللصوص أولى من إسناده إلى الملائكة.
الثاني: قوله: إِنَّ هَذَا أَخِي لَم يَسْعُ وَتَسْعُونَ نَعْجَةً وَلِي نَعْجَةٌ وَاحِدَةٌ [ص: ٢٣] هذا أيضًا كذب، والقوم يحملون النعاج على النسوان وهو عدول عن الظاهر، وأما على قولنا فقد نسبنا هذا الكذب إلى اللصوص، وهو أولى من نسبته إلى الملائكة.
وبالجملة: فليس في الآية لفظ يشهد بصحة ما ذكره من القصة إلا ثلاث:
أحدها: قوله: ﴿وَظَنَّ دَاوُدُ أَنَّمَا فَتَنَّهُ﴾ [ص: ٢٤] وذلك لأن لفظ الفتنة يوهم.
وثانيها: قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاسْتَغْفَرَ رَبَّهُ﴾ [ص: ٢٤] وذلك يوهم صدور الذنب منه.
وثالثها: قوله: ﴿فَغَفَرْنَا لَهُ ذَلِكَ﴾ [ص: ٢٥]
واعلم أن شيئًا من ذلك لا يدل على أقوالهم.
ويدل عليه وجوه:
الوجه الأول: أما قوله: ﴿وَظَنَّ دَاوُدُ أَنَّمَا فَتَنَّهُ﴾ فالمعنى: امتحناه واختبرناه، فإنه لما أساء الظن بهم، فهل يعاجلهم بالعقوبة أم لا؟ ثم إنه لكمال سلطته وقوة مملكته لم يعاجلهم بالعقوبة، ولم ينتقم منهم، ولم يضربهم، فكان ذلك سببًا لازدياد منصبه في الحكم والدين.
وأما قوله: ﴿فَاسْتَغْفَرَ رَبَّهُ﴾ فليس في الآية أن ذلك الاستغفار لنفسه أو لغيره، ألا ترى أنه تعالى حكى عن الملائكة بأنهم يستغفرون للذين آمنوا؟ وقال أولاد يعقوب: ﴿يَا أَبَانَا اسْتَغْفِرْ لَنَا ذُنُوبَنَا﴾ [يوسف: ٩٧]، قال تعالى لمحمد: ﴿وَاسْتَغْفِرْ لِذَنْبِكَ وَلِلْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَالْمُؤْمِنَاتِ﴾ [محمد: ١٩]، وإذا كان ذلك كذلك احتمل أن يكون المراد أن القوم لما أقدموا على ذلك الفعل المنكر لم يعاجلهم داود بالعقوبة، بل أظهر الحلم، وزاد على ذلك طلبه من الله تعالى أن يعفو عنهم وأن يغفر لهم.
وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿فَغَفَرْنَا لَهُ ذَلِكَ﴾ فيحتمل أن يكون المراد: فغفرنا لأجل حرمته، ولبركة شفاعته ذلك الفعل المنكر الذي أتى به أولئك المتسورون، وهذا التأويل الذي ذكرناه ينطبق عليه القرآن ولا نحتاج فيه إلى إسناد الكذب إلى الملائكة وحمل النعاج على النسوان، ثم إنه يليق به أن يذكر عقيب قوله: ﴿إِنَّا جَعَلْنَاكَ خَلِيفَةً فِي الْأَرْضِ﴾ [ص: ٢٦] فمن بلغت رحمته وشفقته على الرعية إلى هذا الحد كان اللائق برحمته أرحم الراحمين تفويض خلافة الأرض إليه، ويليق به أن يأمر محمدًا ﷺ عند تأذيه من قومه بأن يقتدي به، وهو قوله في أول الآية: ﴿اصْبِرْ عَلَى مَا يَقُولُونَ وَاذْكُرْ عَبْدَنَا دَاوُدَ ذَا الْأَيْدِ﴾ [ص: ١٧]، ومن طلب الحق وأنصف علم أن ما ذكرناه هو الحق الصريح.
الوجه الثاني: لعل الاستغفار إنما كان لأن القوم لما تسوروا داره ظن بهم أنهم يقصدون قتله ثم إنه لما لم تظهر الأمارات الدالة على أن ذلك الظن حق ندم على ذلك الظن، فكان الاستغفار بسببه.
الوجه الثالث: أنه لما هضم نفسه ولم يؤذهم ولم ينتقم منهم مع القدرة التامة دخله شيء من العجب بسبب كمال حلمه فكان الاستغفار منه لأن العجب من المهلكات.
فهذا قول من يقول: لا دلالة في الآية على إثباته بشيء من الزلات، وهو الحق عندي.
وأما من سلم دلالة الآية على الصغيرة فلهم فيه وجوه:
أحدها: أنه كان عالمًا بحسن امرأة أوريا، فلما سمع أنه قتل قَلَ غمه لميل نفسه إلى نكاح زوجته، فعوتب عليه.
وثانيها: أن أهل زمان داود كان يسأل بعضهم بعضًا أن ينزل له عن امرأته ليتزوج بها إذا أعجبته، وكان ذلك جائزًا فيما بينهم، واتفق أن عين داود وقعت على امرأة أوريا فأحبها، فسأله النزول عنها، فاستحيى أن يرده ففعل، فتزوجها، وأم سليمان فقيل له: إنك مع ارتفاع قدرك وكثرة نسائك ما كان يليق بك أن تسأل رجلاً ليس له إلا امرأة واحدة أن ينزل عنها، بل كان الواجب عليك قهر النفس.
The thirty-second issue. Know that interpreting the verse as we have done is taking the speech according to its apparent meaning. As for interpreting it according to the famous story, it requires deviation from the apparent meaning in two respects: First, when the angels said 'Two adversaries, some of us transgressed against others' (Surah Sad 22), this would be a lie, because no angel transgressed against another, and attributing the lie to the thieves is more fitting than attributing it to the angels. Second, His saying 'Indeed this brother of mine has ninety-nine ewes, and I have one ewe' (Surah Sad 23) is also a lie, and they interpret the ewes as women, which is a deviation from the apparent meaning. As for our view, we have attributed this lie to the thieves, which is more fitting than attributing it to the angels. In summary, there is nothing in the verse that testifies to the correctness of the story they mentioned except three things: One: His saying 'And Dawud thought that We had tested him' (Surah Sad 24), because the word 'fitnah' suggests [something]. Second: His saying 'So he sought forgiveness from his Lord' (Surah Sad 24), which suggests the occurrence of sin from him. Third: His saying 'And We forgave him that' (Surah Sad 25). Know that none of this indicates what they claim. There are proofs for our view: First proof: As for His saying 'And Dawud thought that We had tested him', the meaning is that We tested and tried him, for when he thought badly of them, would he hasten to punish them or not? Then, due to the perfection of his authority and the strength of his kingdom, he did not hasten to punish them, nor did he take revenge from them, nor did he strike them, and that became a reason for the increase of his rank in judgment and religion. As for His saying 'So he sought forgiveness from his Lord', it is not in the verse that this seeking forgiveness was for himself or for others. Do you not see that Allah Almighty related about the angels that they seek forgiveness for those who believe? And the sons of Jacob said 'O our father, seek forgiveness for us for our sins' (Surah Yusuf 97). Allah said to Muhammad: 'And seek forgiveness for your sin and for the believing men and believing women' (Surah Muhammad 19). If that is the case, then it is possible that the meaning is that when the people committed that reprehensible act, Dawud did not hasten to punish them, but rather showed forbearance, and in addition he asked Allah to pardon them and forgive them. As for His saying 'So We forgave him that', it is possible that the meaning is: We forgave, on account of his sanctity and the blessing of his intercession, that reprehensible act which those trespassers committed. This interpretation we have mentioned conforms to the Quran, and we do not need therein to attribute lies to the angels or to interpret ewes as women. Moreover, it is fitting that it be mentioned after His saying 'Indeed We have made you a vicegerent on earth' (Surah Sad 26). For one whose mercy and compassion for subjects reaches this extent, it is befitting for the Most Merciful of the merciful to entrust to him the vicegerency of the earth. And it is fitting that He command Muhammad, when he is harmed by his people, to follow his example, which is His saying at the beginning of the verse: 'Be patient over what they say and remember Our servant Dawud, the possessor of strength' (Surah Sad 17). Whoever seeks the truth and is fair knows that what we have mentioned is the manifest truth. Second proof: Perhaps the seeking forgiveness was because when the people scaled his wall, he thought that they intended to kill him. Then, when the signs did not appear indicating that that thought was correct, he regretted that thought, and so the seeking forgiveness was due to it. Third proof: When he humbled himself and did not harm them nor take revenge from them despite complete ability, some self-admiration entered him due to the perfection of his forbearance, so he sought forgiveness, because self-admiration is among the destructive things. This is the view of one who says: There is no indication in the verse of proving any lapses for him, and it is the truth in my view. As for one who concedes that the verse indicates a minor sin, they have several interpretations: One: He was aware of the beauty of the wife of Uriah, and when he heard that he was killed, his grief diminished due to his inclination to marry his wife, so he was reproached for that. Second: The people of Dawud's time used to ask one another to give up his wife for him to marry her if he admired her, and that was permissible among them. It happened that Dawud's eye fell on the wife of Uriah, so he loved her, and he asked him to give her up. Uriah was too shy to refuse him, so he did it, and Dawud married her, and she was the mother of Solomon. So it was said to him: 'With your high status and many wives, it is not befitting for you to ask a man who has only one wife to give her up; rather, you should have subdued your soul.'
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument defending the sinlessness of the prophet Dawud (David) against interpretations that suggest he committed a sin based on the verses of Surah Sad. Razi begins by stating that his own interpretation adheres to the apparent meaning of the Quran, while the popular story (al-qissah al-mashhurah) requires deviation from the apparent meaning in two ways. First, if the angels were the speakers when they said 'Two adversaries, some of us transgressed against others' (38:22), that would be a lie because angels do not transgress against each other. Razi points out that attributing a lie to the thieves (al-lusus) who trespassed is more fitting than attributing it to angels. Second, if the verse 'This brother of mine has ninety-nine ewes' (38:23) is taken literally as a claim by the angels, it would also be a lie, and interpreting 'ewes' as women is a deviation from the apparent meaning. Razi argues that those who accept the popular story must commit these deviations, whereas his view avoids them by attributing the lie to the trespassers. He then identifies three elements in the verses that might seem to imply sin: the word 'fitnah' (trial) in 'Dawud thought that We had tested him' (38:24), his seeking forgiveness (38:24), and Allah's forgiveness (38:25). Razi argues that none of these necessarily indicate sin. He offers three detailed interpretations (wujuh) to show how these verses can be understood without implying sin. In the first interpretation, he explains that 'fitnah' means Allah tested Dawud's forbearance: when Dawud thought badly of the trespassers, he had the power to punish them immediately but instead showed restraint, which increased his rank. As for seeking forgiveness, Razi argues that the Quranic context shows that prophets can seek forgiveness for others (e.g., angels for believers, Jacob for his sons, Muhammad for all believers). Therefore, Dawud's plea could have been for the trespassers, not for himself. Similarly, Allah's forgiveness could mean He forgave the trespassers due to Dawud's intercession. Razi emphasizes that this interpretation fits the Quranic style and avoids the need to attribute lies to angels or interpret ewes metaphorically as women. He also connects this to the following verse (38:26) about vicegerency, showing that Dawud's mercy qualifies him for such a role, and to the earlier command to Muhammad to be patient, implying that Dawud's example is one of patience and mercy. The second interpretation suggests that Dawud's seeking forgiveness was due to regretting his initial suspicion that the trespassers intended to kill him. The third interpretation suggests that Dawud experienced a moment of self-admiration for his forbearance, which is a destructive quality, so he sought forgiveness for that. Razi concludes that the verses contain no proof of any lapse (zallat) for Dawud, and this is the truth in his view. He then reports two alternative views held by those who concede that the verses indicate a minor sin (saghirah): one involving Dawud's desire to marry Uriah's wife after Uriah's death, and another involving a customary practice in Dawud's time where men could request a wife from another man, and Dawud was reproached for not controlling his desire despite his high status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the three elements (fitnah, istighfar, maghfirah) necessarily prove Dawud committed a sin.
Correction: Razi shows each can be interpreted in a way consistent with sinlessness: fitnah as a test, istighfar as intercession or regret for a suspicion, and maghfirah as forgiveness of others.

Checkpoint
In Razi's first interpretation, what is the meaning of 'fitnah' in the verse?
A) Dawud committed a sin
B) Allah tested Dawud's patience
C) Dawud was tempted by a woman
D) The angels were tested

Key Takeaway
Razi provides three interpretations that show the verses do not imply sin; they can refer to tests, intercession, or self-critique.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When someone wrongs you and you have the power to retaliate, do you restrain yourself like Dawud, or do you seek revenge? What does your response say about your trust in Allah's justice? Ask Allah to grant you patience like His prophets.
?
Have you ever found yourself proud of your own forbearance or patience, like Dawud might have felt? Did that pride lead you to seek forgiveness from Allah? Reflect on a recent instance and commit to checking your heart for self-admiration.
?
Razi argues that prophets can seek forgiveness for others. Do you regularly intercede in prayer for those who have wronged you? If not, what stops you? Make a list of people you will pray for this week.

Unseen Matters

Views that Accept a Minor Sin for Dawud
Razi reports two interpretations for those who accept a minor sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two interpretations offered by scholars who concede that the verses imply a minor sin (saghirah) for Dawud.

Core Idea
Even if the verses imply a minor sin, the two proposed scenarios involve personal inclination or custom, not major sin.

After presenting his own view that no sin is indicated, Razi reports the views of those who accept the verses as implying a minor sin. He mentions two interpretations that attempt to explain what the sin might have been, both involving his relationship with Uriah's wife. Read the passage to see the details.

Guided Path
1
Read the first view
Razi reports that some say Dawud's sin was that his grief diminished upon hearing of Uriah's death because he desired to marry his wife. He was reproached for this.
This involves a human inclination, not a sinful act.
2
Read the second view
Another view says that in Dawud's time, it was permissible to request a wife from another man. Dawud asked Uriah for his wife, and Uriah complied, but Dawud was criticized for his high status and many wives.
This was not a sin in itself but was considered unbecoming of a prophet.
3
Compare with Razi's own view
Notice that Razi does not endorse these views; he presents them as alternatives for those who insist the verses indicate sin.
His own position is the one from the previous lesson.

المسألة الثانية والثلاثون
واعلم أن حمل الآية على ما ذكرناه حمل الكلام على ظاهره، أما حملها على القصة المشهورة فإنه يقتضي العدول عن الظاهر من وجهين:
الأول: أن الملائكة لما قالوا خَصْمَانِ بَغَى بَعْضُنَا عَلَى بَعْضٍ [ص: ٢٢] كان هذا كذبًا؛ لأنه لم يبغ أحد من الملائكة على الآخر، وإسناد الكذب إلى اللصوص أولى من إسناده إلى الملائكة.
الثاني: قوله: إِنَّ هَذَا أَخِي لَم يَسْعُ وَتَسْعُونَ نَعْجَةً وَلِي نَعْجَةٌ وَاحِدَةٌ [ص: ٢٣] هذا أيضًا كذب، والقوم يحملون النعاج على النسوان وهو عدول عن الظاهر، وأما على قولنا فقد نسبنا هذا الكذب إلى اللصوص، وهو أولى من نسبته إلى الملائكة.
وبالجملة: فليس في الآية لفظ يشهد بصحة ما ذكره من القصة إلا ثلاث:
أحدها: قوله: ﴿وَظَنَّ دَاوُدُ أَنَّمَا فَتَنَّهُ﴾ [ص: ٢٤] وذلك لأن لفظ الفتنة يوهم.
وثانيها: قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاسْتَغْفَرَ رَبَّهُ﴾ [ص: ٢٤] وذلك يوهم صدور الذنب منه.
وثالثها: قوله: ﴿فَغَفَرْنَا لَهُ ذَلِكَ﴾ [ص: ٢٥]
واعلم أن شيئًا من ذلك لا يدل على أقوالهم.
ويدل عليه وجوه:
الوجه الأول: أما قوله: ﴿وَظَنَّ دَاوُدُ أَنَّمَا فَتَنَّهُ﴾ فالمعنى: امتحناه واختبرناه، فإنه لما أساء الظن بهم، فهل يعاجلهم بالعقوبة أم لا؟ ثم إنه لكمال سلطته وقوة مملكته لم يعاجلهم بالعقوبة، ولم ينتقم منهم، ولم يضربهم، فكان ذلك سببًا لازدياد منصبه في الحكم والدين.
وأما قوله: ﴿فَاسْتَغْفَرَ رَبَّهُ﴾ فليس في الآية أن ذلك الاستغفار لنفسه أو لغيره، ألا ترى أنه تعالى حكى عن الملائكة بأنهم يستغفرون للذين آمنوا؟ وقال أولاد يعقوب: ﴿يَا أَبَانَا اسْتَغْفِرْ لَنَا ذُنُوبَنَا﴾ [يوسف: ٩٧]، قال تعالى لمحمد: ﴿وَاسْتَغْفِرْ لِذَنْبِكَ وَلِلْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَالْمُؤْمِنَاتِ﴾ [محمد: ١٩]، وإذا كان ذلك كذلك احتمل أن يكون المراد أن القوم لما أقدموا على ذلك الفعل المنكر لم يعاجلهم داود بالعقوبة، بل أظهر الحلم، وزاد على ذلك طلبه من الله تعالى أن يعفو عنهم وأن يغفر لهم.
وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿فَغَفَرْنَا لَهُ ذَلِكَ﴾ فيحتمل أن يكون المراد: فغفرنا لأجل حرمته، ولبركة شفاعته ذلك الفعل المنكر الذي أتى به أولئك المتسورون، وهذا التأويل الذي ذكرناه ينطبق عليه القرآن ولا نحتاج فيه إلى إسناد الكذب إلى الملائكة وحمل النعاج على النسوان، ثم إنه يليق به أن يذكر عقيب قوله: ﴿إِنَّا جَعَلْنَاكَ خَلِيفَةً فِي الْأَرْضِ﴾ [ص: ٢٦] فمن بلغت رحمته وشفقته على الرعية إلى هذا الحد كان اللائق برحمته أرحم الراحمين تفويض خلافة الأرض إليه، ويليق به أن يأمر محمدًا ﷺ عند تأذيه من قومه بأن يقتدي به، وهو قوله في أول الآية: ﴿اصْبِرْ عَلَى مَا يَقُولُونَ وَاذْكُرْ عَبْدَنَا دَاوُدَ ذَا الْأَيْدِ﴾ [ص: ١٧]، ومن طلب الحق وأنصف علم أن ما ذكرناه هو الحق الصريح.
الوجه الثاني: لعل الاستغفار إنما كان لأن القوم لما تسوروا داره ظن بهم أنهم يقصدون قتله ثم إنه لما لم تظهر الأمارات الدالة على أن ذلك الظن حق ندم على ذلك الظن، فكان الاستغفار بسببه.
الوجه الثالث: أنه لما هضم نفسه ولم يؤذهم ولم ينتقم منهم مع القدرة التامة دخله شيء من العجب بسبب كمال حلمه فكان الاستغفار منه لأن العجب من المهلكات.
فهذا قول من يقول: لا دلالة في الآية على إثباته بشيء من الزلات، وهو الحق عندي.
وأما من سلم دلالة الآية على الصغيرة فلهم فيه وجوه:
أحدها: أنه كان عالمًا بحسن امرأة أوريا، فلما سمع أنه قتل قَلَ غمه لميل نفسه إلى نكاح زوجته، فعوتب عليه.
وثانيها: أن أهل زمان داود كان يسأل بعضهم بعضًا أن ينزل له عن امرأته ليتزوج بها إذا أعجبته، وكان ذلك جائزًا فيما بينهم، واتفق أن عين داود وقعت على امرأة أوريا فأحبها، فسأله النزول عنها، فاستحيى أن يرده ففعل، فتزوجها، وأم سليمان فقيل له: إنك مع ارتفاع قدرك وكثرة نسائك ما كان يليق بك أن تسأل رجلاً ليس له إلا امرأة واحدة أن ينزل عنها، بل كان الواجب عليك قهر النفس.
The thirty-second issue. Know that interpreting the verse as we have done is taking the speech according to its apparent meaning. As for interpreting it according to the famous story, it requires deviation from the apparent meaning in two respects: First, when the angels said 'Two adversaries, some of us transgressed against others' (Surah Sad 22), this would be a lie, because no angel transgressed against another, and attributing the lie to the thieves is more fitting than attributing it to the angels. Second, His saying 'Indeed this brother of mine has ninety-nine ewes, and I have one ewe' (Surah Sad 23) is also a lie, and they interpret the ewes as women, which is a deviation from the apparent meaning. As for our view, we have attributed this lie to the thieves, which is more fitting than attributing it to the angels. In summary, there is nothing in the verse that testifies to the correctness of the story they mentioned except three things: One: His saying 'And Dawud thought that We had tested him' (Surah Sad 24), because the word 'fitnah' suggests [something]. Second: His saying 'So he sought forgiveness from his Lord' (Surah Sad 24), which suggests the occurrence of sin from him. Third: His saying 'And We forgave him that' (Surah Sad 25). Know that none of this indicates what they claim. There are proofs for our view: First proof: As for His saying 'And Dawud thought that We had tested him', the meaning is that We tested and tried him, for when he thought badly of them, would he hasten to punish them or not? Then, due to the perfection of his authority and the strength of his kingdom, he did not hasten to punish them, nor did he take revenge from them, nor did he strike them, and that became a reason for the increase of his rank in judgment and religion. As for His saying 'So he sought forgiveness from his Lord', it is not in the verse that this seeking forgiveness was for himself or for others. Do you not see that Allah Almighty related about the angels that they seek forgiveness for those who believe? And the sons of Jacob said 'O our father, seek forgiveness for us for our sins' (Surah Yusuf 97). Allah said to Muhammad: 'And seek forgiveness for your sin and for the believing men and believing women' (Surah Muhammad 19). If that is the case, then it is possible that the meaning is that when the people committed that reprehensible act, Dawud did not hasten to punish them, but rather showed forbearance, and in addition he asked Allah to pardon them and forgive them. As for His saying 'So We forgave him that', it is possible that the meaning is: We forgave, on account of his sanctity and the blessing of his intercession, that reprehensible act which those trespassers committed. This interpretation we have mentioned conforms to the Quran, and we do not need therein to attribute lies to the angels or to interpret ewes as women. Moreover, it is fitting that it be mentioned after His saying 'Indeed We have made you a vicegerent on earth' (Surah Sad 26). For one whose mercy and compassion for subjects reaches this extent, it is befitting for the Most Merciful of the merciful to entrust to him the vicegerency of the earth. And it is fitting that He command Muhammad, when he is harmed by his people, to follow his example, which is His saying at the beginning of the verse: 'Be patient over what they say and remember Our servant Dawud, the possessor of strength' (Surah Sad 17). Whoever seeks the truth and is fair knows that what we have mentioned is the manifest truth. Second proof: Perhaps the seeking forgiveness was because when the people scaled his wall, he thought that they intended to kill him. Then, when the signs did not appear indicating that that thought was correct, he regretted that thought, and so the seeking forgiveness was due to it. Third proof: When he humbled himself and did not harm them nor take revenge from them despite complete ability, some self-admiration entered him due to the perfection of his forbearance, so he sought forgiveness, because self-admiration is among the destructive things. This is the view of one who says: There is no indication in the verse of proving any lapses for him, and it is the truth in my view. As for one who concedes that the verse indicates a minor sin, they have several interpretations: One: He was aware of the beauty of the wife of Uriah, and when he heard that he was killed, his grief diminished due to his inclination to marry his wife, so he was reproached for that. Second: The people of Dawud's time used to ask one another to give up his wife for him to marry her if he admired her, and that was permissible among them. It happened that Dawud's eye fell on the wife of Uriah, so he loved her, and he asked him to give her up. Uriah was too shy to refuse him, so he did it, and Dawud married her, and she was the mother of Solomon. So it was said to him: 'With your high status and many wives, it is not befitting for you to ask a man who has only one wife to give her up; rather, you should have subdued your soul.'
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument defending the sinlessness of the prophet Dawud (David) against interpretations that suggest he committed a sin based on the verses of Surah Sad. Razi begins by stating that his own interpretation adheres to the apparent meaning of the Quran, while the popular story (al-qissah al-mashhurah) requires deviation from the apparent meaning in two ways. First, if the angels were the speakers when they said 'Two adversaries, some of us transgressed against others' (38:22), that would be a lie because angels do not transgress against each other. Razi points out that attributing a lie to the thieves (al-lusus) who trespassed is more fitting than attributing it to angels. Second, if the verse 'This brother of mine has ninety-nine ewes' (38:23) is taken literally as a claim by the angels, it would also be a lie, and interpreting 'ewes' as women is a deviation from the apparent meaning. Razi argues that those who accept the popular story must commit these deviations, whereas his view avoids them by attributing the lie to the trespassers. He then identifies three elements in the verses that might seem to imply sin: the word 'fitnah' (trial) in 'Dawud thought that We had tested him' (38:24), his seeking forgiveness (38:24), and Allah's forgiveness (38:25). Razi argues that none of these necessarily indicate sin. He offers three detailed interpretations (wujuh) to show how these verses can be understood without implying sin. In the first interpretation, he explains that 'fitnah' means Allah tested Dawud's forbearance: when Dawud thought badly of the trespassers, he had the power to punish them immediately but instead showed restraint, which increased his rank. As for seeking forgiveness, Razi argues that the Quranic context shows that prophets can seek forgiveness for others (e.g., angels for believers, Jacob for his sons, Muhammad for all believers). Therefore, Dawud's plea could have been for the trespassers, not for himself. Similarly, Allah's forgiveness could mean He forgave the trespassers due to Dawud's intercession. Razi emphasizes that this interpretation fits the Quranic style and avoids the need to attribute lies to angels or interpret ewes metaphorically as women. He also connects this to the following verse (38:26) about vicegerency, showing that Dawud's mercy qualifies him for such a role, and to the earlier command to Muhammad to be patient, implying that Dawud's example is one of patience and mercy. The second interpretation suggests that Dawud's seeking forgiveness was due to regretting his initial suspicion that the trespassers intended to kill him. The third interpretation suggests that Dawud experienced a moment of self-admiration for his forbearance, which is a destructive quality, so he sought forgiveness for that. Razi concludes that the verses contain no proof of any lapse (zallat) for Dawud, and this is the truth in his view. He then reports two alternative views held by those who concede that the verses indicate a minor sin (saghirah): one involving Dawud's desire to marry Uriah's wife after Uriah's death, and another involving a customary practice in Dawud's time where men could request a wife from another man, and Dawud was reproached for not controlling his desire despite his high status.

Key Terms
الصغيرة
أوريا
النزول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the verses prove Dawud committed a major sin like adultery.
Correction: The interpretations here only suggest a minor sin (saghirah) such as diminished grief or a request that was socially inappropriate, not a grave sin.

Checkpoint
According to the second interpretation, why was Dawud criticized?
A) He committed adultery
B) He asked a man with one wife to give her up
C) He killed Uriah
D) He worshipped idols

Key Takeaway
Those who accept a minor sin interpret Dawud's action as either diminished grief or an inappropriate request, not as a grave sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever excused a wrong action by telling yourself it was 'just a small mistake'? Is that not the same mindset as the minor sin interpretation? Will you hold yourself to the same standard you hold the prophets, or do you lower the bar for yourself?
?
The second interpretation shows that something permissible (asking for a wife) was unbecoming for Dawud given his status. Are there permissible things in your life that are beneath the station of a Muslim? Will you choose what is 'allowed' or what is befitting of someone who stands before Allah every day?
?
Razi does not accept these interpretations; he insists on complete innocence. When you read verses that seem to criticize a prophet, do you rush to find excuses, or do you trust that the prophet is innocent and seek deeper understanding? How does your heart's posture toward the prophets reflect your love for them?

The Fourth Proof: Angels' Perpetual Worship
Imam Razi presents the fourth proof that angels' continuous worship makes them superior.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth proof for the superiority of angels based on the perpetuity of their worship, including its scriptural basis and four supporting arguments.

Core Idea
Angels' continuous worship, combined with equal quality, makes their reward greater.

Imam Razi presents a compelling argument focusing on the uninterrupted nature of angelic worship. He first establishes that angels worship perpetually, then provides four reasons why this makes their worship superior, supported by Quran and hadith. This proof is part of a broader discussion on the relative merits of angels and humans.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp the overall argument.
Pay attention to the Quranic verse and the four numbered reasons.
2
Identify the main claim and Quranic proof
Notice how Imam Razi first asserts that angels' worship is more perpetual (adwam) and cites Quran 21:20. Consider why this verse is sufficient evidence.
He also mentions the lifespan comparison to strengthen the point.
3
Examine each of the four reasons
Go through each of the four reasons why perpetual worship is superior: difficulty, hadith on long life, hadith on elder, and equality in quality plus added duration.
The fourth reason is the most detailed, using multiple Quranic verses.
4
Reflect on the combination of quality and quantity
Notice that the argument does not rely solely on duration; it first establishes that angels' worship equals humans' in quality (fear and humility), then adds duration. This avoids the misconception that duration alone matters.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثالثة والثلاثون : الحجة الرابعة عبادات الملائكة أدوم فوجب أن تكون أفضل. إنما قلنا أدوم لقوله تعالى : يُسَبِّحُونَ الَّيْلَ وَالنَّهَارَ لَا يَفْتَرُونَ [الأنبياء : ٢٠] وعلى هذا التقدير لو كانت أعمارهم مساوية لأعمار البشر لكانت طاعتهم أكثر وأدوم، فكيف ولا نسبة لعمر كل البشر إلى عمر الملائكة ؟ وإنما قلنا إن الأدوم أفضل لوجوه : أحدها: أن الأدوم أشق فكان أفضل، وقد بينا هذا الوجه. الثاني : قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : أفضل العباد من طال عمره وحسن عمله والملائكة أطول العباد عمرًا وأحسنهم عملاً، فوجب أن يكونوا أفضل العباد. والثالث : قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : الشيخ في قومه كالنبي في أمته وهذا يقتضي أن يكون الملك فيما بين البشر كالنبي في الأمة، وذلك يوجب فضلهم على البشر. الرابع : أن طاعات الملائكة مساوية لطاعات بني آدم في الخوف والخشية، قال تعالى : يَخَافُونَ رَبَّهُم مِّن فَوْقِهِمْ [النحل : ٥٠] وقال : لَا يَسْبِقُونَهُ بِالْقَوْلِ وَهُم بِأَمْرِهِ يَعْمَلُونَ [الأنبياء : ٢٧] وقال: وَهُم مِّنْ خَشْيَتِهِ مُشْفِقُونَ [الأنبياء: ٢٨] وقال تعالى: حَتَّى إِذَا فُرْعَ عَن قُلُوبِهِمْ قَالُوا مَاذَا قَالَ رَبُّكُمْ قَالُوا الْحَقَّ وَهُوَ الْعَلِيُّ الْكَبِيرُ [سبأ : ٢٣] فهذه الآيات دالة على أن غاية خشوع الملائكة وخضوعهم إن لم يكن أزيد من خشوع البشر وخضوعهم فلا يكون أقل منه، وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : طاعات الملائكة مساوية لطاعات البشر في الكيفية الموجبة للثواب، وهي الخشوع والخضوع، وأزيد منها في المدة والدوام، فوجب القطع بأن ثوابهم أزيد وأكثر.
The Thirty-Third Issue: The Fourth Proof: The worship of angels is more perpetual, so they must be superior. We say it is more perpetual because of His statement: 'They glorify [Him] night and day, never slackening' (Quran 21:20). On this assumption, if their lifespans were equal to those of humans, their obedience would be greater and more perpetual; how then [when there is] no proportion between the lifespan of all humans and the lifespan of angels? And we say that the more perpetual is better for several reasons: First: The more perpetual is more difficult, so it is better, and we have already explained this aspect. Second: His statement, peace be upon him: 'The best of servants is one whose life is long and whose deeds are good'; and angels are the longest-lived servants and the best of them in deeds, so they must be the best of servants. Third: His statement, peace be upon him: 'The elder among his people is like the prophet among his nation'; this implies that the angel among humans is like the prophet among the nation, and that necessitates their superiority over humans. Fourth: The acts of obedience of angels are equal to those of the children of Adam in fear and awe; He said: 'They fear their Lord above them' (Quran 16:50), and He said: 'They do not precede Him in speech, and they act by His command' (Quran 21:27), and He said: 'And they are fearful of Him' (Quran 21:28), and He said: 'Until when their hearts are relieved, they say: What did your Lord say? They say: The truth, and He is the Most High, the Grand' (Quran 34:23). These verses indicate that the utmost humility and submission of angels, if not greater than that of humans, is not less than it. When this is established, we say: The acts of obedience of angels are equal to those of humans in the quality that necessitates reward, namely humility and submission, and exceed them in duration and perpetuity, so it must be concluded that their reward is greater and more abundant.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof for the superiority of angels over humans, focusing on the perpetuity of their worship. Imam Razi begins by asserting that angels' worship is more continuous (adwam) based on Quran 21:20, which says they glorify God night and day without ceasing. He then explains that even if angels' lifespans were equal to humans', their obedience would be more, but in fact angels live much longer. Next, he gives four reasons why the more perpetual is superior: (1) Perpetuity implies greater difficulty, which increases reward. (2) A hadith states that the best servant is one with long life and good deeds; angels have both. (3) The hadith likening an elder to a prophet implies angels are like prophets among humans, showing their high status. (4) Qualitatively, angels' worship equals humans' in fear and humility, as proven by several verses, but exceeds in duration, so their reward must be greater. The reasoning is layered, grounding each point in scripture and logical implication.

Key Terms
أدوم
أفضل
طاعات
خشوع
خضوع
ثواب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That duration alone determines superiority without considering quality.
Correction: Imam Razi first establishes that angels' worship equals humans' in quality (fear and humility), then adds duration. The argument combines both quantity and quality.

Checkpoint
Which Quranic verse does Imam Razi use to prove angels worship perpetually?
A) Quran 16:50
B) Quran 21:20: 'They glorify night and day, never slackening'
C) Quran 34:23
D) Quran 21:27

Key Takeaway
Angels' worship is superior because it is both qualitatively equal to humans' worship and quantitatively perpetual.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to love God, but do you glorify Him night and day without slackening, or do you allow distractions to interrupt your worship? How will you increase the perpetuity of your obedience starting today?
?
The angels match humans in humility and awe, yet exceed in duration. If your life were compared to an angel's, would your deeds be equal in quality? Where do you need to increase khushu' and khudu' in your prayer and daily life?
?
The hadith says the best servant is one with long life and good deeds. If your life ended today, would your deeds be considered good enough to be among the best? What specific change can you make this week to align with this standard?

Angels' Priority in Worship and Their Superiority
Imam Razi argues that angels are prior in worship and the prior is superior.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Razi argues that angels are superior to humans due to their temporal priority in worship, and the scriptural evidence he uses.

Core Idea
Priority in worship implies superior reward because of the precedent's multiplied merit.

Imam Razi continues his proofs for the superiority of angels with a fifth argument based on temporal priority. He asserts that angels were the first to perform all acts of worship, and because the one who establishes a good practice earns the reward of all who follow, angels accumulate enormous merit. In this lesson, we examine his reasoning and the Quranic and prophetic evidence he presents.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
2
Identify the two claims
The passage makes two main claims: angels are prior in worship, and the prior is better. Notice how the author structures the argument.
3
Examine the evidence for priority
The author states that angels are the imams and establishers of all religious practices. Reflect on what this implies about their role.
4
Study the two proofs for superiority
The Quranic verse about the foremost and the hadith about establishing a good practice. Understand how each supports the claim.
5
Reflect on the implication
Angels' reward includes all rewards of prophets plus their own prior deeds. How does this establish superiority?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة : الملائكة أسبق في العبادة من البشر، والأسبق أفضل، أما أنهم أسبق فلا شك فيه إذ من المعلوم أنه لا خصلة من خصال الدين إلا وهم أئمة مقتندون فيها بل هم المنشؤون العامرون لطرق الدين. وأما أن الأسبق أفضل فلوجهين : الأول : قوله تعالى : وَالسَّبِقُونَ السَّبِقُونَ أُولَيْكَ الْمُقَرَّبُونَ [الواقعة: ١٠-١١] الثاني : قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : من سن سنة حسنة فله أجرها وأجر من عمل بها إلى يوم القيامة وهذا يقتضي أن يكون قد حصل للملائكة من الثواب كل ما حصل للأنبياء مع زيادة الثواب التي استحقوها بأفعالهم التي أتوا بها قبل خلق البشر.
The Fifth Proof: Angels are prior in worship to humans, and the prior is better. As for their being prior, there is no doubt about it, since it is known that there is no trait of religion except that they are the imams followed in it; rather they are the establishers and cultivators of the ways of religion. As for the prior being better, there are two aspects: First: His statement: 'And the foremost, the foremost – those are the ones brought near' (Quran 56:10-11). Second: His statement, peace be upon him: 'Whoever establishes a good practice has its reward and the reward of those who act upon it until the Day of Judgment.' This implies that angels have obtained all the reward that the prophets obtained, plus the additional reward they deserved for their deeds that they performed before the creation of humans.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth proof, focusing on temporal priority in worship. Imam Razi asserts without doubt that angels are prior (asbaq) in every religious practice; they are the imams and establishers of religious ways. Then he gives two evidences that priority implies superiority: (1) Quranic verse about the 'foremost' being brought near to God. (2) The hadith that one who establishes a good practice gets the reward of all who follow it until Judgment Day. Applying this, angels, who first performed worship, earn reward equal to that of all later worshippers, including prophets, plus extra for their own prior deeds. Thus their reward exceeds that of any human.

Key Terms
أسبق
مقتندون
منشؤون
عامرون
سنة حسنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That priority alone without evidence is sufficient to prove superiority.
Correction: Imam Razi provides scriptural evidence from Quran and hadith to support the claim that priority implies superiority.

Checkpoint
What hadith does Imam Razi use to argue that the prior gets more reward?
A) The best of servants is one whose life is long...
B) Whoever establishes a good practice has its reward and the reward of those who act upon it...
C) The elder among his people is like the prophet...
D) My companions are like stars...

Key Takeaway
Imam Razi uses temporal priority and the multiplied reward of the establisher to prove angels' superiority over humans.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your worship, do you aim to be a founder of good practices that outlive you, or are you content to follow? What one sunnah hasanah could you establish starting today, knowing its reward will continue even after you?
?
The angels are prior in worship and superior. Does this challenge any pride you feel in your own acts of worship? How can you learn from their constant devotion without comparison?
?
If you knew that a single good deed you initiate could be followed by countless others until Judgment Day, would you hesitate? What is holding you back from taking that step right now?

The First Premise: Angels as Messengers to Prophets
Razi cites Quranic verses to prove angels are messengers to prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first premise of the sixth proof: that angels are messengers to prophets, supported by Quranic verses.

Core Idea
Angels are divinely appointed messengers to prophets, a key proof of their superiority.

Imam Razi begins his sixth proof by establishing a foundational premise: angels are messengers sent by Allah to the prophets. This claim is supported by several Quranic verses that depict angels, especially Jibril, as the ones who bring revelation. In this lesson, we will examine these verses and understand how they set the stage for the argument of angelic superiority.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once to get the rhythm of the argument.
Pay attention to the citation of Quranic verses.
2
Identify the Quranic verses
List the three verses cited and note how each one describes angels as messengers.
Verses are from Surah An-Najm, Ash-Shu'ara, and An-Nahl.
3
Understand the premise
Reflect on how these verses collectively prove that angels are sent to prophets as messengers.
This is the foundation for the rest of the proof.
4
Consider Jibril's role
Note that Jibril is specifically mentioned as the Trustworthy Spirit who brings revelation to the Prophet's heart.
Jibril is a prime example of an angelic messenger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : الملائكة رسل الله إلى الأنبياء، والرسول أفضل من [؟] المقدمة الأولى : وهي أن الملائكة رسل الله إلى الأنبياء قوله تعالى : ذُو مِرَّةٍ فَاسْتَوَى [النجم: ٦] نَزَلَ بِهِ الرُّوحُ الْأَمِينُ عَلَى قَلْبِكَ [الشعراء: ١٩٣-١٩٤]، يُنَزِّلُ الْمَلَائِكَةَ بِالرُّوحِ مِنْ أَمْرِهِ عَلَى مَن يَشَاءُ مِنْ عِبَادِهِ [النحل : ٢] . وأما المقدمة الثانية : وهي أن الرسول أفضل من أمته فلوجهين : الأول : أن الرسول البشر أفضل من أمته فكذا ههنا. فإن قيل : العرف أن السلطان إذا أرسل واحدًا إلى جمع عظيم ليكون متولياً لأمورهم وحاكماً فيهم فذلك الشخص أفضل من ذلك الجمع، وأما إذا أرسل شخصاً واحداً إلى شخص واحد لأجل الإعلام فالظاهر أن الرسول أقل حالاً [؟] كَمَا إذا أرسل الملك عبده إلى الوزير. قلنا : هذا مدفوع ؛ لأن جبريل المبعوث إلى كافة الأنبياء، والرسل من البشر، فجبريل الرسول وأمته كل الأنبياء، فعلى القانون الذي ذكره السائل يلزم أن يكون جبريل أفضل منهم. الوجه الثاني : أن الملائكة رسل الله صلوات الله وسلامه عليهم لقوله : جَاعِلِ الْمَلَائِكَةِ رُسُلًا [فاطر: ١] والملك إما أن يكون رسولاً إلى ملك آخر، وإما أن يكون رسولاً إلى البشر، وعلى التقديرين فالملك رسول وأمته أيضاً رسل، وأما الرسول البشري فهو رسول لكن أمته ليسوا برسل ومعلوم أن الرسول الذي تكون كل أمته رسلاً أفضل من الرسول الذي لا يكون أحد من أمته رسولاً. فثبت فضل الملائكة على البشر من هذه الجهة ولأن إبراهيم كان رسولاً إلى أخيه لوط، وكان أفضل منه، وموسى كان رسولاً إلى الأنبياء الذين كانوا في عسكره، وكان أفضل منهم فكذا ههنا.
The Sixth Proof: Angels are the messengers of God to the prophets, and the messenger is superior to the one to whom he is sent. The first premise: that angels are messengers of God to the prophets, based on His statement: 'Endowed with firmness, then he stood upright' (Quran 53:6), 'The Trustworthy Spirit descended with it upon your heart' (Quran 26:193-194), 'He sends down the angels with the spirit by His command upon whom He wills of His servants' (Quran 16:2). As for the second premise: that the messenger is superior to his nation, for two reasons: First: the human messenger is superior to his nation, so likewise here. If it is said: Convention is that if a sultan sends one person to a great assembly to be in charge of their affairs and judge among them, that person is superior to that assembly; but if he sends one person to a single person for the sake of notification, it appears that the messenger is of a lower status [؟], just as when a king sends his slave to the vizier. We say: This is refuted, because Jibril is sent to all prophets, and the messengers are from humans; so Jibril is the messenger and his nation is all the prophets. According to the rule mentioned by the questioner, it follows that Jibril is superior to them. The second reason: that angels are messengers of God, peace be upon them, based on His statement: 'Who makes the angels messengers' (Quran 35:1). The angel is either a messenger to another angel or a messenger to humans. In both cases, the angel is a messenger and his nation are also messengers. As for the human messenger, he is a messenger but his nation are not messengers. It is known that a messenger whose entire nation are messengers is superior to a messenger of whom none of his nation are messengers. Thus the superiority of angels over humans is established from this aspect, and because Ibrahim was a messenger to his brother Lut and was superior to him, and Musa was a messenger to the prophets in his army and was superior to them, so likewise here.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth proof, a complex argument based on the superiority of a messenger over those to whom he is sent. Imam Razi first establishes that angels are messengers to prophets (premise one) using Quranic verses. Then he argues that a messenger is superior to his nation (premise two) because human messengers are superior to their nations. An objection is raised: convention says a messenger sent to a single person (like a slave to a vizier) is lower in status. The answer rebuts by noting that Jibril is sent to all prophets, so his 'nation' includes all prophets, and by the objector's own logic, Jibril is superior. Then a second reason is given: angels are messengers, and their nation also consists of messengers (other angels or prophets who are also messengers), whereas human prophets have nations of non-messengers. Thus angelic messengers are superior. Additional analogies from Ibrahim and Musa reinforce the point.

Key Terms
رسول
روح أمين
جبريل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Angels are purely spiritual beings with no role as messengers to prophets.
Correction: The Quran explicitly describes angels as bearers of revelation to prophets, as seen in verses 53:6, 26:193-194, and 16:2.

Checkpoint
Which angel is specifically mentioned as the 'Trustworthy Spirit' in the verses cited?
A) Israfil
B) Mikail
C) Jibril
D) Ridwan

Key Takeaway
The first premise of the sixth proof is solidly grounded in Quranic texts that present angels as the bearers of revelation to prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Every verse of the Quran you recite was delivered by an angel to the Prophet's heart. Does this truth shape how you approach the Quran? Starting today, what will you do to honor this chain of transmission?
?
If angels are God's messengers, and the message they carry is the Quran, are you treating that message as urgent and life-giving? What concrete change in your daily routine can reflect that urgency?
?
The Trustworthy Spirit descended with the Quran upon the Prophet's heart. Do you trust that the same Quran, unchanged, is sufficient guidance for your life right now? What area of your life are you still reluctant to submit completely to its command?

Second Premise – First Reason: Messenger Superior to Nation and the Objection
Razi presents the second premise, its first proof, and an objection with refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second premise that a messenger is superior to his nation, its first proof using human messengers, and the objection and answer concerning the nature of the mission.

Core Idea
Even when a messenger is sent to a high-ranking individual, the scope of the mission determines status.

Imam Razi continues by asserting that a messenger is inherently superior to those he is sent to, drawing an analogy from human messengers. He then addresses an objection: what if a messenger is sent to a single high-ranking person? Through the example of Jibril sent to all prophets, he shows that the scale of the mission proves superiority.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text including the objection and answer.
Note the structure: premise, objection, answer.
2
Understand the first reason
Grasp the analogy: just as a human messenger is superior to his nation, so is an angelic messenger.
This is the initial argument.
3
Analyze the objection
The objection distinguishes between sending to a group (superior) vs. sending to a single person (inferior).
The example of a king sending a slave to a vizier is used.
4
See the refutation
Imam Razi refutes by showing that Jibril is sent to all prophets, not just one person, so he is like the messenger to a great assembly.
This turns the objection on its head.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

?

Second Premise – Second Reason: Angels' Nation of Messengers and Analogies
Razi offers a second reason: angels are messengers whose nations are also messengers, with analogies from Ibrahim and Musa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second reason for the superiority of angels: that angels are messengers whose nations are also messengers, and the analogies from Ibrahim and Musa.

Core Idea
An angelic messenger is superior to a human one because the angel's entire nation consists of messengers.

Imam Razi presents a second, more direct argument: angels are messengers, and their 'nations' (other angels or prophets) are also messengers. In contrast, human prophets are messengers but their nations are not. This, combined with examples of prophets sent to other prophets, solidifies the case for angelic superiority.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text for the second reason and the concluding analogies.
Notice the logical structure: classification, comparison, examples.
2
Understand the Quranic basis
The verse 'Who makes the angels messengers' (35:1) establishes angels as messengers.
This is the foundation.
3
Analyze the classification
Imam Razi classifies angelic missions: to other angels or to humans. In both cases, the angel is a messenger and his nation (the recipients) are also messengers.
This is the key contrast with human prophets.
4
Compare with human messengers
Human prophets are messengers, but their nations are not messengers. Hence angelic messengers are superior.
This is the direct argument.
5
Reflect on the analogies
Examples of Ibrahim and Musa being messengers to other prophets illustrate that a messenger sent to fellow prophets is superior.
These reinforce the general rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Sixth Proof: Angels are the messengers of God to the prophets, and the messenger is superior to the one to whom he is sent. The first premise: that angels are messengers of God to the prophets, based on His statement: 'Endowed with firmness, then he stood upright' (Quran 53:6), 'The Trustworthy Spirit descended with it upon your heart' (Quran 26:193-194), 'He sends down the angels with the spirit by His command upon whom He wills of His servants' (Quran 16:2). The angel is either a messenger to another angel or a messenger to humans. In both cases, the angel is a messenger and his nation are also messengers. As for the human messenger, he is a messenger but his nation are not messengers. It is known that a messenger whose entire nation are messengers is superior to a messenger of whom none of his nation are messengers. Thus the superiority of angels over humans is established from this aspect, and because Ibrahim was a messenger to his brother Lut and was superior to him, and Musa was a messenger to the prophets in his army and was superior to them, so likewise here.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth proof, a complex argument based on the superiority of a messenger over those to whom he is sent. Imam Razi first establishes that angels are messengers to prophets (premise one) using Quranic verses. Then he argues that a messenger is superior to his nation (premise two) because human messengers are superior to their nations. An objection is raised: convention says a messenger sent to a single person (like a slave to a vizier) is lower in status. The answer rebuts by noting that Jibril is sent to all prophets, so his 'nation' includes all prophets, and by the objector's own logic, Jibril is superior. Then a second reason is given: angels are messengers, and their nation also consists of messengers (other angels or prophets who are also messengers), whereas human prophets have nations of non-messengers. Thus angelic messengers are superior. Additional analogies from Ibrahim and Musa reinforce the point.

Key Terms
رسول
أمة
إبراهيم
موسى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the second reason, what makes angelic messengers superior to human prophets?
A) Angels are stronger than humans
B) Angels are sent to other angels only
C) An angel's nation are all messengers, whereas a human prophet's nation are not
D) Human prophets are not messengers

Key Takeaway
Angels are superior because they are messengers whose nations are also messengers, unlike human prophets, and this is further supported by examples of prophets sent to other prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You read that angels are superior because their entire nation are messengers. You, as a human, are not even a messenger, let alone having a nation of messengers. Do you feel humbled by your low rank? Or does this motivate you to strive to be among those who carry the message? How will you change your daily actions to reflect the honor of being from the nation of the Prophet (saw)?
?
Ibrahim was sent to Lut, and Musa to the prophets in his army. Both were superior to those they were sent to. In your life, you are sent as a believer to your family, friends, and community. Do you act with the awareness that you are an ambassador of truth, or do you lower yourself to please others? What specific situation will you correct starting today to embody the responsibility of being a carrier of the message?
?
The angel's entire nation are messengers. In contrast, your nation (the Muslim community) includes many who are not messengers. Does this reality make you appreciate the greater rank of angels? Or does it make you grateful that you are from a nation that at least has some messengers? How does this affect your conviction in the superiority of angels and your role in following them in obedience?

Angels Are More Pious Than Humans
Imam Razi argues for angelic superiority through piety.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational and scriptural argument that angels are more pious than humans, and why this implies their superiority over prophets in terms of piety.

Core Idea
Angels' constant fear of God makes them sinless, while prophets had minor faults.

Imam Razi presents a proof based on piety (taqwa). He argues that angels are free from all sins and even inclinations to sin, unlike prophets who had minor shortcomings. This distinction, supported by Quran and hadith, leads to the conclusion that angels are superior in piety.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the claim, the supporting evidence, and the conclusion.
The argument has three parts: claim of greater piety, evidence for angels, evidence for prophets, and the general principle linking piety to honor.
2
Identify the premises
Find the premises: (1) angels are free from slips and have constant fear; (2) prophets had minor sins or omissions; (3) the more pious is better (Quran 49:13).
3
Examine the scriptural evidence
Look at the Quranic verses for angels (16:50, 21:28) and the hadith about prophets. Understand how they support the premises.
The hadith mentions only Yahya ibn Zakariyya as sinless among prophets.
4
Understand the conclusion
Combine the premises: angels are more pious than prophets, and piety determines honor, so angels are superior in this aspect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة : الملائكة أتقى من البشر، والأتقى أفضل. إنما قلنا : إنهم أتقى لأنهم مبرؤون عن الزلات، وعن الميل إليها؛ لأن خوفهم دائم، قال تعالى : يَخَافُونَ رَبَّهُم مِّن فَوْقِهِمْ [النحل : ٥٠] وقال: وَهُم مِّنْ خَشْيَتِهِ مُشْفِقُونَ [الأنبياء : ٢٨] والخوف والإشفاق ينافيان العزم على المعصية، أما الأنبياء صلوات الله وسلامه عليهم فلم يخل أحد منهم عن شيء هو صغير أو ترك مندوب، قال صلوات الله وسلامه عليه : ما منا أحد إلا عصى أو هم بمعصية غير يحيى بن زكريا. إنما قلنا : إن الأتقى أفضل لقوله : إِنَّ أَكْرَمَكُمْ عِندَ اللَّهِ أَتْقَاكُمْ [الحجرات : ١٣]
The Seventh Proof: Angels are more pious than humans, and the more pious is better. We say: They are more pious because they are free from slips and from inclination towards them, because their fear is constant. He said: 'They fear their Lord above them' (Quran 16:50), and He said: 'And they are fearful of Him' (Quran 21:28). Fear and dread are incompatible with resolve to sin. As for the prophets, peace be upon them, none of them was free from something minor or from neglecting a recommended act. He said, peace be upon him: 'There is none among us but he sinned or intended a sin, except Yahya ibn Zakariyya.' We say: The more pious is better because of His statement: 'Indeed the most honored of you in the sight of God is the most pious of you' (Quran 49:13).
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh proof: angels are more pious (atqa) than humans. The reasoning: angels are sinless, free from slips and inclination to sin, because their constant fear of God prevents any resolve to disobey. This is supported by Quranic verses describing their fear and awe. In contrast, prophets, despite their high status, had minor faults or omissions (though not major sins). A hadith states that all humans except John the Baptist have sinned or intended sin. Thus angels are more pious. The conclusion that the more pious is superior is based on Quran 49:13, which links honor to piety. So angels are superior.

Key Terms
أتقى
زلات
خوف
خشية
معصية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That prophets are completely sinless and never commit any minor fault or omission.
Correction: This passage shows that prophets, except John the Baptist, had minor sins or omissions, while angels are completely free from any slip or inclination.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what distinguishes angels from prophets in terms of piety?
A) Angels never commit even minor faults or omit recommended acts
B) Angels are more knowledgeable
C) Prophets are not sinful at all
D) Angels are not fearful

Key Takeaway
Angels are more pious than humans because their constant fear of God prevents any sin, while prophets had minor faults, and piety determines honor.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If constant fear of God prevents sin, how often does that fear actually govern your daily choices? When was the last time it stopped you from a wrongdoing, and what does your answer say about the depth of your taqwa?
?
The prophets had minor faults, yet they are the best of creation. Are you using the excuse that 'minor sins don't matter' to neglect the struggle for piety? What small compromise have you made today that you need to confront tonight?
?
Angels' piety is constant; yours is intermittent. What would it take for you to live every moment conscious of God's presence? Are you willing to actually do that next time you face a temptation, and how will you remind yourself?
