Angels and the Celestial Hierarchy
Razi describes celestial structures and argues angelic superiority by analogy with physical domination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi uses the structure of the cosmos—spheres, planets, and stars—to argue for the superiority of angels over humans.

Core Idea
The cosmos is a hierarchy: upper structures dominate lower, so upper spirits dominate lower spirits.

Imam Razi presents his twenty-second argument for the superiority of angels by examining the celestial order. He describes the noble structures (planets and fixed stars) as the bodies of the spiritual realm, with angels as their spirits. By observing how celestial motions affect the lower world, he establishes a clear hierarchy that extends from physical structures to spiritual beings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Razi uses a layered description: spheres, stars, then spirits.
2
Identify the cosmic components
Find the description of the noble structures (planets, fixed stars), spheres as bodies, stars as hearts, and angels as spirits. Note the hierarchy.
This sets up the analogy for spiritual hierarchy.
3
Understand ratq and fatq
Razi introduces the concepts of closure (ratq) and opening (fatq) of the spheres' zones. Observe how these cause changes in the lower world—cessation or transfer of flourishing.
This demonstrates the influence of upper structures on the lower world.
4
Follow the analogy to spirits
Since upper structures dominate lower structures, Razi concludes that upper spirits must dominate lower spirits. Consider the logical step from physical hierarchy to spiritual hierarchy.
This is the core of the argument for angelic superiority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية والعشرون: الروحانيون مختصون بالهياكل الشريفة - وهي السيارات السبع وسائر الثوابت - والأفلاك لها كالأبدان والكواكب كالقلوب، والملائكة كالأرواح، ونسبة الأرواح إلى الأرواح كنسبة الأبدان إلى الأبدان، ثم إنا نعلم أن اختلاف أحوال الكواكب والأفلاك يتأدى لحصول الاختلافات في أحوال هذا العالم، فإنه يحصل من حركات الكواكب مناطق الأفلاك تارة ينطبق بعضها على بعض - وهو الرتق - وعنده تبطل عمارة العالم، وأخرى ينفصل بعضها عن بعض - وذلك هو الفتق - وعنده تنتقل العمارة في هذا العالم السفلي من جانب إلى جنب. فإذا رأينا أن هياكل العالم العلوي مسئولية على هياكل العالم السفلي فكذا أرواح العالم العلوي يجب أن تكون مستولية على أرواح العالم السفلي، لاسيما وقد دلت المباحث الفلسفية على أن أرواح هذا العالم معلولات أرواح العالم العلوي، ونسبة كمالات هذا العالم معلولات لكمال ذلك العالم، وكمالات هذه الأرواح إلى أرواح ذلك العالم وكمالاته كالشعلة الصغيرة بالنسبة إلى قرص الشمس، وكالقطرة الصغيرة في البحر الأعظم. وهذه الأرواح البشرية كالذرات وأما البحار والعيون والجبال والمعادن، فهي كالأرواح العلوية، فكيف يمكن أن يقابل أحدهما بالآخر ؟ فهذاه حكاية أدلة الفريقين في هذه المسألة على الاختصار.
The twenty-second argument: The spiritual beings are specialized with noble structures—that is the seven planets and the rest of the fixed stars—and the spheres are like bodies for them, and the stars are like hearts, and the angels are like spirits. And the relation of spirits to spirits is like the relation of bodies to bodies. Then we know that the differing states of the stars and spheres lead to differences in the states of this world, for from the movements of the stars the zones of the spheres sometimes overlap each other—that is closure (ratq)—and at that time the flourishing of the world ceases, and other times they separate from each other—that is opening (fatq)—and at that time flourishing transfers in this lower world from one side to another. So if we see that the structures of the upper world are dominant over the structures of the lower world, likewise the spirits of the upper world must be dominant over the spirits of the lower world, especially since philosophical investigations have shown that the spirits of this world are effects of the spirits of the upper world, and the relation of the perfections of this world is that they are effects of the perfections of that world, and the perfections of these spirits compared to the spirits of that world and its perfections are like a small flame compared to the disc of the sun, and like a small drop in the great ocean. And these human spirits are like atoms, while the seas, springs, mountains, and minerals are like the upper spirits. So how can one be compared to the other? This is the account of the proofs of the two groups on this issue in summary.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage presents the twenty-second argument for the superiority of angels. It is an argument from cosmic hierarchy and causation. Imam Razi begins by describing the structure of the celestial realm: angels are associated with noble structures—the seven planets and fixed stars. The spheres are like bodies, the stars like hearts, and the angels like spirits. The relationship between upper and lower spirits mirrors that between upper and lower bodies. He then introduces the astronomical concepts of ratq (closure) and fatq (opening), where the overlapping or separation of celestial spheres causes changes in the lower world—cessation or transfer of flourishing. Since the upper structures dominate the lower, so too must the upper spirits dominate the lower spirits. Philosophical investigations confirm that lower spirits are effects (ma'lulat) of upper spirits, and the perfections of the lower world depend on the perfections of the upper world. The disparity is likened to a small flame versus the sun, or a drop versus the ocean. Human spirits are compared to atoms, while upper spirits are like seas, mountains, etc. The argument concludes that the two are incomparable. This argument synthesizes cosmological observation with philosophical causation to establish a clear hierarchy.

Key Terms
الهياكل الشريفة
السيارات السبع
الرتق والفتق
الأرواح العلوية والسفلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the argument is purely philosophical and not grounded in observation.
Correction: Razi relies on observable celestial motions (ratq and fatq) and scriptural references to angels' roles, combining philosophy and cosmology.

Checkpoint
What do the terms 'ratq' and 'fatq' refer to in this argument?
A) The creation and destruction of stars
B) The overlapping and separation of celestial spheres
C) The birth and death of angels
D) The movement of planets around the sun

Key Takeaway
The physical hierarchy of the cosmos mirrors and justifies the spiritual hierarchy, with angels at the top.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the angels are as superior to you as the sun to a flame, how does this reshape your daily awareness of your own limitations and dependence on Allah's mercy? Will you today consciously remind yourself of your lowly status and seek refuge from arrogance?
?
Razi argues that your spirit is like an atom compared to the vastness of the upper spirits. How does this humble your ambitions when you strive for status or recognition? What one concrete action will you take today to lower yourself in humility before the unseen realities?
?
The hierarchy of spirits is mirrored in the physical world. If you truly believed that your deeds are witnessed by beings far superior, how would that change your private moments? Commit to one small act of obedience that only you and Allah (and His angels) know about.

The Causation and Analogy of Spiritual Perfection
Razi presents causal proofs and analogies for angelic superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi uses philosophical causation and vivid analogies to prove that angels' perfections far surpass human perfections.

Core Idea
Lower spirits are mere effects of upper spirits; their perfections are like a spark compared to the sun.

After establishing the physical hierarchy, Imam Razi deepens the argument with philosophical reasoning. He states that lower spirits are effects (ma'lulat) of upper spirits and that all perfections of the lower world derive from the upper. He employs striking analogies—a small flame versus the sun, a drop versus the ocean, atoms versus seas—to demonstrate the incomparable superiority of angelic spirits over human spirits.

Guided Path
1
Locate the causal claim
Find where Razi states that lower spirits are effects (ma'lulat) of upper spirits. This is a key philosophical premise.
The phrase 'معلولات أرواح العالم العلوي' indicates causation.
2
Understand the chain of perfections
Razi says the perfections of this world are effects of the perfections of the upper world. Consider how this establishes a dependent relationship.
Implication: lower perfections are derived and limited.
3
Analyze the analogies
Razi uses three analogies: a small flame to the sun, a small drop to the ocean, and human spirits as atoms to upper spirits as vast elements. Compare the scale.
The analogies emphasize vast disparity, not just difference.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The final rhetorical question 'how can one be compared to the other?' underscores the incomparability. Understand that this concludes the argument for angelic superiority.
The conclusion is that human and angelic perfections are categorically distinct.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية والعشرون: الروحانيون مختصون بالهياكل الشريفة - وهي السيارات السبع وسائر الثوابت - والأفلاك لها كالأبدان والكواكب كالقلوب، والملائكة كالأرواح، ونسبة الأرواح إلى الأرواح كنسبة الأبدان إلى الأبدان، ثم إنا نعلم أن اختلاف أحوال الكواكب والأفلاك يتأدى لحصول الاختلافات في أحوال هذا العالم، فإنه يحصل من حركات الكواكب مناطق الأفلاك تارة ينطبق بعضها على بعض - وهو الرتق - وعنده تبطل عمارة العالم، وأخرى ينفصل بعضها عن بعض - وذلك هو الفتق - وعنده تنتقل العمارة في هذا العالم السفلي من جانب إلى جنب. فإذا رأينا أن هياكل العالم العلوي مسئولية على هياكل العالم السفلي فكذا أرواح العالم العلوي يجب أن تكون مستولية على أرواح العالم السفلي، لاسيما وقد دلت المباحث الفلسفية على أن أرواح هذا العالم معلولات أرواح العالم العلوي، ونسبة كمالات هذا العالم معلولات لكمال ذلك العالم، وكمالات هذه الأرواح إلى أرواح ذلك العالم وكمالاته كالشعلة الصغيرة بالنسبة إلى قرص الشمس، وكالقطرة الصغيرة في البحر الأعظم. وهذه الأرواح البشرية كالذرات وأما البحار والعيون والجبال والمعادن، فهي كالأرواح العلوية، فكيف يمكن أن يقابل أحدهما بالآخر ؟ فهذاه حكاية أدلة الفريقين في هذه المسألة على الاختصار.
The twenty-second argument: The spiritual beings are specialized with noble structures—that is the seven planets and the rest of the fixed stars—and the spheres are like bodies for them, and the stars are like hearts, and the angels are like spirits. And the relation of spirits to spirits is like the relation of bodies to bodies. Then we know that the differing states of the stars and spheres lead to differences in the states of this world, for from the movements of the stars the zones of the spheres sometimes overlap each other—that is closure (ratq)—and at that time the flourishing of the world ceases, and other times they separate from each other—that is opening (fatq)—and at that time flourishing transfers in this lower world from one side to another. So if we see that the structures of the upper world are dominant over the structures of the lower world, likewise the spirits of the upper world must be dominant over the spirits of the lower world, especially since philosophical investigations have shown that the spirits of this world are effects of the spirits of the upper world, and the relation of the perfections of this world is that they are effects of the perfections of that world, and the perfections of these spirits compared to the spirits of that world and its perfections are like a small flame compared to the disc of the sun, and like a small drop in the great ocean. And these human spirits are like atoms, while the seas, springs, mountains, and minerals are like the upper spirits. So how can one be compared to the other? This is the account of the proofs of the two groups on this issue in summary.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage presents the twenty-second argument for the superiority of angels. It is an argument from cosmic hierarchy and causation. Imam Razi begins by describing the structure of the celestial realm: angels are associated with noble structures—the seven planets and fixed stars. The spheres are like bodies, the stars like hearts, and the angels like spirits. The relationship between upper and lower spirits mirrors that between upper and lower bodies. He then introduces the astronomical concepts of ratq (closure) and fatq (opening), where the overlapping or separation of celestial spheres causes changes in the lower world—cessation or transfer of flourishing. Since the upper structures dominate the lower, so too must the upper spirits dominate the lower spirits. Philosophical investigations confirm that lower spirits are effects (ma'lulat) of upper spirits, and the perfections of the lower world depend on the perfections of the upper world. The disparity is likened to a small flame versus the sun, or a drop versus the ocean. Human spirits are compared to atoms, while upper spirits are like seas, mountains, etc. The argument concludes that the two are incomparable. This argument synthesizes cosmological observation with philosophical causation to establish a clear hierarchy.

Key Terms
الأرواح العلوية والسفلية
معلولات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the argument is purely philosophical and not grounded in observation.
Correction: Razi relies on observable celestial motions (ratq and fatq) and scriptural references to angels' roles, combining philosophy and cosmology.

Checkpoint
What analogy does Imam Razi use to compare the perfections of human spirits to angelic spirits?
A) A small flame to the sun
B) A drop to the ocean
C) Atoms to vast elements
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The perfections of angels so exceed human perfections that comparison is impossible—like comparing a flame to the sun.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Razi compares your spiritual perfection to a small flame next to the sun. If you truly believed that, would you still feel proud of your spiritual achievements? What specific act of humility can you perform today to align with this reality?
?
The passage says your spirit is an effect of angelic spirits. Do you live as though you are utterly dependent on forces beyond your control, or do you act as if you are self-sufficient? What one change in your daily attitude would remind you of your place in the cosmic hierarchy?
?
The analogy of drop in the ocean is meant to show your insignificance. How does that make you feel about your sins and your worship? Are you still comfortable with sins that you think are 'small'? Will you repent of one specific sin today because you now see the immense gap between you and the angels?

First Proof for Miracles of Saints from Maryam's Story
Razi presents the first proof for saints' miracles and refutes an objection with three responses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Razi uses the story of Maryam (AS) as the first proof for the miracles of saints (karamat al-awliya) and how he refutes the objection that these events were prophetic miracles for Zakariyya (AS).

Core Idea
Maryam's miracles without prophethood prove that saints can perform miracles.

In this passage, Imam al-Razi begins the discussion on the miracles of saints by presenting his first proof. He draws from the well-known story of Maryam, who experienced extraordinary events—pregnancy without a male and provision without apparent cause—despite not being a prophet. After establishing that these are violations of custom, he anticipates and refutes an objection that these might have been miracles for the prophet of the time, Zakariyya. Through three logical arguments, he demonstrates why that objection is invalid, thereby supporting the Ash'ari position that saints can indeed perform miracles.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and the literal translation to get an overall sense of the argument.
Focus on the flow from the proof to the objection and the three responses.
2
Identify the core proof
Notice how Razi uses the two violations of custom in Maryam's life and the fact that she was not a prophet to argue for saintly miracles.
What makes this proof effective?
3
Analyze the objection and the three refutations
The objection suggests these events were miracles for Zakariyya. Razi gives three reasons why this is false. Read each one and understand the logic.
Pay attention to the conditions of a prophetic miracle that Razi lists.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this argument supports the broader Ash'ari doctrine of karamat al-awliya and counters the Mu'tazila denial.
This is one of three proofs Razi will present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الرابعة والثلاثون
في كرامات الأولياء
المعتزلة ينكرونها، ووافقهم الأستاذ أبو إسحاق من أصحابنا، وأكثر أصحابنا يثبتونها، وبه قال أبو الحسين البصري من المعتزلة.
لنا
وجوه ثلاثة :
الحجة الأولى : أن حدوث الحبل لمريم من غير الذكر من خوارق العادات، وحضور الرزق عندها من غير سبب ظاهر ومن خوارق العادات وأنها ما كانت من الأنبياء، فوجب أن يقال : إن هذه الوقائع من كرامات الأولياء.
فإن قيل : لم لا يجوز أن يقال: إن تلك الخوارق كانت معجزات لنبي ذلك الزمان، وهو زكريا ?
قلنا : هذا باطل لوجوه.
الأول : أن المعجزة لا بد أن تكون أمرًا ظاهرًا للمنكرين حتى يمكن الاستدلال بها على المنكر، وظهور جبريل لمريم وحبلها من غير ذكر، ما كان يطلع عليه أحد إلا مريم فكيف يمكن جعل هذه الأشياء معجزة لزكريا ؟
ثانيها : أن عند ظهور المعجز لبعض الأنبياء لا بد أن يكون الرسول حاضرًا، ولا بد أن يكون القوم حاضرين حتى يتمكن ذلك الرسول من الاستدلال بذلك المعجز، وفي الوقت الذي كان يقول جبريل لمريم : ﴿وَهُزَى إِلَيْكِ يجذع النَّخْلَةِ تسقط عليك رطباً جنتا﴾ [مريم : ٢٥] من كان زكريا حاضرًا هناك حتى يستدل بظهور هذه الخوارق على نبوة نفسه بل ما كان أحد من البشر هناك حاضراً، بدليل قوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِمَّا تَرَينَ مِنَ الْبَشَرِ أَحَدًا فَقُولِي إِنِّي نَذَرْتُ لِلرَّحْمَنِ صَوْمَال﴾ [مريم : ٢٦] فبطل القول بأن هذه الأشياء معجزة لزكريا .
ثالثها: أن حصول المعجز لا بد أن يكون بالتماس الرسول، وكان زكريا غافلا عن كيفية حدوث هذه الأشياء، بدليل قوله تعالى : ﴿كُلَّمَا دَخَلَ عَلَيْهَا زَكَرِيَّا﴾ [آل عمران: ٣٧] ...
The Thirty-Fourth Issue: On the Miracles of Saints. The Mu'tazila deny them, and al-Ustadh Abu Ishaq among our companions agreed with them. Most of our companions affirm them, and Abu al-Husayn al-Basri of the Mu'tazila also said so. We have three proofs: The first proof: That the occurrence of pregnancy for Maryam without a male is a violation of custom, and the provision coming to her without an apparent cause is a violation of custom, and she was not among the prophets. Therefore, it must be said that these events are among the miracles of saints. If it is said: Why is it not permissible to say that those violations were miracles for the prophet of that time, namely Zakariyya? We say: This is false for reasons. First: A miracle must be a matter manifest to the deniers so that it can be used as evidence against the denier. The appearance of Jibril to Maryam and her pregnancy without a male were not witnessed by anyone except Maryam. So how can these things be made a miracle for Zakariyya? Second: When a miracle appears for a certain prophet, the messenger must be present, and the people must be present so that that messenger can use that miracle as evidence. At the time when Jibril said to Maryam: 'And shake toward yourself the trunk of the palm tree; it will drop upon you fresh, ripe dates' [Maryam:25], was Zakariyya present there to use the appearance of these violations as evidence for his own prophethood? Rather, there was no human being present there, as evidenced by His saying: 'So if you see any human, say: Indeed, I have vowed to the Most Merciful a fast' [Maryam:26]. So the claim that these things are miracles for Zakariyya is invalid. Third: The occurrence of a miracle must be at the request of the messenger, and Zakariyya was unaware of how these things happened, as evidenced by His saying: 'Every time Zakariyya entered upon her in the sanctuary' [Aal-Imran:37]...
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage opens the Thirty-Fourth Issue on the miracles of saints (karamat al-awliya). Razi first states the positions: the Mu'tazila deny them, and among the Ash'aris, Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini agreed with them, but the majority of Ash'aris affirm them, and even the Mu'tazilite Abu al-Husayn al-Basri affirmed them. Then Razi presents three proofs. The first proof is based on the story of Maryam. Maryam experienced two violations of custom (khawariq al-'adat): becoming pregnant without a male, and receiving provision without an apparent cause. Maryam was not a prophet, so if these violations are not considered prophetic miracles, they must be considered saintly miracles. Razi then anticipates an objection: could these not be miracles for the prophet of the time, Zakariyya? He refutes this with three points. First, a miracle must be manifest to deniers; but Maryam's experiences were private, known only to her. Second, a miracle requires the prophet and his audience to be present so the prophet can use it as evidence; but when Jibril came to Maryam and she gave birth, no one else was present, as the Quran indicates by commanding her to say she vowed a fast if she sees any human. Third, a miracle must be at the prophet's request; Zakariyya was unaware of these events, as the Quran shows him entering her sanctuary and finding provision, not requesting it. The text ends mid-sentence in the third refutation.

Key Terms
كرامات الأولياء
معجزات
خوارق العادات
المعتزلة
أبو إسحاق
مريم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that any violation of custom must be a prophetic miracle.
Correction: Razi shows that it can be a saintly miracle if the person is not a prophet, as in the case of Maryam.

Checkpoint
Why does Razi present the story of Maryam as evidence for the miracles of saints?
A) Because Maryam was a prophet and her miracles prove prophecy.
B) Because Maryam experienced violations of custom despite not being a prophet.
C) Because Maryam's miracles were witnessed by many people.
D) Because Maryam was a companion of Zakariyya.

Key Takeaway
Maryam's story provides a clear example of saintly miracles, as she experienced violations of custom without being a prophet, and these cannot be attributed to Zakariyya for three reasons.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Maryam's miracles were private—known only to her—does it challenge your need for public recognition in your own acts of devotion? Are you willing to serve Allah even if no one ever sees your sacrifice?
?
Razi argues that a miracle must be manifest to deniers to serve as evidence. In your own life, are you more concerned with appearing righteous to others (deniers or not) than with the hidden reality of your faith that only Allah sees?
?
If Maryam, a non-prophet, could experience such profound interventions from Allah, what does that say about your own potential for divine closeness? Are you living as if you expect Allah to support you in extraordinary ways, or have you settled for a mundane faith?

The Ash'ari Position on Reward and the First Proof
Al-Razi states the Ash'ari view and gives the first proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari argument that no one has a right over God and the first proof based on the obligation of gratitude.

Core Idea
Past blessings obligate obedience; fulfilling an obligation cannot create a new right.

Al-Razi introduces the Ash'ari stance on reward by contrasting it with the Mu'tazili view. The first proof rests on a logical point: if God's blessings already obligate gratitude and obedience, then performing that obedience cannot be a cause for deserving additional reward. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
The passage is from the Thirty-Fifth Issue on reward and punishment. Al-Razi first states the basic ruling: obedient people are rewarded by Allah. Then he contrasts the Mu'tazili claim that obedience is a cause for deserving reward with the Ash'ari view that no one has a right over God.
2
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Note key terms: ثواب, عقاب, طاعة, استحقاق, حق, إنعام, شكر.
3
Analyze the first proof
Focus on the logic: Allah's past blessings obligate the servant to obedience and gratitude. Since performing an obligation cannot be a cause for something else, obedience cannot be a cause for deserving reward.
The proof uses the Quranic verse from Ibrahim 14:34.
4
Contrast with Mu'tazili view
Understand why the Mu'tazili view is problematic according to Ash'aris: it implies that humans have a claim on God, which is denied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الخامسة والثلاثون وفيها فصول : في أحكام الثواب والعقاب الفصل الأول : في حكم الثواب والعقاب اعلم أن المكلف إما أن يكون مطيعا أو عاصيًا، فإن كان مطيعا فالله تعالى يثيبه، وزعم البصريون من المعتزلة أن أداء الطاعة علة لاستحقاق الثواب على الله تعالى. ومذهبنا أنه ليس لأحد على الله تعالى حق لنا وجوه : · الحجة الأولى : أن الإنعام يوجب على المنعم عليه الاشتغال بالشكر والخدمة، ونعم الله تعالى على العبد في الماضي وفي الحاضر كثيرة خارجة عن الحصر والإحصاء، كما قال تعالى: ﴿ وَإِن تَعُدُّوا نِعْمَتَ اللَّهِ لَا تُحْصُوهَا ﴾ [إبراهيم: ٣٤] وإذا كان كذلك فتلك النعم السالفة توجب على العبد الاشتغال بالطاعة وبالشكر، وأداء الواجب لا يكون سببًا لاستحقاق شيء آخر، فوجب أن لا يكون اشتغال العبد بالطاعة سببًا لاستحقاق الثواب على الله تعالى.
The Thirty-Fifth Issue, comprising chapters on the rulings of reward and punishment. Chapter One: On the ruling of reward and punishment. Know that the legally responsible person is either obedient or disobedient. If he is obedient, then Allah Most High rewards him. The Basran Mu'tazilites claimed that performing obedience is a cause for deserving reward from Allah Most High. Our school is that no one has a right over Allah Most High. For us there are proofs: The first proof: That bestowal of blessings obligates the recipient to engage in gratitude and service, and the blessings of Allah Most High upon the servant in the past and present are many, beyond enumeration and counting, as He said: 'And if you count the blessings of Allah, you cannot enumerate them.' [Ibrahim: 34]. If that is so, then those past blessings obligate the servant to engage in obedience and gratitude, and performing an obligation is not a cause for deserving something else. Therefore, the servant's engagement in obedience should not be a cause for deserving reward from Allah Most High.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage introduces the Thirty-Fifth Issue on reward and punishment, specifically the first chapter on the ruling of reward. Al-Razi begins by stating that the morally responsible person is either obedient or disobedient; if obedient, Allah rewards him. He then contrasts the Mu'tazili view (Basran school) that performing obedience is a cause ('illah) for deserving (istihqāq) reward from Allah, with the Ash'ari position that no one has a right (haqq) over Allah. The first proof (al-ḥujjah al-ūlā) argues that Allah's past and present blessings obligate the servant to gratitude and obedience, not to deserve further reward. Since the servant already owes obedience for previous blessings, fulfilling that duty cannot create a new entitlement. Thus, obedience is not a cause for deserving reward from Allah.

Key Terms
ثواب
عقاب
طاعة
معصية
استحقاق
حق
إنعام
شكر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God is obligated to reward the obedient because obedience is good and deserves reward.
Correction: Ash'aris argue that God is not obligated by anyone's actions; rather, past blessings already obligate us, so obedience cannot be a cause for deserving reward.

Checkpoint
What is the foundation of al-Razi's first proof against the Mu'tazili view on reward?
A) That obedience cannot be a cause for reward because reward is a gift, not an obligation.
B) That Allah's past blessings already obligate obedience, so performing obedience does not create a new right to reward.
C) That the Mu'tazili view implies injustice on God's part.
D) That the Quran states reward is only in the afterlife.

Key Takeaway
The first Ash'ari proof for reward not being obligatory on God is that past blessings already obligate obedience, so performing obedience cannot create a new right to reward.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform acts of worship, do you ever feel that God owes you something in return? How does this lesson challenge that feeling, and what would it mean to truly let go of that transactional mindset?
?
Think of the countless blessings you have received from God since birth. How many of them have you adequately thanked Him for? Does the realization that you are already in debt change how you view your obedience – not as earning reward, but as paying back an unpayable debt?
?
If obedience does not 'earn' you reward, then why do you obey? Does this truth free you from a transactional relationship with Allah, or does it leave you uncomfortable? What needs to change in your heart so that your obedience springs from gratitude rather than from a desire to claim something?

Second Argument: Only Deniers Enter Hell
Razi presents a Qur'anic proof that only deniers enter Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses the Qur'anic dialogue of Hell's keepers to prove that only deniers of prophets enter Hell.

Core Idea
Hell's inhabitants confess: we denied the warner, so only deniers are there.

Razi now turns to a direct Qur'anic proof to show that Hell is reserved for those who reject the messengers. He cites the scene where the keepers of Hell question each incoming group, and every group replies that they denied the warner who came to them. This universal confession, Razi argues, establishes that only deniers enter Hell.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic text of the verse and Razi's commentary once without translating. Notice the key words: فوج, نذير, كذبناهم.
The verse is from Surah al-Mulk.
2
Understand the logic of the argument
Razi claims that the verse states 'every group' that enters Hell says the same thing: a warner came but we denied him. If every group says this, then every person in Hell is a denier.
3
Reflect on the implication
If only deniers enter Hell, then believers—even sinful ones—do not enter Hell. This is a key point in Razi's defense of the view that major sinners among believers are not in Hell forever.
This argument addresses a specific theological dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحجة الثانية : قوله تعالى : ﴿وَكُلَّمَا أُلْقِيَ فِيهَا فَوْجٌ سَأَلَهُمْ خَزَنَتُهَا أَلَمْ يَأْتِكُمْ نَذِيرٌ قَالُوا بَلَى قَدْ جَاءَنَا نَذِيرٌ فَكَذَّبْنَا وَقُلْنَا مَا نَزَّلَ اللَّهُ مِنْ شَيْءٍ﴾ [الملك: 8-9] أخبر الله تعالى أن كل فوج يدخل النار فإنهم يقولون : قد جاءنا نذير ولكن كذبناه وهذا صريح في أن كل من دخل النار كان مكذبًا بأنبياء الله تعالى، فيقتضي أن من لم يكن كذلك لم يدخل النار.
And the second proof: His saying, the Most High: 'And whenever a group is thrown into it, its keepers ask them, 'Did no warner come to you?' They say, 'Yes, a warner came to us, but we denied and said, 'Allah has not sent down anything.'' [al-Mulk 67:8-9] Allah the Most High informed that every group that enters Hell, they say: 'A warner came to us but we denied him.' This is explicit that everyone who entered Hell was a denier of the prophets of Allah, and it implies that whoever was not like that did not enter Hell.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage presents a Qur'anic argument proving that Hell-fire is exclusively for those who deny the prophets. Razi cites the verse where the keepers of Hell ask every incoming group: 'Did no warner come to you?' and they reply that a warner came but they denied him. Razi points out that this dialogue is described for every group entering Hell, which shows that every inhabitant of Hell is a denier (mukadhdhib) of Allah's prophets. Therefore, anyone who is not a denier – i.e., a believer, even if sinful – cannot enter Hell. The argument hinges on the universality of the statement: all who enter Hell confess to having denied the warner.

Key Terms
الحجة
النار
التكذيب
الأنبياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this verse only refers to a specific group of disbelievers, not all people in Hell.
Correction: Razi uses the general wording 'every group' (كل فوج) to show it applies universally to all who enter Hell.

Checkpoint
According to this argument, what do all who enter Hell admit?
A) They were believers but sinned
B) A warner came but they denied him
C) They never received a warner
D) They repented before death

Key Takeaway
The Qur'anic testimony of every group entering Hell confirms that only deniers of prophets enter Hell.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, do you ever find yourself denying Allah's warnings through your actions? When was the last time you ignored a clear sign from Allah, treating it as if it were not from Him? What will you do this week to heed a warning you have been ignoring?
?
The people of Hell confessed that a warner came to them but they denied him. Is there a truth about Islam that you have heard repeatedly but still resist applying? If you were asked by the keepers of Hell today, could you honestly say you did not receive a warner?
?
Only deniers enter Hell. This means that as long as you have faith (iman), you are not among them. But does your faith make you feel secure? Or does it drive you to obey Allah more urgently? What is one area where your actions do not match your belief that you will change today?

Third Argument: The Blazing Fire Is for Deniers
Razi argues from Quran 92:14-16 that the blazing fire is only for deniers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi uses the attribute of 'blazing' to generalize a Quranic verse about a specific fire to all hellfires, thereby excluding sinful believers from eternal punishment.

Core Idea
The blazing fire is for deniers only, not for sinful believers.

Imam Razi continues his proofs for the fate of sinners by citing a Quranic verse that describes a blazing fire reserved for the most wretched. However, he anticipates an objection: perhaps this verse refers only to a particular fire, not to all hellfires. In this lesson, we will see how Razi responds by focusing on the attribute of 'blazing' to argue that all hellfires share this quality, and thus the verse applies universally to disbelievers.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse and its translation
Start by reading the verse (92:14-16) in Arabic and English. Notice the terms 'blazing fire' and 'most wretched' that Razi uses as his proof.
The verse explicitly links the fire to denial and turning away.
2
Identify the objection Razi addresses
Razi presents an objection: perhaps the verse only refers to a specific fire, not all hellfires. Understand why this objection could undermine the argument.
If true, the verse would not apply to all disbelievers.
3
Analyze Razi's response
Razi argues that all hellfires are blazing, and the verse indicates that the blazing fire afflicts disbelievers. See how he extends the ruling to all hellfires.
He uses the attribute 'blazing' as a common property.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The desired conclusion is that only deniers enter any blazing fire, so sinful believers are excluded. Confirm how this supports Razi's broader theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحجة الثالثة : قوله تعالى: ﴿فَأَنذَرْتُكُمْ نَارًا تَلَظَّى لَا يَصْلَاهَا إِلَّا الْأَشْقَى الَّذِي كَذَّبَ وَتَوَلَّى﴾ [الليل: 14-16] ولا يقال : قوله تعالى : فأَنذرتكم نارا تلفى [الليل: 14] نار مخصوصة، وهي مختصة بالأشقى الَّذِى كَذَّبَ وَتَوَلَّى [الليل: 16] فلم قلتم : إن سائر النيران لا يدخلها فساق أهل الصلاة؟ لأنا نقول : النيران لا بد أن تكون متلظية والآية دلت على أن النار المتلظية تصيب الكفار، وحينئذ يحصل المطلوب.
And the third proof: His saying, the Most High: 'So I have warned you of a blazing fire. None shall enter it except the most wretched, who denies and turns away.' [al-Layl 92:14-16] And it is not said: His saying 'I have warned you of a fire' [al-Layl 92:14] refers to a specific fire, which is specific to the most wretched who denies and turns away [al-Layl 92:16] – so why do you say that other fires do not enter them the sinful among the people of prayer? For we say: All fires must be blazing, and the verse indicates that the blazing fire afflicts the disbelievers, and then the desired conclusion is obtained.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage presents a proof from the verse that a specific blazing fire is reserved for the most wretched who denied and turned away. Razi anticipates an objection: perhaps this verse refers only to a particular fire, not to all hellfires. He answers that all hellfires are necessarily blazing, and the verse indicates that the blazing fire afflicts the disbelievers. Thus, by extension, any fire that is blazing afflicts only disbelievers, so sinful believers who do not deny are excluded. The argument relies on the attribute 'blazing' being characteristic of all hellfires.

Key Terms
النار المتلظية
الأشقى
التكذيب
التولي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the verse only speaks about a particular fire, so sinful believers could still enter other hellfires.
Correction: Razi shows that all hellfires are 'blazing,' and the verse uses that attribute, so the ruling applies universally.

Checkpoint
What attribute of hellfire does Razi use to generalize the verse?
A) It is eternal
B) It is blazing
C) It is painful
D) It is dark

Key Takeaway
Razi uses the attribute 'blazing' to show that the Quranic verse about a specific fire covers all hellfires, excluding sinful believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The verse describes the 'most wretched' as those who deny and turn away. When you read the Quran or hear reminders, do you ever catch yourself mentally rejecting or ignoring what is hard for you to accept? Is there an area of your life where you are 'turning away' rather than submitting? What will you do today to face it?
?
Razi's argument comforts believers that they are not destined for the blazing fire. But does this comfort make you complacent? Reflect: Is your faith alive? What signs in your life prove you are truly a believer, not just someone who hopes to be saved without effort? Ask Allah to strengthen your faith and save you from hypocrisy.

Fourth Argument: Disgrace and Hell
Razi's fourth argument: disgrace only for disbelievers => Hell only for disbelievers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses two Quranic verses to argue that only disbelievers will enter Hell, based on the concept of disgrace.

Core Idea
Disgrace is exclusive to disbelievers, and Hell entails disgrace.

Imam Razi presents a concise syllogism grounded in Quranic verses. He establishes that disgrace (al-khizy) is a punishment specifically for disbelievers. Then, through another verse, he shows that entering Hell necessarily involves disgrace. Therefore, Hell must be reserved for disbelievers alone.

Guided Path
1
Read the two verses
Read the Arabic verses from Surah al-Nahl and Surah Aal-e-Imran. Notice how they are used as premises.
The first verse emphasizes disgrace upon disbelievers; the second links Hell to disgrace.
2
Understand the logical connection
Identify the major premise (disgrace for disbelievers) and minor premise (Hell brings disgrace) to reach the conclusion.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this argument is important for the doctrine of the afterlife.
This argument reinforces that believers will not be eternally punished.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحجة الرابعة : إِنَّ الْخِزْيَ الْيَوْمَ وَالسُّوءَ عَلَى الْكَافِرِينَ [النحل: 27] دلت هذه الآية على اختصاص الخزي بالكافرين، ثم إن كل من دخل النار فقد حصل له الخزي لقوله تعالى : ﴿رَبَّنَا إِنَّكَ مَن تُدْخِلِ النَّارَ فَقَدْ أَخْزَيْتَهُ﴾ [آل عمران: 192] ولما لم يحصل الخزي إلا للكافرين وجب أن لا يحصل دخول النار إلا لهم.
And the fourth proof: 'Indeed, disgrace today and evil are upon the disbelievers' [al-Nahl 16:27]. This verse indicates that disgrace is specific to disbelievers. Then, everyone who enters Hell has certainly incurred disgrace, due to His saying, the Most High: 'Our Lord, indeed whoever You admit to the Fire, You have disgraced him' [Aal-e-Imran 3:192]. Since disgrace is not incurred except by disbelievers, it follows that entering the Fire does not occur except for them.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
Razi combines two verses: one states that disgrace (al-khizy) is exclusively for disbelievers; another states that anyone admitted to Hell is disgraced. Therefore, only disbelievers can enter Hell, because if a believer entered Hell, he would be disgraced, but disgrace is only for disbelievers. This is a syllogism: major premise – disgrace is only for disbelievers; minor premise – entering Hell entails disgrace; conclusion – entering Hell is only for disbelievers.

Key Terms
الخزي
السوء
الكافرون
دخول النار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Believers who enter Hell temporarily might also be disgraced.
Correction: The Qur'an states that disgrace is specifically upon disbelievers (Surah al-Nahl 16:27). Since entering Hell entails disgrace, believers cannot enter Hell because that would contradict the exclusivity of disgrace.

Checkpoint
According to this argument, what is the relationship between entering Hell and disgrace?
A) Entering Hell causes disgrace
B) Disgrace causes entering Hell
C) They are unrelated
D) Entering Hell prevents disgrace

Key Takeaway
Razi uses the exclusive nature of disgrace and the disgrace of Hell to prove that only disbelievers will enter Hell.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Disgrace is exclusive to disbelievers. When you sin, do you ever feel a sense of disgrace that should drive you to repent, or do you become comfortable with it? How does this verse from al-Nahl make you reconsider your own state of faith?
?
The believers' prayer in Aal-e-Imran acknowledges that anyone admitted to the Fire has been disgraced. Do you truly fear that disgrace enough to avoid sins that could lead to Hell? What specific habit in your life right now contradicts this fear?
?
Razi uses logic to prove that believers will never enter Hell. Is your heart at peace with this guarantee, or does it make you complacent? How should this assurance change how you live today?

Fifth Argument: Forgiveness of All Sins Without Repentance
Razi argues from a general verse that forgiveness can be without repentance, then addresses an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses the verse 'Forgive all sins' to argue that forgiveness can occur without repentance, and how he addresses the objection that this includes disbelief.

Core Idea
A general verse can imply forgiveness without repentance, but it may be specified by stronger texts.

Razi begins his fifth argument by citing a powerful verse that promises forgiveness for all sins without any condition of repentance. An immediate objection arises: does this mean even disbelief is forgiven? Razi's response shows the sophistication of theological reasoning when general verses meet specific ones.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and its implication
Read the Arabic of verse 39:53 and its translation. Notice that it says 'forgives all sins' without mentioning repentance. Ask yourself: what does this imply about the necessity of repentance?
2
Understand the objection
The objection is that if the verse covers all sins, it would include disbelief (kufr). But we know from other texts that disbelief is not forgiven without repentance. How can Razi reconcile this?
3
Follow Razi's response
Razi gives two responses: (1) the general statement can be specified by other evidence, leaving the rest valid; (2) the word 'servants' in the verse is often limited to believers, so the verse applies to believers only.
Notice how Razi uses linguistic and contextual arguments.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how this argument supports the possibility of forgiveness without repentance for sins other than shirk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة : قوله تعالى: ﴿يَا عِبَادِيَ الَّذِينَ أَسْرَفُوا عَلَى أَنفُسِهِمْ لَا تَقْنَطُوا مِن رَحْمَةِ اللَّهِ إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَغْفِرُ الذُّنُوبَ جَمِيعاً﴾ [الزمر: 53] حكم بغفران الذنوب جميعا، ولم يشترط فيه التوبة وذلك يدل على أنه تعالى يغفر الذنوب جميعا قبل التوبة وبعدها، فإن قيل : فيلزم من دلالتها مغفرة الكفر لأنه من الذنوب قلنا هب أن هذا العام دخله هذا : التخصيص، فيبقى فيما عداه حجة، وأيضًا لفظ العباد في القرآن مخصوص بالمؤمنين، قال تعالى : ﴿عَيْنًا يَشْرَبُ بِهَا عِبَادُ اللَّهِ﴾ [الإنسان: 6] الحجة السادسة : قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنَّ رَبَّكَ لَذُو مَغْفِرَةٍ لِلنَّاسِ عَلَى ظُلْمِهِمْ﴾ [الرعد: 6] وكلمة "على" تفيد الحال كقولك : رأيت الأمير على أكله، أي رأيته حال أكله، فكذا ههنا دلت الآية على أنه تعالى يغفر لهم حال اشتغالهم بالظلم، وحال اشتغالهم بالظلم يمنع حصول التوبة، فعلمنا أنه يحصل الغفران بدون التوبة، فيقتضي هذا الدليل حصول الغفران للمشرك ؛ لأن الشرك ظلم، بدليل قوله تعالى : ﴿إِنَّ الشِّرْكَ لَظُلْمٌ عَظِيمٌ﴾ [لقمان: 13] إلا أنه ترك العمل به لقوله تعالى : ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَن يُشْرَكَ بِهِ﴾ [النساء: 48] فيبقى حجة فيما عداه، والفرق أن الكفر أعظم حالا من المعصية.
The fifth proof: His saying, the Most High: 'O My servants who have transgressed against themselves, do not despair of the mercy of Allah. Indeed, Allah forgives all sins' [al-Zumar 39:53]. It rules forgiveness of all sins and does not stipulate repentance, and that indicates that He forgives all sins before repentance and after it. If it is said: This would entail forgiveness of disbelief because it is among the sins. We say: Even if this general statement includes this specification, it remains a proof for what is beyond it. Also, the word 'servants' in the Qur'an is specific to believers, as He said: 'A spring from which the servants of Allah drink' [al-Insan 76:6]. The sixth proof: His saying, the Most High: 'And indeed, your Lord is full of forgiveness for the people despite their wrongdoing' [al-Ra'd 13:6]. The word 'on' (على) indicates accompaniment, like your saying: I saw the prince while he was eating, i.e., I saw him in the state of his eating. So likewise here, the verse indicates that He forgives them while they are engaged in wrongdoing, and being engaged in wrongdoing prevents the occurrence of repentance. Thus we know that forgiveness occurs without repentance. This proof necessitates forgiveness for the polytheist because polytheism is wrongdoing, as per His saying: 'Indeed, polytheism is a great wrongdoing' [Luqman 31:13]. However, it is not acted upon due to His saying: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him' [al-Nisa 4:48]. So it remains a proof for what is beyond that. The difference is that disbelief is a greater state than disobedience.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage combines two closely related arguments. In the fifth argument, Razi cites the verse that says Allah forgives all sins without stipulating repentance, which implies that forgiveness can occur without repentance. An objection is raised: this would include forgiveness of disbelief. Razi answers that this general statement may be specified (excluding disbelief) by other texts (like 4:48), but remains valid for lesser sins. He also notes that the word 'servants' in the verse is often specific to believers, as in 76:6. In the sixth argument, Razi uses the verse where forgiveness is given 'on' (على) their wrongdoing, which he interprets as 'while' they are doing wrong, meaning forgiveness is granted at the very moment of sin, which precludes repentance. Thus, repentance is not required. Again, this would even include polytheists, but that is excluded by the specific verse 4:48. Razi concludes that the argument remains valid for sins other than shirk. The final line notes the distinction: disbelief is a more severe state than mere disobedience.

Key Terms
الغفران
التوبة
الذنوب
العموم
التخصيص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'forgives all sins' means that everyone, including disbelievers, is forgiven without any condition.
Correction: Razi shows that the general statement is specified by other texts (like 4:48) and the address is limited to believers, so it does not apply to shirk.

Checkpoint
What does Razi use to argue that the verse 'forgives all sins' does not include disbelief?
A) The word 'servants' is specific to believers
B) The verse is abrogated
C) Repentance is a condition in all verses
D) Disbelief is not a sin

Key Takeaway
A general verse can imply forgiveness without repentance, but it must be interpreted in light of other texts and context.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have heard that Allah forgives all sins. But have you ever knowingly delayed repentance, assuming His mercy will cover you regardless? Is that not a dangerous presumption that this verse warns against when properly understood? Will you commit to repenting promptly, without relying on the general wording alone?
?
When you read 'O My servants who have transgressed against themselves', do you see yourself as that servant? And if so, does the verse give you comfort or does it demand that you not despair? But what if you are not truly His servant in the sense of belief? Examine your heart: are you among those addressed? If not, what must you change?
?
Razi shows that a general verse can be limited by other texts. How often do you cherry-pick verses that suit your desires while ignoring the clarifying ones? Will you commit to reading the Quran holistically, not selectively, and accept its full guidance even when it challenges your assumptions?

Sixth Argument: Forgiveness During Wrongdoing
Razi interprets a preposition to argue that forgiveness occurs during the sin, thus without repentance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi interprets the word 'on' in verse 13:6 to mean accompaniment, proving that forgiveness can occur while one is sinning, thus without repentance.

Core Idea
The word 'on' can indicate simultaneous action, showing forgiveness without repentance.

Razi's sixth argument uses a subtle linguistic point: the preposition 'on' (على) in the verse about forgiveness for wrongdoing indicates the state of doing wrong. This suggests forgiveness is granted at the very moment of sin, making repentance impossible at that moment. Again, Razi must address the problem of polytheism.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and its key word
Read verse 13:6: 'Your Lord is full of forgiveness for the people despite their wrongdoing.' Focus on the word 'on' (على). Razi interprets it as meaning 'while' or 'in the state of'.
Compare with the example: 'I saw the prince on his eating' meaning 'while eating'.
2
Understand the implication
If forgiveness happens while they are doing wrong, then they are not repenting at that moment. Thus forgiveness is without repentance.
3
Follow the objection and response
The objection: this would include polytheists because shirk is wrongdoing. Razi concedes this, but says it is excluded by the explicit verse 4:48. So the argument stands for other sins.
Razi also notes the difference: disbelief is a greater state than disobedience.
4
Reflect on the method
Observe how Razi uses linguistic analysis (the meaning of 'على') to derive theological conclusions. This is a hallmark of kalam reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة : قوله تعالى: ﴿يَا عِبَادِيَ الَّذِينَ أَسْرَفُوا عَلَى أَنفُسِهِمْ لَا تَقْنَطُوا مِن رَحْمَةِ اللَّهِ إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَغْفِرُ الذُّنُوبَ جَمِيعاً﴾ [الزمر: 53] حكم بغفران الذنوب جميعا، ولم يشترط فيه التوبة وذلك يدل على أنه تعالى يغفر الذنوب جميعا قبل التوبة وبعدها، فإن قيل : فيلزم من دلالتها مغفرة الكفر لأنه من الذنوب قلنا هب أن هذا العام دخله هذا : التخصيص، فيبقى فيما عداه حجة، وأيضًا لفظ العباد في القرآن مخصوص بالمؤمنين، قال تعالى : ﴿عَيْنًا يَشْرَبُ بِهَا عِبَادُ اللَّهِ﴾ [الإنسان: 6] الحجة السادسة : قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنَّ رَبَّكَ لَذُو مَغْفِرَةٍ لِلنَّاسِ عَلَى ظُلْمِهِمْ﴾ [الرعد: 6] وكلمة "على" تفيد الحال كقولك : رأيت الأمير على أكله، أي رأيته حال أكله، فكذا ههنا دلت الآية على أنه تعالى يغفر لهم حال اشتغالهم بالظلم، وحال اشتغالهم بالظلم يمنع حصول التوبة، فعلمنا أنه يحصل الغفران بدون التوبة، فيقتضي هذا الدليل حصول الغفران للمشرك ؛ لأن الشرك ظلم، بدليل قوله تعالى : ﴿إِنَّ الشِّرْكَ لَظُلْمٌ عَظِيمٌ﴾ [لقمان: 13] إلا أنه ترك العمل به لقوله تعالى : ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَن يُشْرَكَ بِهِ﴾ [النساء: 48] فيبقى حجة فيما عداه، والفرق أن الكفر أعظم حالا من المعصية.
The fifth proof: His saying, the Most High: 'O My servants who have transgressed against themselves, do not despair of the mercy of Allah. Indeed, Allah forgives all sins' [al-Zumar 39:53]. However, it is not acted upon due to His saying: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him' [al-Nisa 4:48]. So it remains a proof for what is beyond that. Key Takeaway
A careful reading of a preposition can reveal that forgiveness is granted at the moment of sin, without requiring repentance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Razi's argument shows that forgiveness can happen without repentance for some sins. Does this truth comfort you or alarm you? Are you using it as an excuse to delay repentance, or does it drive you to seek His forgiveness more earnestly?
?
The argument excludes shirk. Do you treat other sins lightly, thinking they will be forgiven anyway, while ignoring the severity of even a single act of disobedience that challenges His lordship? What would it take for you to truly hate the sin you are currently committing?

Seventh Argument: Recompense Only for the Ungrateful
Razi argues that punishment is only for extreme disbelievers using an intensive form.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that divine recompense (punishment) is reserved for the extreme disbeliever (original disbeliever), and how he resolves apparent conflict with other verses.

Core Idea
Recompense is only for the extreme ingrate, not the sinful believer.

Razi presents a proof based on a Qur'anic verse that uses an intensive form, restricting punishment to the most severe category of disbelief. He then anticipates an objection from another verse that seems more universal. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and his principle of giving precedence to forgiveness.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and translation
Read the Arabic verse (Saba 34:17) and its translation. Notice the word 'الكفور' (al-kafur).
This is the proof text for Razi's argument.
2
Understand the inference from the intensive form
Razi argues that the intensive form 'كفور' (extremely ungrateful) limits the ruling to the original disbeliever. Consider why this linguistic point is important.
The intensive form indicates a heightened degree of ingratitude.
3
Engage with the objection
Read the objection: the verse 'Whoever does evil will be recompensed for it' (4:123) seems to contradict. Reflect on the apparent conflict.
This objection challenges the specificity of the first verse.
4
Learn Razi's resolution
Razi's response: when verses conflict, priority is given to forgiveness (the more merciful interpretation). This is a principle in dealing with apparent contradictions.
This resolution shows the methodology of balancing textual evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَهَلْ يُجَازَى إِلَّا الْكَفُورَ﴾ [سبأ: 17] ولفظ الكفور للمبالغة، فوجب أن يختص هذا الحكم بالكافر الأصلي، لا يقال : هذا معارض بقوله تعالى: ﴿مَن يَعْمَلْ سُوءًا يُجْزَ بِهِ﴾ [النساء: 123] لأنا نقول : لما وقع التعارض بين العفو والوعيد، كان الرجحان لجانب العفو - على ما سيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى في وجوه الترجيحات.
The seventh proof: His saying, the Most High: 'And how can there be recompense except for the ungrateful?' [Saba 34:17]. The word 'kafur' (الْكَفُورَ) indicates intensiveness, so it follows that this ruling is specific to the original disbeliever (al-kafir al-asli). It cannot be said that this is contradicted by His saying, the Most High: 'Whoever does evil will be recompensed for it' [al-Nisa 4:123]. For we say: When there is a conflict between forgiveness and threat, the preponderance is given to the side of forgiveness – as will come, Allah willing, in the chapters on preponderances.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
Razi cites a verse that uses the intensive form 'al-kafur' (extreme ingrate), arguing that such a term is limited to the original disbeliever who persists in ingratitude, not to a sinful believer. He then anticipates an objection: another verse (4:123) seems to say that anyone who does evil will be recompensed. Razi responds that when two verses conflict, one promising forgiveness (or limiting punishment) and another threatening punishment, the side of forgiveness is given precedence. This is a general principle in dealing with apparent contradictions.

Key Terms
الكفور
المبالغة
الكافر الأصلي
الترجيحات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that 'kafur' applies to any sinner or disbeliever, but Razi restricts it to the original disbeliever due to the intensive form.
Correction: The term 'kafur' is an intensive form, so it refers to extreme ingratitude, i.e., the original disbeliever who persists in disbelief.

Checkpoint

A) Because it uses an intensive form
B) Because it is abrogated
C) Because it appears in a Meccan sura
D) Because it refers to the afterlife only

Key Takeaway
Razi limits the threat of punishment to the original disbeliever based on the intensive form 'kafur', and resolves conflicting verses by prioritizing divine forgiveness.

Eighth Argument: Black Faces for Apostates Only
Razi argues that only apostates get black faces and punishment, using specification to address the objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses Quran 3:106 to argue that only apostates receive black faces and punishment, and how he applies the principle of specification (takhsis) to address the objection about original disbelievers.

Core Idea
Black faces and punishment are for apostates, not original disbelievers.

Razi presents a proof from the Quran (3:106) where Allah distinguishes two groups on Judgment Day: those with white faces and those with black faces. The black-faced are directly addressed as having disbelieved after faith, implying they were believers first. This raises a question about original disbelievers, and Razi resolves it through the concept of specification (takhsis). In this lesson, we will explore how this argument supports the Sunni position regarding the fate of sinful believers and the specificity of the verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Pay attention to the verse citation and Razi's response to the objection.
2
Identify the two groups in the verse
Notice that the verse mentions two categories: those whose faces become white and those whose faces become black. The black-faced are addressed with 'Did you disbelieve after your faith?'.
This indicates that the black-faced had faith before disbelieving—they are apostates.
3
Understand the problem
Recognize the potential issue: if only apostates are punished, what about original disbelievers? Razi acknowledges this objection.
The objection is that the verse seems to exclude original disbelievers from punishment, which contradicts other proofs.
4
Learn Razi's solution: specification
Razi replies that the generality of the verse is specified to this particular case (apostates), so it does not negate punishment for original disbelievers, who are punished by other evidence.
This is an application of the usul al-fiqh principle of takhsis (specification).
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this argument matters: it helps defend the idea that sinful believers are not punished with lasting punishment, while original disbelievers are punished through other texts.
This argument is part of a larger debate about the fate of grave sinners (murtaqib al-kabira).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثامنة : أنه تعالى جعل المكلفين صنفين، فقال: ﴿يَوْمَ تَبْيَضُ وُجُوهٌ وَتَسْوَدُ وُجُوهٌ فَأَمَّا الَّذِينَ اسْوَدَّتْ وُجُوهُهُمْ أَكَفَرْتُم بَعْدَ إِيمَانِكُمْ فَذُوقُوا الْعَذَابَ بِمَا كُنتُمْ تَكْفُرُونَ﴾ [آل عمران: 106] فجعل كل من اسودت وجوههم من الذين كفروا بعد إيمانهم من أهل العذاب وجعل من ابيضت وجوههم من أهل الثواب وأقصى ما في الباب أن يقال : يشكل هذا بالكافر الأصلي إلا أنا نقول خص العموم في هذه الصورة، فيبقى حجة فيما سواها.
The eighth proof: That He, the Most High, made the morally responsible people into two categories, saying: 'On the Day when faces become white and faces become black. As for those whose faces become black, 'Did you disbelieve after your faith? Then taste the punishment for what you used to disbelieve.' [Aal-e-Imran 3:106]. Thus He made everyone whose faces become black among those who disbelieved after their faith to be among the people of punishment, and He made those whose faces become white among the people of reward. The most that can be said is that this is problematic regarding the original disbeliever, but we say: the generality is specified in this case, so it remains a proof for what is beyond it.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
Razi uses the verse that distinguishes two groups on Judgment Day: those with white faces and those with black faces. The black-faced are addressed: 'Did you disbelieve after your faith?' This shows they had faith before, so they are apostates, not original disbelievers. Therefore, the punishment (Hell) is for those who disbelieved after faith, not for original disbelievers? But Razi acknowledges that this seems to exclude original disbelievers from punishment, which is not intended. He explains that the verse's generality is specified to this particular case (apostates), and it remains a valid argument for excluding sinful believers (who did not apostatize) from Hell.

Key Terms
ابيضاض الوجوه
اسوداد الوجوه
الكفر بعد الإيمان
التخصيص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse about black faces implies that original disbelievers are not punished.
Correction: Razi clarifies that the verse is specific to apostates; original disbelievers are punished through other proofs, and the verse's generality is specified.

Checkpoint

B) Those who disbelieved after faith
C) All sinners
D) Those who never believed

Key Takeaway
Razi's eighth argument shows that only those who disbelieve after belief are addressed with black faces and punishment, and the verse's generality is specified, preserving punishment for original disbelievers.

Bright Faces vs Dusty Faces: The Ninth Proof
Razi cites Quranic verse to argue for punishment of disbelievers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses the description of faces on the Day of Judgment to argue that only disbelievers will be punished in Hell.

Core Idea
Dusty faces signal eternal disgrace for the disbelievers.

In this ninth proof, Razi turns to another vivid description from the Qur'an about the Day of Judgment: the contrast between bright, laughing faces and dusty, darkened faces. The verse explicitly labels the dust-faced as 'the disbelievers, the wicked,' connecting their external state to their eternal fate. This lesson unpacks that connection.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and translation
Read the Arabic verse and its English translation carefully. Notice the two contrasting descriptions of faces.
The verse is from Surah Abasa, verses 38-42.
2
Identify the two groups
The verse first describes bright and laughing faces, then dusty and darkened faces. It then identifies the latter as 'the disbelievers, the wicked.' This is the key link between appearance and identity.
3
Understand the argument
Razi argues that because the dusty-faced are explicitly called disbelievers, only they will suffer the punishment described in Hell. The bright-faced are implied to be believers who will be rewarded.
Razi mentions the reasoning is similar to his second proof.

The reasoning is similar to the second proof: only those who are described as disbelievers will face punishment.

Razi's Tenth Argument: Hell is Only for Deniers of Resurrection
Razi argues that Hell is only for deniers of the resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's argument that only those who deny the resurrection are condemned to Hell, based on the Quranic classification of mankind.

Core Idea
Hell is exclusively for those who deny the resurrection.

Razi presents a logical argument based on the Quran's threefold division of humanity into the foremost, companions of the right, and companions of the left. He shows that only the companions of the left are in Hell, and they are defined as those who deny the resurrection. This argument carries implications for the fate of sinful believers, distinguishing them from deniers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once to get a feel for the argument. Then read the literal translation to ensure you understand each part.
Notice the Quranic verse quoted in the passage.
2
Identify the three groups and their fates
Razi lists three categories: السابقون, أصحاب الميمنة, أصحاب المشأمة. Note that the first two are in Paradise, the third in Hell.
3
Trace the logical deduction
Follow the reasoning: (1) Hell's inhabitants are only companions of the left. (2) Companions of the left are those who deny resurrection. Therefore, Hell's inhabitants are only deniers of resurrection.
This is a syllogism: A = B, B = C, so A = C.
4
Consider the final remark
Razi notes that this argument is not applied to all disbelievers (ترك العمل به في حق سائر الكفار) but remains a proof for sinners (الفساق). Think about what this means for believers who sin.
This suggests that sinful believers are not condemned to eternal Hell, unlike those who deny resurrection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة العاشرة : أنه تعالى قسم المكلفين إلى ثلاثة أقسام السابقون وأصحاب الميمنة، وأصحاب المشأمة، ثم ذكر أن السابقين وأصحاب الميمنة في الجنة، وأن أصحاب المشأمة في النار ثم بين أن أصحاب المشأمة الذين يقولون : ﴿وَقَالُوا أَئِذَا مِتْنَا وَكُنَّا تُرَابًا وَعِظَامًا أَئِنَّا لَمَبْعُوثُونَ﴾ [المؤمنون: 82] ولما ثبت أن أصحاب النار ليسوا إلا أصحاب المشأمة وثبت أن أصحاب المشأمة الذين ينكرون البعث وجب أن يقال: إن أصحاب النار ليسوا إلا الذين ينكرون البعث. ترك العمل به في حق سائر الكفار فيبقى حجة في الفساق.
The tenth proof: That He, the Most High, divided the morally responsible into three categories: the foremost, the companions of the right, and the companions of the left. Then He mentioned that the foremost and the companions of the right are in Paradise, and that the companions of the left are in the Fire. Then He explained that the companions of the left are those who say: 'And they say, 'When we have died and become dust and bones, will we indeed be resurrected?'' [al-Mu'minun 23:82]. And since it is established that the inhabitants of the Fire are only the companions of the left, and it is established that the companions of the left are those who deny the resurrection, it follows that the inhabitants of the Fire are only those who deny the resurrection. It is not acted upon with regard to other disbelievers, so it remains a proof for the sinful (fussaq).
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
Razi uses the classification from Surah al-Waqi'ah (though he references verses from al-Mu'minun) to argue that only those who deny the resurrection (i.e., the companions of the left) are in Hell. The foremost and companions of the right are in Paradise. Since deniers of the resurrection are specifically the companions of the left, and only they enter Hell, it follows that Hell is exclusively for those who deny the resurrection. This excludes believers who sin but do not deny resurrection. Razi notes that this argument is not applied to all disbelievers (perhaps because some disbelievers might not deny resurrection in the same way? He says 'ترك العمل به في حق سائر الكفار' meaning it is set aside for other disbelievers, but remains a proof for sinners (meaning sinful believers are not included in Hell).

Key Terms
السابقون
أصحاب الميمنة
أصحاب المشأمة
إنكار البعث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that this argument condemns all disbelievers to Hell.
Correction: Razi specifically limits the conclusion to those who deny resurrection. He says it is not acted upon regarding other disbelievers, meaning disbelievers who do not deny resurrection may be treated differently.

Checkpoint

A) The foremost
B) The companions of the right
C) The companions of the left
D) All three groups

Key Takeaway
Razi uses the Quranic threefold division to prove that Hell is exclusively for those who deny the resurrection.

Razi's Proof That the Grave Sinner Does Not Enter the Fire
Razi argues that the grave sinner is a believer and will not be disgraced, hence not enter the fire.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's deductive argument from Quranic verses that a grave sinner, being a believer, will not be disgraced or enter the Fire.

Core Idea
The grave sinner’s faith guarantees freedom from disgrace and the Fire.

In this passage, Imam Razi presents a tightly reasoned proof for the Ash'ari position on the fate of grave sinners. He uses three Quranic verses to establish two premises, from which he deduces that no believer—including the grave sinner—will ever enter the Fire. Let's examine the logical chain step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Razi uses a very compressed style here.
2
Identify the two key premises
Razi first cites two verses to establish that the grave sinner is a believer and that the believer is not disgraced. Find these two premises in the text.
The verses are from Surat al-Tahrim and Surat Aal 'Imran.
3
Understand the link between fire and disgrace
Razi then cites a third verse equating entry into the Fire with disgrace. See how this connects to the previous premises.
This verse is from Surat Aal 'Imran, verse 192.
4
Follow the logical conclusion
Combine the premises: if the grave sinner is a believer and believers are not disgraced, then the grave sinner is not disgraced; and since entering the Fire is disgrace, the grave sinner cannot enter the Fire.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الخامسة والثلاثون: تعالى: ﴿يَوْمَ لَا يُخْزِي اللهُ النَّبِيَّ وَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا مَعَهُ﴾ [التحريم: ٨] ولقوله تعالى حكاية عن المؤمنين: ﴿وَلَا تُخْزِنَا يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ﴾ [آل عمران: ١٩٤] ثم قال تعالى: ﴿فَاسْتَجَابَ رَبُّهُمْ﴾ [آل عمران: ١٩٥] فثبت أن صاحب الكبيرة مؤمن، وثبت أن المؤمن لا يخزى، فيلزم أن صاحب الكبيرة لا يخزى، وإنما قلنا إن كل من أدخل النار فقد أخزي لقوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّكَ مَن تُدْخِلِ النَّارَ فَقَدْ أَخْزَيْتَهُ﴾ [آل عمران: ١٩٢] ولما ثبتت هاتان المقدمتان لزم القطع بأن صاحب الكبيرة لا يدخل النار.
The thirty-fifth issue: He, exalted, says: {The day when God will not disgrace the Prophet and those who believed with him} [al-Tahrim: 8]. And by His saying, exalted, narrating from the believers: {And do not disgrace us on the Day of Resurrection} [Aal 'Imran: 194]. Then He, exalted, said: {So their Lord responded to them} [Aal 'Imran: 195]. So it is established that the committer of a major sin is a believer, and it is established that the believer is not disgraced, so it necessarily follows that the committer of a major sin is not disgraced. And we only said that everyone who enters the fire has been disgraced because of His saying, exalted: {Indeed, whoever You admit into the fire, You have disgraced him} [Aal 'Imran: 192]. And when these two premises are established, the certainty follows that the committer of a major sin does not enter the fire.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage presents a proof (hujja) from the Ash'ari position on the fate of grave sinners. The author first cites two verses that promise that believers will not be disgraced on the Day of Resurrection: one about the Prophet and those with him, and another where the believers ask not to be disgraced, with God's response. From these he establishes two premises: (1) the committer of a major sin is a believer, and (2) the believer is not disgraced. Then he introduces a third verse that equates entering the fire with disgrace. Combining these, he concludes that the grave sinner will not enter the fire, because if he did, he would be disgraced, contradicting the premise that believers are not disgraced. The argument is deductive: if the grave sinner is a believer and believers are not disgraced, then the grave sinner cannot be disgraced, and since entering fire is disgrace, he cannot enter the fire.

Key Terms
صاحب الكبيرة
يخزى
النار
المقدمتان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'لا يخزى' applies only to a specific group and not to all believers.
Correction: The verse promises no disgrace for the Prophet and those who believed with him, and the believers' prayer for no disgrace shows it applies to all believers, including grave sinners.

Checkpoint
According to Razi's argument, what does the verse 'إِنَّكَ مَن تُدْخِلِ النَّارَ فَقَدْ أَخْزَيْتَهُ' establish?
A) That entering the fire is a form of disgrace.
B) That the grave sinner is a believer.
C) That no believer enters the fire.
D) That the Prophet will not be disgraced.

Key Takeaway
Razi proves that the grave sinner, being a believer, will not be disgraced and therefore will not enter the Fire.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you fall into a major sin, do you truly believe that Allah will not disgrace you because of your faith? How does that assurance shape your repentance?
?
Razi's proof relies on the fact that you are still a believer even after sin. Does this passage make you more hopeful or more careless about sin? Be honest—how must you respond to keep it from cheapening grace?
?
If you were standing before Allah tomorrow and He asked why you deserve not to be disgraced, would your answer rest on your deeds or on His promise in this verse? What change must you make today to live in that promise?
