Second Objection: Reinterpreting the Verse
Razi presents the second objection and answers by appealing to the original meaning of the verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second objection to the third proof and Razi's answer that the original meaning of 'pleased with' refers to the person's pleasing deeds.

Core Idea
The verse's 'pleased with' primarily means pleased with the person's deeds, not merely the intercession.

The second objection reinterprets Quran 21:28 to mean 'except for whom Allah is pleased with their intercession,' shifting the focus from the person to the act. Razi counters by arguing that the primary meaning of 'pleased with' relates to the person's attributes and deeds, and that the fasiq's faith is a pleasing deed. This lesson explores that debate.

Guided Path
1
Read the second objection
Read how the opponent reinterprets the verse: 'except for whom Allah is pleased with his intercession.' They cite other verses to support this.
Notice the opponent uses the context of angels being commanded.
2
Understand Razi's answer
Razi argues that the permission to intercede for some but not others must be based on a distinction in the persons themselves. So the verse's 'pleased with' goes back to something in the person, not just the act of intercession.
3
Identify the original meaning
Razi says the original (asli) meaning is that Allah is pleased with a deed from the person. The fasiq has that pleasing deed—faith. So he is included.
Carrying the expression to its original meaning is more appropriate.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The fasiq is included in the exception because he has a pleasing deed (faith). How does this answer the objection?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة : قوله تعالى في حق الملائكة: ﴿وَلَا يَشْفَعُونَ إِلَّا لِمَنِ ارْتَضَى﴾ [الأنبياء: ٢٨] وصاحب الكبيرة مرتضى عند الله؛ لأنه مرتضى عند الله إيمانه، ومتى صدق عليه أنه مرتضى في الصفة الفلانية صدق عليه أنه مرتضى؛ لأنه صدق المركب فقد صدق المفرد، وإذا كان كذلك وجب أن يدخل تحت قوله: ﴿إِلَّا لِمَنِ ارْتَضَى﴾ والاستثناء من النفي إثبات، فوجب ثبوت الشفاعة له.
فإن قيل: الكلام على هذا الاستدلال من وجهين:
الأول: أن الفاسق ليس بمرتضى، فوجب أن لا يكون أهلاً لشفاعة الملائكة له. إنما قلنا: إنه ليس بمرتضى لأنه ليس بمرتضى بحسب فسقه، ومتى صدق عليه أنه ليس بمرتضى بحسب فسقه صدق عليه أنه ليس بمرتضى بعين ما ذكرتم، وحينئذ يكون داخلاً تحت النفي.
الثاني: أنا نحمل الآية على أن المراد ﴿وَلَا يَشْفَعُونَ إِلَّا لِمَنِ ارْتَضَى اللَّهُ شَفَاعَتَهُ﴾ بدليل قوله تعالى: ﴿مَن ذَا الَّذِي يَشْفَعُ عِندَهُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِهِ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٥٥] وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا يَسْبِقُونَهُ بِالْقَوْلِ وَهُم بِأَمْرِهِ يَعْمَلُونَ﴾ [الأنبياء: ٢٧] فلم قلتم: إن الله ارتضى شفاعة الفاسقين وهذا أول المسألة؟
والجواب عن الأول: أنه ثبت في العلوم العقلية أن المهملتين لا يتناقضان، كقوله: زيد عالم وزيد ليس بعالم لا يتناقضان لاحتمال أن يكون المراد عالمًا بالفقه وغير عالم بالكلام، فكذا قولنا: الفاسق مرتضى والفاسق ليس بمرتضى لا يتناقضان؛ لأنه مرتضى بحسب إيمانه غير مرتضى بحسب فسقه.
إذا ثبت هذا فنقول: لا شك أن الفاسق مرتضى بحسب إيمانه، وثبت أنه متى صدق أنه مرتضى بحسب إيمانه وجب أن يصدق عليه أنه مرتضى، والمستثنى هو القدر، وكل من صدق عليه هذا القدر وجب أن يكون داخلاً في الاستثناء وخارجًا من المستثنى منه، ويلزم من هذا أن يقال: الفاسق من أهل الشفاعة.
والجواب عن الثاني: أن كون الشافع مأذونًا لأن يشفع لأحد الشخصين دون الآخر لا بد أن يكون لامتياز ذلك الشخص عن الشخص الثاني بصفة مرضية وأفعال حسنة مقبولة، فيكون الأصل والعمدة في الباب إنما هو صدور الأفعال المرضية عن المشفوع له، وحمل اللفظ على المعنى الأصلي أولى من حمله على المعنى العرضي المعتبر على سبيل التبع، وإذا كان كذلك كان قوله: ﴿وَلَا يَشْفَعُونَ إِلَّا لِمَنِ ارْتَضَى﴾ معناه: ولا يشفعون إلا لمن ارتضى الله منه فعلاً، والفاسق قد ارتضى الله منه فعلاً وهو الإيمان، فكان داخلاً تحت هذا الاستثناء.
The third proof: His statement the Exalted concerning the angels: 'And they do not intercede except for whom He is pleased' [Q. 21:28]. And the grave sinner is one with whom Allah is pleased because His faith is something with which Allah is pleased. Whenever it is true of him that he is pleased with in a certain attribute, it is true of him that he is pleased with, because the truth of the compound implies the truth of the simple. And if that is the case, then he must be included under His statement 'except for whom He is pleased', and the exception from negation is affirmation, so intercession is affirmed for him.
If it is said: The discussion regarding this proof is from two aspects:
First: The wicked sinner is not one with whom Allah is pleased, so he must not be worthy of the angels' intercession for him. We say: He is not pleased with because he is not pleased with in respect of his sin, and whenever it is true of him that he is not pleased with in respect of his sin, it is true of him that he is not pleased with, by the very same argument you mentioned, and then he falls under the negation.
Second: We interpret the verse to mean 'and they do not intercede except for whom Allah is pleased with his intercession', as evidence by His statement 'Who is there that can intercede with Him except by His permission?' [Q. 2:255] and His statement 'and they do not precede Him in speech, and they act by His command' [Q. 21:27]. So why do you claim that Allah is pleased with the intercession for the wicked sinners, and this is the beginning of the issue?
The answer to the first: It is established in the rational sciences that two unqualified propositions do not contradict each other, such as the statement 'Zayd is learned' and 'Zayd is not learned' do not contradict because it is possible that by 'learned' is meant learned in jurisprudence and not learned in theology. Similarly, our statement 'the wicked sinner is pleased with' and 'the wicked sinner is not pleased with' do not contradict, because he is pleased with in respect of his faith and not pleased with in respect of his sin.
If this is established, we say: There is no doubt that the wicked sinner is pleased with in respect of his faith, and it is established that whenever it is true that he is pleased with in respect of his faith, it must be true of him that he is pleased with, and the exception is the quantity, and everyone of whom this quantity is true must be included in the exception and excluded from the excepted-from. From this it follows that the wicked sinner is among the people of intercession.
The answer to the second: The fact that the intercessor is permitted to intercede for one person and not another must be due to the distinction of that person from the second by a pleasing attribute and acceptable good deeds. So the origin and foundation in this matter is the occurrence of pleasing deeds from the one for whom intercession is made, and carrying the expression to its original meaning is more appropriate than carrying it to a secondary meaning considered as subsidiary. And if that is the case, His statement 'and they do not intercede except for whom He is pleased' means: 'and they do not intercede except for one from whom Allah is pleased with a deed', and the wicked sinner, Allah is pleased with a deed from him, which is faith, so he is included under this exception.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the reality of intercession for grave sinners, presented by Imam al-Razi as his third argument. It begins by citing the Quranic verse (21:28) that angels intercede only for those with whom Allah is pleased. Razi asserts that a grave sinner (fasiq) is indeed 'pleased with' (murtada) because his faith is something pleasing to Allah. He argues that if a person is pleasing in one attribute, he is pleasing in a general sense, since affirming a composite (the person having faith) implies affirming a simple attribute (being pleasing in that regard). Thus, the exception in the verse includes such a person, and intercession is affirmed. Then Razi addresses two objections. The first objection claims that the fasiq is not pleased with because of his sin, so he falls under negation. Razi answers by explaining that unqualified propositions (muhmalaat) do not contradict; the fasiq can be both pleased with (in respect of faith) and not pleased with (in respect of sin). So the fasiq is pleased with regarding faith, and the exception applies to that aspect, making him eligible for intercession. The second objection reinterprets the verse to mean 'except for whom Allah is pleased with his intercession', implying that the intercession itself must be pleasing, not the person. Razi rebuts this by arguing that the intercessor's permission to intercede for some and not others must be based on a pleasing attribute in the person for whom intercession is made. The primary and original meaning of 'pleased with' refers to the person's deeds, and the fasiq has a pleasing deed (faith), so he is included. The proof thus concludes that the fasiq is within the exception and qualifies for intercession.

Key Terms
شفاعة
مرتضى
فاسق
استثناء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Razi, what is the primary basis for why an intercessor is permitted to intercede for one person and not another?
A) The intercessor's rank.
B) The person's pleasing attribute or deed.
C) The time of day.
D) The number of sins.

Key Takeaway
The original meaning of 'pleased with' in the verse is about the person's pleasing deed (faith), so the fasiq qualifies for intercession.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the faith in your heart is a deed that pleases Allah enough to grant you intercession, or do you rely on some other merit? What evidence from this verse would you give to support your answer?
?
When you consider your own sins, do you ever think that Allah might be pleased with you despite them? On what basis? This lesson argues that faith itself is a pleasing deed—does that change how you view your own standing before Allah?
?
If the condition for intercession is Allah's pleasure with your deed of faith, how does that affect your daily actions? Are you living as someone who is 'pleased with' in the original sense, or are you merely hoping for intercession without that foundational deed?

Fourth Proof: Quran 74:48 and the Specificity of Threat
Razi argues from Q. 74:48 that the threat is specific to disbelievers, so believers receive intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi uses Quran 74:48 to argue that intercession must benefit believers, even grave sinners, because the verse specifically threatens disbelievers.

Core Idea
A threat that applies to everyone is no threat at all.

Imam Razi continues his arguments for intercession by turning to a verse about the disbelievers. He points out that if the verse were general, it would be meaningless. This lesson unpacks his logical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and Razi's argument
Read the full Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the verse citation and how Razi interprets its context.
2
Understand the logical structure
Razi uses a conditional: if Muslims were also denied intercession, the threat would not distinguish believer from disbeliever. Therefore, the threat must be specific to disbelievers.
This is a key logical move—'takhsees al-kafir'.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why Razi's argument supports intercession for sinful Muslims. If the threat only applies to disbelievers, then believers (even sinners) can benefit from intercession.
This connects to the broader discussion on shafa'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَا نَفَعَهُمْ شَفَاعَةُ الشَّافِعِينَ﴾ [المدثر: ٤٨] ذكر ذلك في معرض التهديد، فلو كان حال المسلم كذلك لم يبق في هذا التهديد فرق بين المؤمن والكافر، فكان تخصيص الكافر عبثًا.
The fourth proof: His statement the Exalted: 'So the intercession of the intercessors will not benefit them' [Q. 74:48]. He mentioned that in the context of threat. So if the case of the Muslim were also like that, there would remain no difference in this threat between the believer and the disbeliever, and thus specifying the disbeliever would be futile.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof for intercession for grave sinners. Razi cites Quran 74:48, which states that the intercession of intercessors will not benefit certain people. He notes that this verse is mentioned in a context of threatening (tahdid) the disbelievers. Razi argues that if Muslims were also deprived of intercession, then the threat would apply equally to both believers and disbelievers, making the specification of disbelievers meaningless. Since the verse specifically addresses the disbelievers, it implies that believers (including grave sinners) can benefit from intercession. This is a logical argument from the specificity of the threat.

Key Terms
تهديد
شفاعة
كافر
مؤمن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Quran 74:48 denies intercession to everyone, including believers.
Correction: Razi shows the verse is a threat specifically to disbelievers, so it does not apply to believers. Thus, intercession can benefit believers.

Checkpoint
What is the key logical point in Razi's fourth proof?
A) The verse explicitly mentions Muslims.
B) The verse is a threat directed specifically at disbelievers, so it does not apply to believers.
C) The verse proves that no intercession exists.
D) The verse is abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The specificity of the threat in Quran 74:48 to disbelievers implies that believers can receive intercession.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the threat in Quran 74:48 is directed at disbelievers, how does that affect your view of your own sins? Do you rely on the hope of intercession, or do you take the threat seriously? What does this verse teach you about the mercy of Allah and the importance of repentance?
?
The verse specifies that intercession will not benefit 'them' (the disbelievers). How does this make you feel about those who reject faith? Does it increase your gratitude for being among the believers? What responsibility does it place on you to seek intercession through good deeds and following the Prophet?
?
Razi's argument hinges on the specificity of the threat. Is there any area of your life where you assume a general threat does not apply to you? How can you ensure you are not among those who mistakenly think they are safe from Allah's punishment?

Proof from Hadith: Intercession for Grave Sinners
Razi cites the prophetic hadith on intercession for grave sinners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet's intercession, according to a clear hadith, is specifically for the grave sinners of his community, affirming divine mercy for major sinners.

Core Idea
The Prophet's intercession is for the grave sinners of his community – no exceptions.

Razi now presents a direct textual proof from the Prophet himself. After logical arguments, this hadith removes any doubt about the scope of intercession. The Prophet explicitly states that his intercession is for those who commit major sins, providing a clear and authoritative foundation for this doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith passage
Carefully read the Arabic and translation. Notice that it is a direct quote from the Prophet. Reflect on the words 'ahl al-kaba'ir' (grave sinners) and 'ummati' (my community).
2
Understand the proof structure
Razi uses this hadith as a dalil naqli (textual proof). Ask yourself: How does this one statement settle the question about intercession?
The Prophet's own words are the highest authority after the Quran.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider the common misunderstanding that intercession is only for righteous believers. This hadith explicitly includes grave sinners. How does this shape our understanding of mercy?
This passage guards against restricting intercession to the pious alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة: قوله: «شفاعتي لأهل الكبائر من أمتي».
The fifth proof: His statement: 'My intercession is for the grave sinners of my community.'
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth and final proof in Razi's series of arguments supporting intercession for grave sinners. It is a direct prophetic hadith in which the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) states explicitly: 'My intercession is for the grave sinners of my community.' This hadith is cited as a textual proof (dalil naqli) that the Prophet's intercession specifically benefits those Muslims who commit major sins (kaba'ir). It leaves no ambiguity regarding the recipients of intercession, clearly indicating that grave sinners are not excluded from divine mercy and prophetic intercession.

Key Terms
شفاعة (intercession)
أهل الكبائر (grave sinners)
أمة (community)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that the Prophet's intercession is only for righteous believers or those without major sins.
Correction: This hadith explicitly states that intercession is for the grave sinners (ahl al-kaba'ir) of his community, showing that major sinners are included.

Checkpoint
What is the scope of the Prophet's intercession according to this hadith?
A) Only for prophets and saints.
B) Only for disbelievers.
C) For the grave sinners of his community.
D) For all of humanity indiscriminately.

Key Takeaway
This hadith is a clear textual proof that the Prophet's intercession is specifically for the grave sinners of his community, affirming divine mercy for major sinners.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the Prophet's intercession includes you, even if you have fallen into major sins? Or do you subconsciously feel that you are beyond mercy? How does this hadith challenge that feeling?
?

?
This hadith is a direct promise from the Prophet. Are you living with the confidence of that promise, or do you let hopelessness about your own sins distance you from seeking his intercession? What is one concrete change you need to make today based on this certainty?

The Quranic Proof for Intercession
Razi presents the fourth proof using Quranic reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical inference from the Quranic threat that intercession is only denied to disbelievers, implying it is available for believers who commit major sins.

Core Idea
Intercession is only denied to disbelievers, so believers are exempt.

Razi presents a subtle argument from Surah al-Muddaththir. The verse threatens disbelievers with no benefit from intercession. If Muslims were also denied, the specification would be pointless. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation to grasp the wording.
Pay attention to the phrase 'في معرض التهديد' (in the context of threat).
2
Understand the verse context
The verse is about disbelievers on the Day of Judgment. Razi notes it is a threat against them.
3
Analyze Razi's logical inference
If the state of the Muslim were like that of the disbeliever (i.e., also denied intercession), then there would be no distinction in the threat. Specifying the disbeliever would be pointless.
Razi uses the principle that specification implies exclusion.
4
Reflect on the implication
Therefore, Muslims who commit grave sins are not included in this threat and can benefit from intercession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة : قوله تعالى : ﴿فَمَا نَفَعُهُمْ شَفَاعَةُ الشَّافِعِينَ﴾ [المدثر: ٤٨] ذكر ذلك في معرض التهديد، فلو كان حال المسلم كذلك لم يبق في هذا التهديد فرق بين المؤمن والكافر، فكان تخصيص الكافر عبثاً. الحجة الخامسة : قوله: «شفاعتي لأهل الكبائر من أمتي».
The fourth proof: His statement exalted: 'So the intercession of intercessors will not benefit them' [al-Muddaththir 74:48]. He mentioned that in the context of threat. If the state of the Muslim were like that, there would remain in this threat no distinction between the believer and the disbeliever, so specifying the disbeliever would be pointless. The fifth proof: His statement: 'My intercession is for the people of major sins from my community.'
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage presents two proofs for the permissibility of intercession for grave sinners. The first proof is from Surah al-Muddaththir 74:48, where Allah says that the intercession of intercessors will not benefit the disbelievers. Razi argues that this threat is directed specifically at disbelievers; if the Muslim grave sinner were also excluded from intercession, the threat would apply equally to believers and disbelievers, making the specification of disbelievers meaningless. The second proof is the well-known hadith in which the Prophet states that his intercession is for those who commit major sins from his community, explicitly including them.

Key Terms
شفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse denies intercession to all humans, including Muslims.
Correction: Razi argues that the verse is specifically about disbelievers, and the threat is only for them. If it included Muslims, specifying disbelievers would be redundant.

Checkpoint
According to Razi's argument, why does the threat in al-Muddaththir 74:48 not apply to Muslims who commit grave sins?
A) Because the verse was revealed specifically about the Quraysh
B) Because specifying the disbeliever in the threat implies that the believer is not included
C) Because the threat is about this world, not the afterlife
D) Because grave sinners are not mentioned in the verse

Key Takeaway
The specific mention of disbelievers in the intercession denial implies that believers, even major sinners, are not included in that denial.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This lesson shows that Allah specifically targets disbelievers with the threat of no intercession. Does your fear of Allah's punishment come from a place of faith or from doubt in His mercy? How can you balance hope and fear after understanding this?
?
If you were to stand before Allah today, would you be counted among those for whom intercession is possible? What concrete step will you take to ensure you remain among the believers who are not under that threat?

The Prophetic Proof for Intercession
Razi presents the fifth proof using a Prophetic hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the clear Prophetic hadith that directly establishes intercession for grave sinners.

Core Idea
The Prophet explicitly said his intercession is for major sinners.

The second proof is a direct hadith of the Prophet: 'My intercession is for the people of major sins from my community.' This simple statement leaves no room for doubt about the scope of intercession.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith
Read the Arabic text of the hadith and its translation.
Notice the direct wording: 'شفاعتي لأهل الكبائر من أمتي'
2
Understand the meaning
The Prophet specifically assigns his intercession to those who commit major sins from his community.
This is a well-known hadith, often cited in discussions of intercession.
3
Reflect on its significance
This hadith explicitly includes grave sinners, confirming that they are not excluded from intercession.
It directly counters the view that intercession is only for minor sins or for obedient believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to stand before Allah tonight with your worst unrepented sin, how does this hadith reshape your hope? Will you let it drive you to sincere repentance or to careless presumption?
?
The Prophet specifically said his intercession is for 'ahl al-kaba'ir' – people of major sins. Does your heart tremble at the weight of your own major sins, or do you dismiss them lightly? What are you doing today to ensure you are among those who deserve his intercession?
?
If you truly believe that the Prophet's intercession is a lifeline for you despite your failures, what concrete step will you take this week to turn back to Allah instead of using this hadith as an excuse to continue sinning?

Mu'tazila's Proof from 2:48 and Razi's Refutation
Razi presents and refutes the Mu'tazila's use of verse 2:48 against intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila's three arguments from verse 2:48 against intercession and how Razi refutes them by limiting the verse's scope to removal of punishment.

Core Idea
The verse only negates intercession that removes punishment, not intercession that increases reward.

In this passage, Razi presents the Mu'tazila's first Quranic proof against intercession and systematically dismantles it. The Mu'tazila read verse 2:48 as a blanket denial of all intercession, but Razi shows that the verse's context and purpose limit its scope. Let's examine the arguments and the response.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice the three aspects the Mu'tazila derive from the verse.
The Arabic uses technical terms like 'عموم اللفظ' and 'خصوص السبب'.
2
Identify the three Mu'tazila arguments
List the three ways the Mu'tazila infer from 2:48 that intercession cannot remove punishment: compensation, general negation, and help.
Each argument corresponds to a phrase from the verse.
3
Understand the anticipated objection
The Mu'tazila anticipate the objection that the verse was revealed about Jews. They argue that even so, the verse negates absolute intercession, and they accuse opponents of inconsistently allowing intercession for reward increase.
Razi will address this in his response.
4
Follow Razi's first response (principle)
Razi asserts the principle that consideration is given to the general wording, not the specific occasion. This counters the objection about the verse's context.
This is a key usul al-fiqh principle.
5
Follow Razi's second response (specificity)
Razi offers two points: first, even if the verse is specific, it concerns only increase of good deeds; second, the verse's purpose is intimidation, which is about punishment, not reward. Thus it only negates intercession for removing punishment.
This effectively limits the verse's scope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الأولى : قوله تعالى: ﴿وَاتَّقُوا يَوْمًا لَا تَجْزِى نَفْسٌ عَن نَّفْسٍ شَيْئًا﴾ [البَقَرَة: ٤٨] والاستدلال بهذه الآية من ثلاثة أوجه: أحدها: أنه لو أثرت الشفاعة في إسقاط العقاب لكانت قد أجزت نفس عن نفس شيئًا. وثانيها: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا يُقْبَلُ مِنْهَا شَفَعَةٌ﴾ [البَقَرَة: ٤٨] وهذا نكرة في معرض النفي فتفيد العموم. وثالثها: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا هُمْ يُنصَرُونَ﴾ [البَقَرَة: ٤٨] والشفاعة نصرة. لا يقال: هذه الآية نازلة في اليهود. وأيضًا فهذه الآية تنفي مطلق الشفاعة والمعتزلة بقرون بإثبات هذه الشفاعة في باب زيادة المنافع لأنا نجيب عن الأول بأن المذهب الصحيح أن العبرة بعموم اللفظ لا بخصوص السبب. وعن الثاني من وجهين: الأول: أن الآية هب أنها صارت منخصوصة إلا أن خصوصها في زيادة الحسنات فتبقى حجة فيما عداها. الثاني: أن المقصود من هذه الآية التخويف والتخويف إنما يحصل بعدم إسقاط العقاب لا بعدم زيادة الحسنات، وهذا يدل على أن هذه الآية مختصة بأن الشفاعات لا تأثير لها يوم القيامة في إسقاط العقوبات.
The first proof: His statement exalted: 'And fear a Day when no soul will compensate for another soul at all' [al-Baqarah 2:48]. The inference from this verse is in three aspects: First, that if intercession were to effect the removal of punishment, it would have compensated one soul for another. Second, His statement: 'And no intercession will be accepted from it' [al-Baqarah 2:48] — this is an indefinite noun in the context of negation, thus indicating generality. Third, His statement: 'Nor will they be helped' [al-Baqarah 2:48] — and intercession is help. It cannot be said: This verse was revealed about the Jews. And also this verse negates absolute intercession, while the Mu'tazila [object] affirming intercession in the matter of increase of benefits. For we answer the first [point] that the correct position is that consideration is given to the generality of the wording, not the specificity of the occasion. And regarding the second [point] from two aspects: First, that the verse, even if it became [؟] specific, its specific application is in increasing good deeds, so it remains an argument for other than that. Second, that the purpose of this verse is intimidation, and intimidation is only achieved by not removing punishment, not by not increasing good deeds, and this indicates that this verse is specific to the fact that intercessions have no effect on the Day of Resurrection in removing punishments.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage presents the Mu'tazila's first proof against intercession from verse 2:48, along with Razi's response. The Mu'tazila argue from the verse in three ways: (1) If intercession could remove punishment, it would be compensating one soul for another, which the verse denies. (2) The phrase 'no intercession will be accepted' is a general negation. (3) The verse says 'nor will they be helped,' and intercession is help. The author then anticipates an objection that the verse refers specifically to Jews. He responds that even if that were true, the Mu'tazila themselves use the verse to negate all intercession, and he then gives his own answer: first, the correct principle is to consider the general wording, not the specific occasion; second, even if the verse were specific, its specificity is about increasing good deeds, so it remains valid against intercession for removing punishment; and third, the verse's purpose is intimidation, which concerns punishment, not reward. Thus the verse only negates intercession for removing punishment, not for increasing reward.

Key Terms
شفاعة
إسقاط العقاب
عموم اللفظ
خصوص السبب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse negates all intercession entirely.
Correction: Razi limits the verse to intercession that removes punishment; it does not negate intercession that increases reward.

Checkpoint
How does Razi argue that the verse in Surah al-Baqarah 2:48 does not negate intercession for increasing rewards?
A) The verse was abrogated
B) The verse's purpose is intimidation, which concerns punishment, not reward increase
C) The verse only applies to Jews
D) The verse uses the word 'shafa'ah' in a metaphorical sense

Key Takeaway
Razi demonstrates that verse 2:48 only negates intercession that removes punishment, not intercession that increases reward, by appealing to the verse's purpose of intimidation and the principle of general wording.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Do you secretly rely on the hope of intercession to overlook your sins while neglecting your duties? How does this lesson's distinction between punishment-removing and reward-increasing intercession challenge that reliance? What will you change today in your worship to ensure you are not merely hoping for a safety net?
?
This lesson shows that Allah's threat of punishment is real and intercession does not remove it. If you stood before Allah now, would your deeds alone be sufficient? What specific sin have you procrastinated in repenting from, assuming intercession might cover it? Will you repent now, or will you continue presuming upon Allah's mercy without action?
?
Razi emphasizes that the verse's purpose is intimidation (التخويف). When you hear verses about punishment, does your heart tremble, or have you become desensitized? What is one way you can make yourself more fearful of Allah's punishment this week, not from despair but from love and reverence?

Refuting the Mu'tazila's Second Proof from Verse 40:18
Razi refutes the Mu'tazila's interpretation of verse 40:18 regarding intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's two-pronged refutation of the Mu'tazila's interpretation of verse 40:18, particularly the meaning of 'obeyed' in the context of intercession.

Core Idea
The term 'intercessor' itself proves no one is above Allah to be obeyed.

The Mu'tazila cite a Quranic verse to argue that intercession is denied to wrongdoers, but they misinterpret the word 'obeyed'. Razi offers a two-part response showing that the verse actually upholds the possibility of intercession by Allah's permission. Let's see how he dismantles their argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Familiarize yourself with the Mu'tazila's claim and Razi's rebuttal.
Pay attention to the nuance of the word 'obeyed'.
2
Identify the two parts of Razi's answer
Razi gives two separate reasons. Identify each and try to understand the logic behind them.
The first reason is about the absurdity of saying Allah obeys someone; the second is about the meaning of 'intercessor'.
3
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Some think 'obeyed' means the intercessor is followed by people. How does Razi correct this?
Use the second reason to see why 'intercessor' implies being beneath Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية : قوله تعالى: ﴿مَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ مِنْ حَمِيمٍ وَلَا شَفِيعٍ يُطَاعُ﴾ [غافر: ١٨] والظالم من يفعل الظلم، فيدخل تحته الكافر والفاسق. لا يقال: هذا ينفي كون الشفيع مطاعًا، ولا ينفي كونه مقبول القول. لأنا نقول: الجواب عنه من وجهين: الأول: أن كل عاقل يعلم أنه ليس في الوجود أحد يطيعه الله تعالى، فلا يكون في حمل الآية على ما ذكرتم فائدة. الثاني: أن الشفيع دون المشفوع إليه؛ لأنه لو كان فوقه يسمى أمرًا وحاكما، ولا يسمى شفيعًا، فلفظ الشفيع أفاد كونه دون الله تعالى فلم يمكن حمل قوله ﴿يُطَاعُ﴾ على من فوقه فكان المراد أنه ليس لهم شفيع يجاب.
The second proof: His statement exalted: 'For the wrongdoers there is no devoted friend and no intercessor who is obeyed' [Ghafir 40:18]. And the wrongdoer is the one who does wrong, so under it enter both the disbeliever and the grave sinner. It cannot be said: This negates the intercessor being obeyed, but does not negate his being accepted. For we say: The answer to it is from two aspects: First, that every rational person knows that there is no one in existence whom Allah obeys, so there is no benefit in interpreting the verse as you have mentioned. Second, that the intercessor is beneath the one for whom intercession is made; because if he were above him, he would be called a commander and a ruler, and would not be called an intercessor. Thus the term 'intercessor' indicates that he is beneath Allah, so it is not possible to interpret His statement 'obeyed' as referring to one above Him; therefore the meaning is that they have no intercessor who is responded to.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage presents the Mu'tazila's second proof from verse 40:18, which states that wrongdoers have no intercessor who is 'obeyed' (yuta'). The Mu'tazila argue that 'wrongdoer' includes both disbelievers and grave sinners. An opponent might object that the verse only denies an intercessor who is 'obeyed', not one whose plea is accepted. Razi responds with two points. First, no one is obeyed by Allah in the sense of being followed against His will, so that interpretation is pointless. Second, the term 'intercessor' implies someone lower than the one interceded to; if the intercessor were above, he would be called a commander or ruler. Hence the verse means that wrongdoers have no intercessor whose plea is answered by Allah.

Key Terms
ظالم
شفيع مطاع
مشفوع إليه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'obeyed' (يُطَاع) in the verse means the intercessor is obeyed by his followers, implying a high status.
Correction: Razi clarifies that 'obeyed' here means the intercessor's plea is accepted (mujab) by Allah, because an intercessor is beneath the one interceded to, and the term 'intercessor' itself precludes being above Allah.

Checkpoint
In responding to the Mu'tazila's second proof, what is Razi's main argument about the meaning of 'obeyed' (يُطَاعُ)?
A) It means the intercessor is obeyed by his followers
B) It means the intercessor's intercession is accepted by Allah
C) It means the angels obey the intercessor
D) It is a metaphorical expression for the intercessor's high status

Key Takeaway
Razi shows that the Mu'tazila's proof from verse 40:18 fails because 'obeyed' refers to being answered by Allah, and the term 'intercessor' itself indicates subordination to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you rely on the intercession of anyone besides Allah? This verse shows that even prophets are beneath Allah. Are you trusting in anyone or anything as an intermediary without recognizing Allah's ultimate authority? How can you ensure your hope in intercession aligns with the fact that only Allah responds?
?
Razi argues that no one is obeyed by Allah. Do you sometimes act as if your own desires or societal norms are above Allah's command? Where in your life do you need to submit fully to Allah's authority, recognizing that He alone is the one to be obeyed?
?
The term 'intercessor' implies lower status. When you seek intercession from the Prophet (peace be upon him), are you mindful that he is a servant of Allah, and that his plea is only accepted by Allah's will? How can you cultivate a heart that relies on Allah alone while still loving the Prophet?

Third Mu'tazila Proof: No Intercession on a Day without Trade or Friendship
Mu'tazila cite 2:254 as a blanket denial of intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila's third proof against intercession from Surah al-Baqarah 2:254 and why its apparent meaning is not decisive.

Core Idea
One verse's apparent generality does not override clear proofs of intercession.

The Mu'tazila continue to press their case against intercession by citing Quranic verses. This third proof relies on a verse that seems to deny all intercession on a particular Day. But is the negation truly universal? This lesson unpacks their reasoning and sets the stage for a response.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and its translation
Start by reading the Arabic verse and its literal meaning. Let the words settle before interpreting.
The verse mentions no trading, no friendship, and no intercession.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila's inference
Notice how they take the verse's general negation to apply to all intercession. Ask: does the verse refer to all times or a specific situation?
3
Consider possible counterarguments
Think about why this verse might not negate intercession entirely. The commentary will guide you.
Context matters: the verse is about a particular Day.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمِن قَبْلِ أَن يَأْتِيَ يَوْمٌ لا بَيْعٌ فِيهِ وَلَا خُلَّةٌ وَلَا شَفَعَةٌ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٥٤] ظاهر هذه الآية ينفي جميع الشفاعات. الحجة الرابعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ مِنْ أَنصَارٍ﴾ [البَقَرَة: ٢٧٠] والشفيع لا شك أنه من الأنصار. الحجة الخامسة: قوله تعالى في صفة الفساق: ﴿وَإِنَّ الْفُجَّارَ لَفِي جَمِيمٍ يَصْلَوْنَها يوم الدين وَمَا هُم عنها بِغَآئِبِينَ﴾ [الانفطار: ١٤-١٦] ولو كانت الشفاعة مقبولة في حق العصاة إما في إسقاط العقاب أو في الإخراج من النار بعد الدخول فيها لكان قوله: ﴿وَمَا هُمْ عَنْهَا بِغَائِبِينَ﴾ خلفا.
The third proof: His statement exalted: 'And before that a Day comes in which there is no trading, no friendship, and no intercession' [al-Baqarah 2:254]. The apparent meaning of this verse negates all intercessions. The fourth proof: His statement exalted: 'And the wrongdoers have no helpers' [al-Baqarah 2:270]. And the intercessor is undoubtedly among the helpers. The fifth proof: His statement exalted describing the wicked: 'Indeed the wicked will be in a blazing fire, burning therein on the Day of Judgment, and they will not be absent from it' [al-Infitar 82:14-16]. If intercession were accepted for the disobedient, either to remove punishment or to exit the Fire after entering it, then His statement 'and they will not be absent from it' would be a contradiction.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage lists three additional proofs from the Mu'tazila. The third proof is from Surah al-Baqarah 2:254, which states that on a certain Day there is no trading, friendship, or intercession. The Mu'tazila take this as a general negation of all intercession. The fourth proof is from Surah al-Baqarah 2:270, which says that wrongdoers have no helpers. Since an intercessor is a helper, this negates intercession for wrongdoers. The fifth proof is from Surah al-Infitar 82:14-16, where Allah says that the wicked will remain in Hell and will not be absent from it. If intercession could remove them or release them, the verse would be contradicted.

Key Terms
شفاعة
خلة
بيع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Surah al-Baqarah 2:254 absolutely negates any intercession on the Day of Judgment.
Correction: The verse is about a specific context (prior to intercession being granted) and does not negate intercession that Allah permits.

Checkpoint
What does the Mu'tazila's third proof rely on?
A) The verse mentions no trading, no friendship, and no intercession
B) The verse explicitly mentions helpers
C) The verse says wrongdoers have no helpers
D) The verse says the wicked will not be absent from Hell

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila use the apparent generality of 2:254 to deny all intercession, but the verse is context-specific.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you lean on the hope of intercession of the Prophet ﷺ? How does this verse, understood correctly, either strengthen or challenge that hope? Do you need to rethink any other verses you might have taken out of context?
?

Fourth Mu'tazila Proof: Wrongdoers Have No Helpers
Mu'tazila cite 2:270 to deny intercession for wrongdoers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila's fourth proof against intercession from Surah al-Baqarah 2:270 and the argument that intercessors are helpers.

Core Idea
If an intercessor is a helper, then wrongdoers have no intercessors—so the Mu'tazila argue.

The Mu'tazila's fourth proof builds on the concept of 'helper' (nasir). They link intercession to helping, then cite a verse that wrongdoers have no helpers. This lesson examines their logic and its vulnerability.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof verse and interpretation
Read the Arabic and translation. Identify the key term 'ansar' (helpers).
The verse is about wrongdoers (zalimin).
2
Understand the Mu'tazila's equation
They equate intercessor with helper. Ask: is every helper an intercessor? Is every intercessor a helper?
This is a conceptual claim.
3
Reflect on counterarguments
Consider that the verse might refer to worldly help or helpers against Allah's punishment. The Sunni response distinguishes between helper and intercessor.

Source Text

Fifth Mu'tazila Proof: The Wicked Never Leave Hell
Mu'tazila cite 82:14-16 to deny intercession for grave sinners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila's fifth proof that intercession cannot remove the wicked from Hell, based on Surah al-Infitar 82:14-16.

Core Idea
If the wicked are never absent from Hell, intercession cannot release them.

The fifth proof takes a different approach: it focuses on the fate of the wicked (fujjar). A verse states they will not be absent from Hell. The Mu'tazila argue that if intercession could remove them, that would contradict the verse. This lesson explores their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the extended passage
The Arabic includes the verses and the Mu'tazila's argument. Notice the condition: 'If intercession were accepted...'.
The verses describe the wicked entering Hell and not being absent.
2
Understand the logical contradiction claim
The Mu'tazila claim that if intercession could remove them or commute the punishment, the verse would be false. Is that necessarily a contradiction?
Consider timing: intercession could happen before entry or after a period.
3
Reflect on Sunni responses
Sunni scholars argue that the verse refers to the Day of Judgment or to the fact that they will not be absent while being punished, but intercession can still occur after a sentence or before entry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمِن قَبْلِ أَن يَأْتِيَ يَوْمٌ لا بَيْعٌ فِيهِ وَلَا خُلَّةٌ وَلَا شَفَعَةٌ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٥٤] ظاهر هذه الآية ينفي جميع الشفاعات. الحجة الرابعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ مِنْ أَنصَارٍ﴾ [البَقَرَة: ٢٧٠] والشفيع لا شك أنه من الأنصار. الحجة الخامسة: قوله تعالى في صفة الفساق: ﴿وَإِنَّ الْفُجَّارَ لَفِي جَمِيمٍ يَصْلَوْنَها يوم الدين وَمَا هُم عنها بِغَآئِبِينَ﴾ [الانفطار: ١٤-١٦] ولو كانت الشفاعة مقبولة في حق العصاة إما في إسقاط العقاب أو في الإخراج من النار بعد الدخول فيها لكان قوله: ﴿وَمَا هُمْ عَنْهَا بِغَائِبِينَ﴾ خلفا.
The third proof: His statement exalted: 'And before that a Day comes in which there is no trading, no friendship, and no intercession' [al-Baqarah 2:254]. The apparent meaning of this verse negates all intercessions. The fourth proof: His statement exalted: 'And the wrongdoers have no helpers' [al-Baqarah 2:270]. And the intercessor is undoubtedly among the helpers. The fifth proof: His statement exalted describing the wicked: 'Indeed the wicked will be in a blazing fire, burning therein on the Day of Judgment, and they will not be absent from it' [al-Infitar 82:14-16]. If intercession were accepted for the disobedient, either to remove punishment or to exit the Fire after entering it, then His statement 'and they will not be absent from it' would be a contradiction.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage lists three additional proofs from the Mu'tazila. The third proof is from Surah al-Baqarah 2:254, which states that on a certain Day there is no trading, friendship, or intercession. The Mu'tazila take this as a general negation of all intercession. The fourth proof is from Surah al-Baqarah 2:270, which says that wrongdoers have no helpers. Since an intercessor is a helper, this negates intercession for wrongdoers. The fifth proof is from Surah al-Infitar 82:14-16, where Allah says that the wicked will remain in Hell and will not be absent from it. If intercession could remove them or release them, the verse would be contradicted.

Key Terms
فجار
جميم
يصلونها
غائبين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse proves that no intercession can ever help the wicked to leave Hell.
Correction: The verse may refer to the state of punishment itself, not to the possibility of intercession altering that state.

Checkpoint
What does the Mu'tazila claim would be contradicted if intercession were accepted for the disobedient?
A) The verse saying there is no intercession
B) The verse saying the wicked will not be absent from Hell
C) The verse saying wrongdoers have no helpers
D) The verse saying there is no friendship

Key Takeaway
The fifth proof argues that the permanence implied by 'not absent' contradicts any intercession that would remove the wicked from Hell.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you rely on the hope of intercession to excuse your sins, while ignoring the warning that the wicked will not be absent from Hell? How can you combine hope with action this week?
?
If you truly believed that no intercession could save you from the Fire unless you repent and reform, what would you change starting today?
?
When you read that the wicked will not be absent from Hell, do you feel a sense of urgency to examine your own deeds, or do you assume you are safe? What specific habit or sin do you need to confront?

General Principle: 'Umum al-Lafz and the Two Responses
Razi establishes methodological rule and two responses to initial Mu'tazila objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the principle that the general wording of the Qur'an takes precedence over the specific cause, and how Razi uses this to refute the Mu'tazila's specification of the intercession verse.

Core Idea
General wording, not specific cause, determines Qur'anic meaning.

Razi begins his discussion of intercession by addressing an objection from the Mu'tazila who claim that a certain verse only denies intercession for increasing benefits. He first establishes the methodological principle that consideration is given to the generality of the wording, then provides two specific responses to counter their argument. This lesson unpacks that foundational move.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice how Razi first states the objection and then gives two distinct answers.
The passage starts with 'وأيضًا فهذه الآية'.
2
Identify the principle of 'umum al-lafz
Find the sentence where Razi says 'المذهب الصحيح أن العبرة بعموم اللفظ لا بخصوص السبب'. This is a key methodological rule.
3
Analyze the two responses
The first response says even if the verse is specified, it's only about increasing good deeds. The second response emphasizes that the verse's purpose is intimidation, which logically focuses on punishment removal.
These responses are enumerated as 'الأول' and 'الثاني'.
4
Connect to the larger debate
Reflect on how this principle and these responses lay the groundwork for the subsequent proofs against intercession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة السابعة والثلاثون
وأيضًا فهذه الآية تنفي مطلق الشفاعة والمعتزلة يقولون بإثبات هذه الشفاعة في باب زيادة المنافع
لأنا نجيب عن الأول بأن المذهب الصحيح أن العبرة بعموم اللفظ لا بخصوص السبب.
وعن الثاني من وجهين:
الأول: أن الآية هب أنها صارت مخصوصة إلا أن خصوصها في زيادة الحسنات فتبقى حجة فيما عداها.
الثاني: أن المقصود من هذه الآية التخويف والتخويف إنما يحصل بعدم إسقاط العقاب لا بعدم زيادة الحسنات، وهذا يدل على أن هذه الآية مختصة بأن الشفاعات لا تأثير لها يوم القيامة في إسقاط العقوبات.
الحجة الثانية: قوله تعالى: ﴿مَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ مِنْ حَمِيمٍ وَلَا شَفِيعٍ يُطَاعُ﴾ [غافر: ١٨] والظالم من يفعل الظلم، فيدخل تحته الكافر والفاسق.
لا يقال: هذا ينفي كون الشفيع مطاعًا، ولا ينفي كونه مقبول القول.
لأنا نقول: الجواب عنه من وجهين:
الأول: أن كل عاقل يعلم أنه ليس في الوجود أحد يطيعه الله تعالى، فلا يكون في حمل الآية على ما ذكرتم فائدة.
الثاني: أن الشفيع دون المشفوع إليه؛ لأنه لو كان فوقه يسمى أمرًا وحاكمًا، ولا يسمى شفيعًا، فلفظ الشفيع أفاد كونه دون الله تعالى فلم يمكن حمل قوله ﴿يُطَاعُ﴾ [غافر: ١٨] على من فوقه فكان المراد أنه ليس لهم شفيع يجاب.
الحجة الثالثة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمِن قَبْلِ أَن يَأْتِيَ يَوْمٌ لَّا بَيْعٌ فِيهِ وَلَا خُلَّةٌ وَلَا شَفَاعَةٌ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٥٤] ظاهر هذه الآية ينفي جميع الشفاعات.
الحجة الرابعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ مِنْ أَنصَارٍ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٧٠] والشفيع لا شك أنه من الأنصار.
الحجة الخامسة: قوله تعالى في صفة الفساق: ﴿وَإِنَّ الْفُجَّارَ لَفِي جَحِيمٍ يَصْلَوْنَهَا يَوْمَ الدِّينِ وَمَا هُمْ عَنْهَا بِغَائِبِينَ﴾ [الانفطار: ١٤-١٦] ولو كانت الشفاعة مقبولة في حق العصاة إما في إسقاط العقاب أو في الإخراج من النار بعد الدخول فيها لكان قوله: ﴿وَمَا هُمْ عَنْهَا بِغَائِبِينَ﴾ [الانفطار: ١٦] خلفًا.
الحجة السادسة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا يَنفَعُونَ إِلَّا لِمَنِ ارْتَضَىٰ﴾ [الأنبياء: ٢٨] والفاسق ليس بمرتضى فوجب نفي الشفاعة عنه.
الحجة السابعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿الَّذِينَ يَحْمِلُونَ الْعَرْشَ وَمَنْ حَوْلَهُ يُسَبِّحُونَ بِحَمْدِ رَبِّهِمْ وَيُؤْمِنُونَ بِهِ﴾ [غافر: ٧] إلى قوله: ﴿وَاتَّبَعُوا سَبِيلَكَ﴾ [غافر: ٧] ولو كانت الشفاعة حاصلة للفاسق قبل التوبة لكان التقييد بقيد التوبة في قوله: ﴿فَاغْفِرْ لِلَّذِينَ تَابُوا وَاتَّبَعُوا سَبِيلَكَ﴾ [غافر: ٧] عبثًا.
الحجة الثامنة: أجمعت الأمة على أنهم يقولون: اللهم اجعلنا من أهل شفاعة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم، ولو لم تحصل أهلية الشفاعة إلا لأهل الكبائر لكان معنى هذا السؤال: اللهم اجعلنا من أهل الكبائر ومن الفساق ومعلوم أن ذلك باطل.
والجواب عن جملة هذه الشبهات بحرف واحد وهو أن دلائلكم في نفي الشفاعة لا بد أن تكون عامة في الأشخاص والأوقات، وإلا لم يدخل محل الخلاف فيها، ودلائلنا في إثبات الشفاعة لا بد أن تكون خاصة في الأشخاص والأوقات؛ لأنا لا نثبت الشفاعة في حق كل الأشخاص ولا نثبتها أيضًا في جميع الأوقات، فثبت أنه لا بد أن تكون دلائلنا خاصة ودلائلكم عامة والخاص مقدم على العام فكان الترجيح من جانبنا، وأما الأجوبة المفصلة فمذكورة في "التفسير الكبير".
The thirty-seventh issue. And also, this verse denies intercession absolutely, and the Mu'tazila affirm this intercession in the matter of increasing benefits. For we reply to the first objection: The correct position is that consideration is given to the generality of the wording, not to the specificity of the cause. And to the second objection in two ways: First: that even if the verse were specified, its specification is in increasing good deeds, so it remains a proof regarding other than that. Second: that the purpose of this verse is intimidation, and intimidation only occurs by not removing punishment, not by not increasing good deeds. This indicates that this verse is specific that intercessions have no effect on the Day of Resurrection in removing punishments. The second proof: His statement, the Most High: {For the wrongdoers there is no friend and no intercessor to be obeyed} [Ghafir: 18]. The wrongdoer is one who commits wrongdoing, so it includes the disbeliever and the transgressor. It cannot be said: This denies the intercessor being obeyed, but does not deny him being accepted in speech. For we say: The answer to it is in two ways: First: every rational person knows that there is no one in existence whom Allah obeys, so there is no benefit in interpreting the verse as you mentioned. Second: the intercessor is beneath the one interceded for; because if he were above him, he would be called a commander and a ruler, and would not be called an intercessor. So the term intercessor indicates that he is beneath Allah, so it is not possible to interpret His statement {obeyed} [Ghafir: 18] as applying to someone above Him. So the meaning is that they have no intercessor who is granted. The third proof: His statement, the Most High: {And before the coming of a Day in which there is no sale nor friendship nor intercession} [Al-Baqarah: 254]. The apparent meaning of this verse denies all intercessions. The fourth proof: His statement, the Most High: {And the wrongdoers have no helpers} [Al-Baqarah: 270]. The intercessor is undoubtedly one of the helpers. The fifth proof: His statement, the Most High, describing the wicked: {Indeed the wicked are in a blaze. They will burn therein on the Day of Recompense, and they will not be absent from it} [Al-Infitar: 14-16]. If intercession were accepted on behalf of sinners, either in removing punishment or in bringing them out of the Fire after entering it, then His statement {and they will not be absent from it} [Al-Infitar: 16] would be contrary. The sixth proof: His statement, the Most High: {And they cannot intercede except for him whom He approves} [Al-Anbiya': 28]. The transgressor is not approved, so intercession for him must be denied. The seventh proof: His statement, the Most High: {Those who bear the Throne and those around it glorify the praise of their Lord and believe in Him} [Ghafir: 7] up to His statement: {and followed Your way} [Ghafir: 7]. If intercession were obtained for the transgressor before repentance, then the restriction by the condition of repentance in His statement: {So forgive those who repent and follow Your way} [Ghafir: 7] would be in vain. The eighth proof: The community is agreed that they say: O Allah, make us among the people of the intercession of Muhammad, peace be upon him. If eligibility for intercession were only for the people of major sins, then the meaning of this supplication would be: O Allah, make us among the people of major sins and among the wicked. And it is known that this is false. And the answer to all these specious arguments is one word: that your proofs for denying intercession must be general in persons and times; otherwise they would not include the disputed matter. And our proofs for affirming intercession must be specific in persons and times, because we do not affirm intercession on behalf of all persons, nor do we affirm it at all times. So it is established that our proofs are specific and your proofs are general, and the specific takes precedence over the general, so the weight is on our side. As for the detailed answers, they are mentioned in 'Al-Tafsir al-Kabir'.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage is a series of objections and a general answer concerning intercession (shafa'a). Raazi responds to seven additional proofs (hujaj) from the opponents (likely the Mu'tazila) who deny intercession for sinners, and then gives a methodological rebuttal. He begins with a continuation of an earlier discussion: the previous proof is handled by stating that the general wording ('umum al-lafz) is the criterion, not the specific cause. Then for the second earlier proof, he gives two responses: first, even if the verse is specified, its specification only concerns increasing good deeds, so it remains evidence for other matters; second, the purpose is intimidation (takhwif), which requires not removing punishment, not the lack of increase. Then he lists seven proofs from the Qur'an that the opponents use to deny intercession: the second proof is from Surah Ghafir 18; he explains that wrongdoers include disbelievers and transgressors, and responds to the objection that the verse only denies the intercessor being 'obeyed' but not 'accepted in speech'. He gives two answers: every rational person knows none are obeyed by Allah, so that interpretation yields no benefit; and the intercessor is beneath the one interceded for, so 'obeyed' cannot mean the intercessor is above Allah, but rather that no intercessor is granted their request. The third proof is from Al-Baqarah 254 which denies all intercessions. The fourth proof from Al-Baqarah 270 equates intercessors with helpers, which wrongdoers lack. The fifth proof from Al-Infitar 14-16 asserts that the wicked will never leave the Fire, contradicting intercession. The sixth proof from Al-Anbiya' 28 restricts intercession to those Allah approves, and the transgressor is not approved. The seventh proof from Ghafir 7 shows that intercession is tied to repentance. The eighth proof is a consensus argument: the people ask to be among the people of intercession, but if intercession were only for major sinners, that would be absurd. Finally, Raazi gives a single comprehensive answer: the opponents' proofs for denying intercession must be universal in persons and times, but the matter under dispute is specific; the proofs for affirming intercession are specific, and specific (khas) takes precedence over general ('amm). This methodological point shifts the burden of proof. The detailed responses are referred to his larger commentary.

Key Terms
عبرة بعموم اللفظ
مخصوص
تخويف
شفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that a verse revealed for a specific reason only applies to that situation.
Correction: The correct principle is that consideration is given to the generality of the wording, not the specificity of the cause.

Checkpoint
What is the correct methodological principle according to Razi?
A) Consideration is given to the specificity of the cause.
B) Consideration is given to the generality of the wording.
C) Both generality and specificity are considered equally.
D) The intended meaning is determined by the occasion of revelation.

Key Takeaway
Razi establishes that the general wording of Qur'anic verses is authoritative, not the specific cause, and uses this to refute the Mu'tazila's limited interpretation of the intercession verse.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly rely on the generality of Allah's promises and warnings, or do you limit them to convenient contexts? On what basis do you assume your deeds alone will save you from punishment?
?
If the verse's purpose is intimidation (takhwif), how deeply does the fear of Allah's punishment affect your daily choices? Are there areas of your life where you live as if Allah's warnings are not general?
?
The Mu'tazila insisted on a narrow interpretation to protect their doctrine. Where in your own heart might you be forcing a narrow understanding of Allah's words to avoid facing a difficult truth about your own need for intercession?

Second Proof: No Intercessor for the Wrongdoers
Razi presents Surah Ghafir 18 as a proof and answers an objection about the meaning of 'obeyed'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses Surah Ghafir 18 to argue against intercession and how he responds to the objection that the verse only denies an intercessor who is obeyed, not one whose request is accepted.

Core Idea
The intercessor is beneath Allah, so 'obeyed' implies granted request.

The opponents of intercession often cite the verse 'For the wrongdoers there is no friend and no intercessor to be obeyed.' Razi explains why this verse is a strong proof, and then deals with a subtle objection by offering two clear answers. This lesson delves into that exchange.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the proof
Read the Arabic and translation. Note how Razi defines 'wrongdoer' to include disbelievers and sinners, and then presents the verse.
2
Examine the objection
The objection claims that the verse only denies an intercessor who is 'obeyed' (muta'), not one who is 'accepted in speech' (maqbul al-qawl). Understand the nuance.
The objection is introduced with 'لا يقال'.
3
Analyze the two answers
First answer: no one exists whom Allah obeys, so the interpretation is useless. Second answer: the term 'intercessor' implies being beneath the one interceded for, so 'obeyed' cannot mean above Allah; rather it means their request is granted.
These answers are enumerated as 'الأول' and 'الثاني'.
4
Reflect on the logic
Consider how these answers solidify the proof: the verse denies any effective intercessor for wrongdoers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة السابعة والثلاثون
وأيضًا فهذه الآية تنفي مطلق الشفاعة والمعتزلة يقولون بإثبات هذه الشفاعة في باب زيادة المنافع
لأنا نجيب عن الأول بأن المذهب الصحيح أن العبرة بعموم اللفظ لا بخصوص السبب.
وعن الثاني من وجهين:
الأول: أن الآية هب أنها صارت مخصوصة إلا أن خصوصها في زيادة الحسنات فتبقى حجة فيما عداها.
الثاني: أن المقصود من هذه الآية التخويف والتخويف إنما يحصل بعدم إسقاط العقاب لا بعدم زيادة الحسنات، وهذا يدل على أن هذه الآية مختصة بأن الشفاعات لا تأثير لها يوم القيامة في إسقاط العقوبات.
الحجة الثانية: قوله تعالى: ﴿مَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ مِنْ حَمِيمٍ وَلَا شَفِيعٍ يُطَاعُ﴾ [غافر: ١٨] والظالم من يفعل الظلم، فيدخل تحته الكافر والفاسق.
لا يقال: هذا ينفي كون الشفيع مطاعًا، ولا ينفي كونه مقبول القول.
لأنا نقول: الجواب عنه من وجهين:
الأول: أن كل عاقل يعلم أنه ليس في الوجود أحد يطيعه الله تعالى، فلا يكون في حمل الآية على ما ذكرتم فائدة.
الثاني: أن الشفيع دون المشفوع إليه؛ لأنه لو كان فوقه يسمى أمرًا وحاكمًا، ولا يسمى شفيعًا، فلفظ الشفيع أفاد كونه دون الله تعالى فلم يمكن حمل قوله ﴿يُطَاعُ﴾ [غافر: ١٨] على من فوقه فكان المراد أنه ليس لهم شفيع يجاب.
الحجة الثالثة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمِن قَبْلِ أَن يَأْتِيَ يَوْمٌ لَّا بَيْعٌ فِيهِ وَلَا خُلَّةٌ وَلَا شَفَاعَةٌ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٥٤] ظاهر هذه الآية ينفي جميع الشفاعات.
الحجة الرابعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا لِلظَّالِمِينَ مِنْ أَنصَارٍ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٧٠] والشفيع لا شك أنه من الأنصار.
الحجة الخامسة: قوله تعالى في صفة الفساق: ﴿وَإِنَّ الْفُجَّارَ لَفِي جَحِيمٍ يَصْلَوْنَهَا يَوْمَ الدِّينِ وَمَا هُمْ عَنْهَا بِغَائِبِينَ﴾ [الانفطار: ١٤-١٦] ولو كانت الشفاعة مقبولة في حق العصاة إما في إسقاط العقاب أو في الإخراج من النار بعد الدخول فيها لكان قوله: ﴿وَمَا هُمْ عَنْهَا بِغَائِبِينَ﴾ [الانفطار: ١٦] خلفًا.
الحجة السادسة: قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا يَنفَعُونَ إِلَّا لِمَنِ ارْتَضَىٰ﴾ [الأنبياء: ٢٨] والفاسق ليس بمرتضى فوجب نفي الشفاعة عنه.
الحجة السابعة: قوله تعالى: ﴿الَّذِينَ يَحْمِلُونَ الْعَرْشَ وَمَنْ حَوْلَهُ يُسَبِّحُونَ بِحَمْدِ رَبِّهِمْ وَيُؤْمِنُونَ بِهِ﴾ [غافر: ٧] إلى قوله: ﴿وَاتَّبَعُوا سَبِيلَكَ﴾ [غافر: ٧] ولو كانت الشفاعة حاصلة للفاسق قبل التوبة لكان التقييد بقيد التوبة في قوله: ﴿فَاغْفِرْ لِلَّذِينَ تَابُوا وَاتَّبَعُوا سَبِيلَكَ﴾ [غافر: ٧] عبثًا.
الحجة الثامنة: أجمعت الأمة على أنهم يقولون: اللهم اجعلنا من أهل شفاعة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم، ولو لم تحصل أهلية الشفاعة إلا لأهل الكبائر لكان معنى هذا السؤال: اللهم اجعلنا من أهل الكبائر ومن الفساق ومعلوم أن ذلك باطل.
والجواب عن جملة هذه الشبهات بحرف واحد وهو أن دلائلكم في نفي الشفاعة لا بد أن تكون عامة في الأشخاص والأوقات، وإلا لم يدخل محل الخلاف فيها، ودلائلنا في إثبات الشفاعة لا بد أن تكون خاصة في الأشخاص والأوقات؛ لأنا لا نثبت الشفاعة في حق كل الأشخاص ولا نثبتها أيضًا في جميع الأوقات، فثبت أنه لا بد أن تكون دلائلنا خاصة ودلائلكم عامة والخاص مقدم على العام فكان الترجيح من جانبنا، وأما الأجوبة المفصلة فمذكورة في "التفسير الكبير".
The thirty-seventh issue. And also, this verse denies intercession absolutely, and the Mu'tazila affirm this intercession in the matter of increasing benefits. For we reply to the first objection: The correct position is that consideration is given to the generality of the wording, not to the specificity of the cause. And to the second objection in two ways: First: that even if the verse were specified, its specification is in increasing good deeds, so it remains a proof regarding other than that. Second: that the purpose of this verse is intimidation, and intimidation only occurs by not removing punishment, not by not increasing good deeds. This indicates that this verse is specific that intercessions have no effect on the Day of Resurrection in removing punishments. The second proof: His statement, the Most High: {For the wrongdoers there is no friend and no intercessor to be obeyed} [Ghafir: 18]. The wrongdoer is one who commits wrongdoing, so it includes the disbeliever and the transgressor. It cannot be said: This denies the intercessor being obeyed, but does not deny him being accepted in speech. For we say: The answer to it is in two ways: First: every rational person knows that there is no one in existence whom Allah obeys, so there is no benefit in interpreting the verse as you mentioned. Second: the intercessor is beneath the one interceded for; because if he were above him, he would be called a commander and a ruler, and would not be called an intercessor. So the term intercessor indicates that he is beneath Allah, so it is not possible to interpret His statement {obeyed} [Ghafir: 18] as applying to someone above Him. So the meaning is that they have no intercessor who is granted. The third proof: His statement, the Most High: {And before the coming of a Day in which there is no sale nor friendship nor intercession} [Al-Baqarah: 254]. The apparent meaning of this verse denies all intercessions. The fourth proof: His statement, the Most High: {And the wrongdoers have no helpers} [Al-Baqarah: 270]. The intercessor is undoubtedly one of the helpers. The fifth proof: His statement, the Most High, describing the wicked: {Indeed the wicked are in a blaze. They will burn therein on the Day of Recompense, and they will not be absent from it} [Al-Infitar: 14-16]. If intercession were accepted on behalf of sinners, either in removing punishment or in bringing them out of the Fire after entering it, then His statement {and they will not be absent from it} [Al-Infitar: 16] would be contrary. The sixth proof: His statement, the Most High: {And they cannot intercede except for him whom He approves} [Al-Anbiya': 28]. The transgressor is not approved, so intercession for him must be denied. The seventh proof: His statement, the Most High: {Those who bear the Throne and those around it glorify the praise of their Lord and believe in Him} [Ghafir: 7] up to His statement: {and followed Your way} [Ghafir: 7]. If intercession were obtained for the transgressor before repentance, then the restriction by the condition of repentance in His statement: {So forgive those who repent and follow Your way} [Ghafir: 7] would be in vain. The eighth proof: The community is agreed that they say: O Allah, make us among the people of the intercession of Muhammad, peace be upon him. If eligibility for intercession were only for the people of major sins, then the meaning of this supplication would be: O Allah, make us among the people of major sins and among the wicked. And it is known that this is false. And the answer to all these specious arguments is one word: that your proofs for denying intercession must be general in persons and times; otherwise they would not include the disputed matter. And our proofs for affirming intercession must be specific in persons and times, because we do not affirm intercession on behalf of all persons, nor do we affirm it at all times. So it is established that our proofs are specific and your proofs are general, and the specific takes precedence over the general, so the weight is on our side. As for the detailed answers, they are mentioned in 'Al-Tafsir al-Kabir'.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage is a series of objections and a general answer concerning intercession (shafa'a). Raazi responds to seven additional proofs (hujaj) from the opponents (likely the Mu'tazila) who deny intercession for sinners, and then gives a methodological rebuttal. He begins with a continuation of an earlier discussion: the previous proof is handled by stating that the general wording ('umum al-lafz) is the criterion, not the specific cause. Then for the second earlier proof, he gives two responses: first, even if the verse is specified, its specification only concerns increasing good deeds, so it remains evidence for other matters; second, the purpose is intimidation (takhwif), which requires not removing punishment, not the lack of increase. Then he lists seven proofs from the Qur'an that the opponents use to deny intercession: the second proof is from Surah Ghafir 18; he explains that wrongdoers include disbelievers and transgressors, and responds to the objection that the verse only denies the intercessor being 'obeyed' but not 'accepted in speech'. He gives two answers: every rational person knows none are obeyed by Allah, so that interpretation yields no benefit; and the intercessor is beneath the one interceded for, so 'obeyed' cannot mean the intercessor is above Allah, but rather that no intercessor is granted their request. The third proof is from Al-Baqarah 254 which denies all intercessions. The fourth proof from Al-Baqarah 270 equates intercessors with helpers, which wrongdoers lack. The fifth proof from Al-Infitar 14-16 asserts that the wicked will never leave the Fire, contradicting intercession. The sixth proof from Al-Anbiya' 28 restricts intercession to those Allah approves, and the transgressor is not approved. The seventh proof from Ghafir 7 shows that intercession is tied to repentance. The eighth proof is a consensus argument: the people ask to be among the people of intercession, but if intercession were only for major sinners, that would be absurd. Finally, Raazi gives a single comprehensive answer: the opponents' proofs for denying intercession must be universal in persons and times, but the matter under dispute is specific; the proofs for affirming intercession are specific, and specific (khas) takes precedence over general ('amm). This methodological point shifts the burden of proof. The detailed responses are referred to his larger commentary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the verse only denies an intercessor who is obeyed in the sense of being a superior, allowing for an intercessor whose request is accepted without being obeyed.
Correction: Razi shows that 'obeyed' in this context means the intercessor's request is granted, as the intercessor is beneath Allah, so the verse denies any effective intercessor for wrongdoers.

Checkpoint
What is the second answer Razi gives to the objection about the word 'obeyed'?
A) The intercessor is above Allah, so 'obeyed' is impossible.
B) The intercessor is beneath Allah, so 'obeyed' means his request is granted.
C) The verse is abrogated by other verses.
D) The word 'obeyed' refers to angels, not humans.

Key Takeaway
Razi uses Surah Ghafir 18 to affirm that wrongdoers have no effective intercessor, and cleverly refutes the objection by analyzing the meaning of 'obeyed' in context.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to stand before Allah tomorrow, would you be counted among the wrongdoers this verse describes? What hope do you have outside of Allah's mercy? This verse strips away false hopes—are you willing to let it strip yours?
?
Do you ever rely on the intercession of a saint, a scholar, or even your own good deeds as if they could compel Allah? This verse says the intercessor is beneath Allah and only effective if He grants. Does your heart place anyone in a position of authority over Allah? Repent of that today.
?
Razi's argument reveals that intercession is entirely subordinate to Allah's will. Have you been living as if your sins are automatically forgiven because of someone's status? Confront that assumption now. Will you change your relationship with sin and repentance?

Three Short Proofs: No Intercession on That Day
Razi presents three concise Qur'anic proofs against intercession: no intercession day, no helpers, and eternal stay in Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses three concise Qur'anic verses to argue that intercession is generally negated for sinners on the Day of Judgment.

Core Idea
Three verses collectively deny any form of intercession for wrongdoers.

Razi continues listing proofs from the Qur'an that opponents use to deny intercession. The third proof cites a verse that explicitly mentions 'no intercession' on a specific day. The fourth equates intercessors with helpers, which wrongdoers lack. The fifth argues that the wicked will forever remain in Hell, contradicting intercession. This lesson covers these three short but powerful proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read all three proofs
Read the Arabic and translation for the third, fourth, and fifth proofs together. Notice how each verse provides a different angle.
2
Analyze the third proof (Surah Al-Baqarah 254)
This verse states that on a certain day there will be no sale, friendship, or intercession. Razi says its apparent meaning negates all intercessions.
3
Analyze the fourth proof (Surah Al-Baqarah 270)
The verse says wrongdoers have no helpers. Razi argues that an intercessor is a helper, so this implies no intercessor for them.
4
Analyze the fifth proof (Surah Al-Infitar 14-16)
The verses state the wicked will burn in Hell and not be absent from it. If intercession could remove them or reduce punishment, this promise would be broken.
5
Reflect on the cumulative force
Consider how these three independent proofs strengthen the case against intercession for sinners.
